Sign up here.</a></h4><hr><h3>This week: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/salesforce-nightmare-scenarios-analysts-acquisitions-cloud-2021-8\">The Salesforce Nightmares </a></h3><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/salesforce-nightmare-scenarios-analysts-acquisitions-cloud-2021-8\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/611440b33dd01000199d3deb?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Salesforce founder Marc Benioff, wearing a sports coat jacket and in front of a blue background on a stage, extends his hands forward during a talk.\" height=\"3712\" width=\"5568\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Marc Benioff\n<p class=\"copyright\">NICHOLAS KAMM/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>Salesforce made the tech world do a double-take this week when it announced plans to <a href=\"https://www.axios.com/salesforce-streaming-service-professionals-30a58e49-77fc-469d-9ff7-99f866678a98.html\">launch Salesforce+, a video streaming service</a> with original content. The videos on Salesforce+ will likely be aimed at an office-worker audience, and designed to promote the company&#39;s tools rather than to win Emmys.</p><p>But since we&#39;re on the subject of plots, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/salesforce-nightmare-scenarios-analysts-acquisitions-cloud-2021-8\">let&#39;s consider some &#34;nightmare&#34; scenarios relating to Salesforce&#39;s business</a>. As Salesforce pushes forward on a mission to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/salesforce-execs-marc-benioff-q4-earnings-revenue-goal-2021-2\">ring up $50 billion in revenue by 2025</a>, and as it expands into new markets with its <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/salesforce-slack-deal-closed-bret-taylor-stewart-butterfield-learnings-2021-7\">acquisition of Slack</a>, the company will need to execute flawlessly on its gameplan - and be prepared for unexpected challenges. Here&#39;s how things could go wrong.</p><h3>Read the full story here:</h3><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/salesforce-nightmare-scenarios-analysts-acquisitions-cloud-2021-8\">Experts say these are the 3 nightmare scenarios for Salesforce</a></h3><hr><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gopuff-cuts-driver-pay-philadelphia-warehouses-drivers-mull-protest-union-2021-8\">GoPuff scores an own goal</a></h3><p>Don&#39;t be surprised if GoPuff, the convenience store delivery startup, becomes the next hot spot in the gig economy worker fight.</p><p>On July 30, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gopuffs-valuation-reaches-15-billion-with-1-billion-funding-round-2021-7\">GoPuff raised a hefty $1 billion of fresh funding</a>. One week later it cut hourly pay for workers at its Philadelphia home base, in at least one case, by 30%. As you might expect that didn&#39;t go over well. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gopuff-cuts-driver-pay-philadelphia-warehouses-drivers-mull-protest-union-2021-8\">Employees have started meeting with worker advocacy groups and there&#39;s talk of a work stoppage. </a></p><hr><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-startup-superhuman-raised-75-million-from-tiger-global-ivp-2021-8\">Venture Capitalists vs Hedge Funds</a></h3><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-startup-superhuman-raised-75-million-from-tiger-global-ivp-2021-8\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6112e7a0ad63f3001950107b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Rahul Vohra CEO of Superhuman\" height=\"2382\" width=\"3176\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rahul Vohra is the CEO and cofounder of the email provider Superhuman.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Rahul Vohra</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>Venture capital firms and hedge funds have very different approaches to startup investing. There&#39;s no better illustration than Superhuman&#39;s recent $75 million funding round, in which the email startup raised cash from IVP, an elite Silicon Valley VC firm, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tiger-global-hedge-fund-startup-investments-2021-5\">Tiger Global, the New York hedge fund that&#39;s plowing money into tech.</a></p><p>How different were the two investors? <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-startup-superhuman-raised-75-million-from-tiger-global-ivp-2021-8\">One of the investors committed to the deal in two months, the other did it in two days.</a></p><hr><h3>Bezos, Branson, and Musk - the space follies</h3><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-hires-spaceport-mixologist-bartender-cocktails-texas-rocket-2021-8\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/55314a9d69bedd74348b456e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"star wars celebration cantina\" height=\"2329\" width=\"3500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Richard Shotwell/Invision/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><p>Disney is getting closer to opening the doors to its <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/star-wars-hotel-disney-world-photos-2019-8\">very-cool looking Star Wars-themed hotel in Florida.</a> But the company wants to avoid any misunderstandings - while the hotel is called the Galactic Starcruiser, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/disney-star-wars-galactic-starcruiser-hotel-doesnt-go-to-space-2021-8\">Disney stresses that it&#39;s not an actual spaceship and guests will not be leaving the planet Earth. </a></p><p>Meanwhile, Elon Musk&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-starbase-city-spacex-texas-launch-site-2021-3?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">SpaceX launch site in Texas</a>, which really does send rockets into the skies, has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spacex-hires-spaceport-mixologist-bartender-cocktails-texas-rocket-2021-8\">a unique job opening: spaceport mixologist.</a></p><ul><li>According to a job posting, SpaceX is looking for an experienced bartender who can pair drinks with a themed menu. The notion of a spaceport bar <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/star-wars-cantina-scene-2015-9\">conjures visions of the famous Star Wars Cantina</a>, where a seedy cast of characters imbibed glowing elixirs, listened to groovy music, and got into arm-severing fights - If Musk&#39;s saloon is anywhere near as cool, the mixologist job should be an exciting gig. </li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/blue-origin-salty-graphics-trash-spacex-and-virgin-galactic-2021-8\">And we might not be too far off from a bar brawl among Musk, Jeff Bezos, and Richard Branson </a>the three billionaire space moguls.</li><li>With big rockets and big egos on the line, the trio are locked in an escalating war of words with each other that&#39;s left them blinded to what may be a more important issue: that the very notion of space tourism is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/emissions-from-space-tourism-could-quickly-add-up-2021-7\">an unnecessary producer of climate-warming emissions</a> that will only make it harder to avert the<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/climate-change-impacts-to-last-millennia-ipcc-report-2021-8\"> environmental catastrophe outlined in this week&#39;s UN report.</a></li></ul><p>And finally, something strange is afoot on the planet Mars. The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nasa-perseverance-rover-self-autonomous-drive-mars-autonav-system-2021-7\">NASA Perseverance rover</a> drilled into the red planet&#39;s surface for the first time this month, carrying out a mission to collect rock samples for future analysis. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nasa-perseverance-rover-first-mars-sample-mysteriously-missing-2021-8\">But for reasons unclear, the sample of Martian soil has vanished</a>. </p><p>There&#39;s probably <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mystery-solved-nasa-to-try-perseverance-rover-sample-collection-again-2021-8\">a perfectly reasonable explanation</a>, even if it sounds like the premise for a sci-fi thriller.</p><hr><h3>Recommended readings: </h3><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cisco-employees-brace-for-layoffs-expected-in-coming-months-2021-8\">Cisco employees are bracing for layoffs, which have become a dreaded summer tradition at the company</a></p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/53-startups-became-unicorns-july-busy-vc-summer-2021-8\">53 startups hit $1 billion valuations in July as &#39;hot unicorn summer&#39; rages. here'","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/nasa-astronauts-saddened-to-see-climate-crisis-wildfires-from-space-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img class=\"copyright\">NASA</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/wildfire-fires-ancient-olympia-the-olympic-games-birthplace-2021-8\">wildfires</a> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/wildfire-smoke-could-turn-full-buck-moon-blood-red-2021-7\">burning</a> across the globe.</li>\n<li>Astronauts on the International Space Station can see the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/oregon-bootleg-fire-creating-fire-clouds-pyrocumulonimbus-storms-2021-7\">extreme weather</a> caused by <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/climate-change-impacts-to-last-millennia-ipcc-report-2021-8\">climate change</a>.</li>\n<li>A <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/still-time-to-address-climate-change-ipcc-scientists-report-2021-8\">new UN report</a> on climate change is &#34;a warning for the entire global community,&#34; McArthur said.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/astronauts-held-first-space-olympics-on-space-station-2021-8\">Astronauts</a> have a better view of Earth than anybody, but lately it&#39;s a discouraging one.</p><p>&#34;We&#39;ve been very saddened to see fires over huge sections of the Earth, not just the United States,&#34; NASA astronaut Megan McArthur told Insider on a recent call from the space station.</p><p>Wildfires are raging across the US, Canada, Greece, Turkey, Italy, Algeria, and Siberia. McArthur&#39;s crewmate, French astronaut Thomas Pesquet, has posted photos of those blazes from above on Twitter.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Thomas Pesquet  (@Thom_astro) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1422888899488145410?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 4, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>Wildfires are one of the most visible hallmarks of the climate crisis. This summer, they&#39;ve come alongside historic heat waves and the western US&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/western-us-extreme-heat-drought-leads-to-wildfires-power-failures-2021-6\">worst drought</a> in the 20-year history of the US Drought Monitor.</p><p>A new report from the UN&#39;s Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC) warns that &#34;fire weather&#34; will probably increase by 2050 in North America, Central America, parts of South America, the Mediterranean, southern Africa, north Asia, Australia, and New Zealand. That means more days where conditions are warm, dry, and windy enough to trigger and sustain wildfires.</p><p>The amount of fuel available to burn in those places - dry vegetation - is also likely to increase as rising temperatures cause the air to absorb more moisture and bring about more droughts.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Thomas Pesquet  (@Thom_astro) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1425063723887173658?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 10, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>The IPCC report, released Monday, is the first part of the group&#39;s sixth assessment, which recruits hundreds of experts to analyze years of scientific research on climate change. Those experts determined that global temperatures will almost certainly rise <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/climate-ipcc-report-temperature-rise-20-years-15-degrees-2021-8\">at least 1.5 degrees Celsius</a> above the preindustrial average by 2040.</p><p>That may sound small, but it brings about huge changes across the planet, including further melting of glaciers and polar ice caps. This contributes to sea-level rise, and water expands as it heats up, so it is virtually certain that oceans will continue rising through the end of this century. In the best case scenario, the IPCC authors said, oceans will rise by nearly a foot over the next 80 years.</p><p>But <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/still-time-to-address-climate-change-ipcc-scientists-report-2021-8\">there is still time to prevent 2 degrees Celsius of warming</a> and the even more catastrophic changes that would bring, the report said.</p><p>&#34;Over many years, scientists around the world have been sounding this alarm bell,&#34; McArthur said. &#34;This is a warning for the entire global community. It&#39;s going to take the entire global community to face this and to work through these challenges.&#34;</p><h2>Astronauts can see the climate crisis unfolding across the planet</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6115ac0cc040ad0018ce1891?format=jpeg\" alt=\"hurricane laura ISS\" height=\"2730\" width=\"3641\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A photo of Hurricane Laura taken from the International Space Station on August 25, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Chris Cassidy/NASA</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Astronauts can see other signs of the changing climate, too: &#34;Big tropical storms - those are always coming, and potentially the flooding that comes after them,&#34; McArthur said. &#34;We can see all of those effects from up here.&#34;</p><p>Future astronauts will probably observe even more of that. The IPCC report found that combinations of extreme events like heavy rainfall and hurricane-caused storm surge, paired with rising seas, will continue to make flooding more likely in coming decades.</p><p>Other <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/satellite-images-show-california-mega-drought-drying-up-lakes-forest-2021-7\">satellites can also see signs of drought</a>, like <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/take-a-look-at-lakes-that-dried-up-california-drought-2021-6\">dried-up reservoirs</a> across California.</p><p>&#34;The other thing that we can see, of course, is the very thin lens of atmosphere,&#34; McArthur said. &#34;That is what protects our Earth and everything on it. And we see how fragile that is, and we know how important it is.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6115a2ddc040ad0018ce1793?format=jpeg\" alt=\"thin atmosphere glowing orange against space stars above nighttime earth city lights\" height=\"1188\" width=\"1584\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The atmosphere glows above the southeastern African coast, as seen from the International Space Station.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.flickr.com/photos/nasa2explore/51355243603/\" target=\"_blank\">NASA</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The burning of fossil fuels like coal and oil is drastically changing that thin atmosphere by filling it with heat-trapping gas.</p><p>In 2019, the concentration of carbon in the atmosphere was higher than at any time in at least 2 million years, according to the IPCC report. Concentrations of methane and nitrous oxide - more potent greenhouse gases than carbon dioxide - were higher than at any time in at least 800,000 years.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6115b886c040ad0018ce1976?format=jpeg\" alt=\"smoke plumes dixie fire as seen from space\" height=\"2784\" width=\"3712\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>On August 4, 2021, an astronaut on the International Space Station shot a photo of the Dixie fireâ€™s thick smoke plume.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://earthobservatory.nasa.gov/images/148669/californias-dixie-fire-keeps-on-growing\" target=\"_blank\">NASA/JSC</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>As those gases fill the atmosphere, they prevent more and more heat from the sun from bouncing back into space. That&#39;s what&#39;s causing global temperatures to rise and bringing about the extreme weather that astronauts are watching in horror.</p><p>&#34;That is the place that we need to be able to live. So it&#39;s important that we take ownership of whatever we can do to help maintain it,&#34; NASA astronaut Mark Vande Hei told Insider.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/nasa-astronauts-saddened-to-see-climate-crisis-wildfires-from-space-2021-8'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a McFall-Johnsen)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/6115b3d83dd01000199d7d40?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn97@2020_4/2021/08/15/03-53-40-113_7cde925b66853b4d.webp","https://i.insider.com/6115ac0cc040ad0018ce1891?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn15@2020_3/2021/08/15/03-53-30-338_56ec8b5820fdbcbc.webp","https://i.insider.com/6115a2ddc040ad0018ce1793?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn67@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-29-162_bb00e87166772adb.webp","https://i.insider.com/6115b886c040ad0018ce1976?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn93@2020_6/2021/08/15/03-53-33-016_19f634795a76a154.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn49@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-32-122_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=qWHtgTeRAWc:LrPrnzbZ3Oo:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn10@2020_2/2021/08/15/03-53-32-236_8119c795e7bd8ebf.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=qWHtgTeRAWc:LrPrnzbZ3Oo:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn72@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-31-249_420521a76beca9a5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn27@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-30-405_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=qWHtgTeRAWc:LrPrnzbZ3Oo:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn51@2020_3/2021/08/15/03-53-30-103_ada093fc0ae47c7a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/qWHtgTeRAWc":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn4@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-28-859_e9ce921711a7abf2.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1628999590233},{"createdTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"There will be one economy for the vaccinated and another for everyone else","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/will-delta-send-us-lockdown-economy-vaccinated-unvaccinated-repeat-2020-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61167d85c040ad0018ce278a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"dining out restaurant\" height=\"1476\" width=\"1968\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Delta surge is sparking fears that America is losing the taste of normalcy it&#39;s had over the summer.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Gerry Broome/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The Delta surge has sparked fears of repeating 2020, but it&#39;s unlikely we&#39;ll experience last year&#39;s economy.</li>\n<li>Not enough people are vaxxed to stop Delta, but enough are to help keep the economy running.</li>\n<li>The economy has also learned how to adapt to the pandemic, but you&#39;ll need a shot to participate.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The Delta variant has thrown a giant curveball at <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/hot-vaxx-summer-pandemic-horniness-is-coming-blissful-release-2021-3\">America&#39;s hot vax summer</a>. </p><p>Hospitals in less-vaccinated regions are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/florida-hospitals-doctors-breaking-point-worst-covid-surge-delta-variant-2021-8\">becoming overcrowded</a>. Mask recommendations <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cdc-fully-vaccinated-new-guidelines-wear-masks-indoors-delta-2021-7\">are back</a>. Many companies have pushed back their <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/newsletters/2021-08-09/tech-s-return-to-office-plans-get-pushed-back-en-masse?sref=BLKWHazc\">return-to-office</a> start dates. And it&#39;s all happening ahead of the upcoming <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/schools-starting-back-up-moms-might-not-return-work-months-2021-8\">school year</a>.</p><p>It&#39;s all revived Covid anxiety in full force for many Americans, who are fearing another lockdown and quarantine, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/university-michigan-sentiment-delta-fear-lockdown-cases-rising-july-report-2021-8\">rapidly losing confidence</a> in the economy&#39;s ability to handle it. But while Delta is a very real threat right now, it&#39;s unlikely we&#39;ll experience the same economy that we did a year ago.</p><p>Scary media headlines <a href=\"https://www.wgbh.org/news/commentary/2021/08/04/yes-delta-is-serious-business-but-the-media-need-to-cover-it-with-context-and-nuance\">lacking crucial context</a> are behind much of the understandable angst, but the emerging science shows the vaccines <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fully-vaccinated-people-not-immune-to-covid-milder-2021-7https://www.businessinsider.com/fully-vaccinated-people-not-immune-to-covid-milder-2021-7\">largely protect against hospitalization</a>. Not enough Americans are vaccinated to prevent Delta&#39;s spread, but enough people <em>are</em> vaccinated to keep the economy open and maintain a sense of normalcy.</p><p>That&#39;s because the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/us-economy-mutating-4-ways-jpmorgan-economic-outlook-delta-variant-2021-8\">economy has also mutated</a> alongside the virus, learning how to adapt to a pandemic world. Once Americans understood how the virus spreads, many professions improvised methods to limit physical contact and keep the economy running while preventing another lockdown.</p><p>Given the recent surge in the Delta variant, cities are imposing their own rules, and if you&#39;re not vaccinated, you&#39;ll have limited participation. For example, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nyc-expcted-require-proof-of-vaccination-indoor-dining-gyms-performances-2021-8\">New York City</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/san-francisco-mandates-proof-of-full-vaccination-for-some-indoor-activities-2021-8\">San Francisco</a> will require proof of a vaccine for indoor activities like dining and using the gym. More and more employers are requiring it of their workers as well and, as <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/you-have-to-be-vaccinated-for-more-more-job-openings-2021-8\">Insider&#39;s Juliana Kaplan reported</a>, it&#39;s even increasingly required in job postings.</p><p>The health risks for the vaccinated aren&#39;t near what they were in 2020, meaning they can still live their lives with a degree of normalcy. What&#39;s emerged is a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/new-york-city-vaccine-mandate-bill-de-blasio-delta-variant-2021-8\">two-track economy</a> marked by a patchwork of highly vaccinated areas and poorly vaccinated regions<em>. </em>This lack of cohesiveness isn&#39;t ideal, but improved from the unvaccinated economy that shut down last year.</p><p>We may still be living in a pandemic, but it&#39;s looking like the economy won&#39;t repeat 2020. </p><h2><strong>Vaccines allow us to live our lives during the pandemic</strong></h2><p>In 2020, Covid was a pandemic for everyone. Now, it&#39;s become &#34;a pandemic of the unvaccinated,&#34; CDC Director Dr. Rochelle Walensky <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cdc-director-says-covid-19-hospitalizations-are-mostly-unvaccinated-2021-7\">said during a press briefing last month</a>.</p><p>The unvaccinated are most at risk of disease from Covid and are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fauci-unvaccinated-could-lead-to-variant-worse-than-delta-2021-8\">largely driving the Delta surge</a>. While the highly contagious variant has increased the odds of &#34;breakthrough&#34; infections among the vaccinated, these cases affect only <a href=\"https://www.kff.org/policy-watch/covid-19-vaccine-breakthrough-cases-data-from-the-states/\">0.01% to 0.29%</a> of fully vaccinated people in all states reporting data to the CDC through July. </p><p>A full vaccination with an mRNA vaccine is about <a href=\"https://www.nejm.org/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa2108891?query=recirc_mostViewed_railB_article\">88% effective</a> at preventing symptomatic disease caused by Delta, according to an August study published by the New England Journal of Medicine. That means the vaccinated also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fully-vaccinated-people-not-immune-to-covid-milder-2021-7https://www.businessinsider.com/fully-vaccinated-people-not-immune-to-covid-milder-2021-7\">remain well protected</a> from serious disease leading to hospitalization and death, likely to have mild or no symptoms. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/608811063f0560001881c390?format=jpeg\" alt=\"covid vaccine\" height=\"1356\" width=\"1807\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Even with the Delta surge, vaccines make a big difference in how our economy can operate.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/medical-assistant-floater-charlene-batas-administers-a-one-news-photo/1309200757?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Mario Tama/Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>But whereas the vaccinated were unlikely to transmit the Alpha variant to others, Delta is a different story: It&#39;s transmissible among the vaccinated, making it more contagious, per <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cdc-fully-vaccinated-new-guidelines-wear-masks-indoors-delta-2021-7\">the CDC</a>. However, <a href=\"https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2021.07.28.21261295v1?%253fcollection=\">a recent study</a> found that even though Delta viral loads are about the same for both the unvaccinated and vaccinated, they fall more quickly for the latter. And because the chances of a breakthrough infection are relatively rare, vaccinated people are overall less likely to transmit the virus to others.</p><p>However, the problem is that <a href=\"https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#vaccinations_vacc-total-admin-rate-total\">only half of Americans</a> are fully vaccinated (vaccines haven&#39;t yet been approved for kids), and they thus need to bear the burden of protecting the unvaccinated half. </p><p>While a portion of the vaccinated very worried about Delta may personally quarantine again, it&#39;s likely most of America will keep keeping on: the vaccinated who are trying to maintain the summer&#39;s taste of normalcy, albeit with more caution, and those among the unvaccinated who are opposed to restrictions and always acted like everything was normal in the first place will continue to stimulate the economy.</p><h2>Even with the Delta surge, we won&#39;t go into full lockdown again</h2><p>The hybrid economy of the vaxxed and unvaxxed also means it&#39;s unlikely America will go under lockdown again. <a href=\"https://www.newsweek.com/biden-says-its-unlikely-delta-variant-will-cause-us-lockdown-wont-rule-it-out-1602181\">President Joe Biden said back in June</a> that he didn&#39;t foresee a lockdown under Delta since so many Americans are vaccinated.</p><p>&#34;The existing vaccines are very effective so no, it&#39;s not a lockdown, but some areas will be very hurt,&#34; he said.</p><p>Dr. Anthony Fauci <a href=\"https://www.newsweek.com/fauci-doesnt-forsee-another-round-lockdowns-says-things-are-going-get-worse-1615042\">echoed a similar sentiment earlier this month</a>, saying that enough people are vaccinated that a lockdown isn&#39;t necessary, although the US would still see a rise in cases because just as many people aren&#39;t vaccinated. &#34;I think we have enough of the percentage of people in the country - not enough to crush the outbreak - but I believe enough to not allow us to get into the situation we were in last winter,&#34; he said.</p><p>It helps, too, that the economy is also better prepared for the latest wave of infections than it was a year ago. It&#39;s become so adaptable that experts widely expect the economic fallout from the Delta variant to be a fraction of early 2020&#39;s historic recession, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-economy-mutating-4-ways-jpmorgan-economic-outlook-delta-variant-2021-8\">Insider&#39;s Ben Winck reported</a>.</p><p>The way the economy is &#34;mutating&#34; has left it less vulnerable and more productive, David Kelly, JPMorgan Funds&#39; chief global strategist, said in a note on Monday. He cited four key shifts that have boosted productivity and would protect the US from another pandemic related recession: the QR menu at restaurants, the continued rise of e-commerce, the video-conferencing boom, and the shift from to cash to cards.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60efa246a8d8c00019b03482?format=jpeg\" alt=\"restaurant dining out\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The economy and its people have  adapted to pandemic life.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Robert Nickelsberg/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The economic forecast from the beginning of the third quarter also looks promising. <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/graphics/global-economic-recovery-q3-nowcast/?sref=BLKWHazc\">Bloomberg Economics</a> predicts GDP will expand by 1.8% in the third quarter from the past three months. It also anticipates inflation peaking before falling to a more moderate pace during the same time frame. </p><p>Then there&#39;s the fact that the US <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/july-jobs-report-cuts-months-off-economic-recovery-payrolls-outlook-2021-8\">added nearly 1 million jobs</a> in July. And US jobless claims slid to 375,000 last week, suggesting little Delta impact. Spending is also going strong - Target and Walmart are <a href=\"https://www.placer.ai/blog/walmart-and-targets-big-summer/\">headed toward a strong back-to-school season</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.placer.ai/blog/malls-rise-once-again/\">malls have made a comeback</a>.</p><p>Now, if the pandemic has taught us anything, it&#39;s that life is uncertain. Things could change for better or for worse overnight. There are still signs of a threatened economy: BofA predicts a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-variant-covid-economy-consumer-behavior-lockdown-bank-of-america-2021-7\">pullback in spending</a>, and already noted a <a href=\"https://twitter.com/carlquintanilla/status/1425809525261623304\">decline in spending on airfare</a> over the past week. Some events, like <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-08-04/new-york-auto-show-cancelled-on-delta-variant-spread-concerns?sref=BLKWHazc\">the New York International Auto Show</a>, have been cancelled. And other countries that have already been experiencing a Delta surge, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/israel-brings-back-covid-19-restrictions-despite-vaccine-success-2021-8\">like Israel</a>, have implemented additional rounds of restrictions.</p><p>But Richard Curtin, chief economist for the University of Michigan&#39;s Surveys of Consumers, said Friday that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/university-michigan-sentiment-delta-fear-lockdown-cases-rising-july-report-2021-8\">Delta may not harm the economy</a> as much as people think. Should economic recovery continue and vaccination rates improve, he said, it&#39;s possible Americans could &#34;shift toward outright optimism.&#34;</p><p>We&#39;ve <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-covid-changes-remote-work-housing-entertainment-fashion-flexible-economy-2021-7\">learned how to be flexible</a>, and so has the US economy. It&#39;s enough to keep us from repeating 2020 all over again as we wait for more people to get vaccinated.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a alt=\"peloton bike\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Peloton bike\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/peloton-stationary-bike-sits-on-display-at-one-of-the-news-photo/1186506761?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Scott Heins/Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Peloton users filed a lawsuit against the exercise company saying it improperly charged sales tax.</li>\n<li>Customers were taxed in New York, Massachusetts, and Virginia where digital goods are tax-exempt, the lawsuit said.</li>\n<li>This is the latest lawsuit for Peloton after its Tread+ treadmill was recalled earlier this year.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/peloton-slammed-with-class-action-lawsuit-after-tread-death-injuries-2021-4\">Peloton</a> users have filed a class action lawsuit against the at-home exercise bike and workout company, claiming it improperly charged a sales tax to its customers.</p><p>Peloton, which costs $39 a month for an &#34;All-Access&#34; membership and $12.99 a month for a &#34;Digitial&#34; membership, unlawfully charged users an additional sales tax between 6.3% and 8.9% in New York, Virginia, and Massachusetts, according to court documents obtained by <a href=\"https://www.bloomberglaw.com/public/desktop/document/SkillernetalvPelotonInteractiveIncDocketNo121cv06808SDNYAug122021?1628944553\">Bloomberg Law</a>. </p><p>Because all Peloton memberships are digital, plaintiffs Brannon Skillern and Ryan Corken believe that Peloton memberships should not have sales tax and should be tax-exempt as &#34;digital goods,&#34; according to the lawsuit.</p><p>While Peloton no longer charges its customers a sales tax in the three states, Skillern and Corken are seeking unspecified compensatory, statutory, and punitive damages, and reasonable attorney&#39;s fees and costs.</p><p>Peloton declined to respond to Insider&#39;s request for comment, stating that the company does not comment on active litigation.</p><p>After <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/child-died-accident-peloton-tread-treadmill-2021-3?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\">a child was fatally injured</a> and on a Peloton Tread+ treadmill in March, the company faced a lawsuit after featuring a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/peloton-slammed-with-class-action-lawsuit-after-tread-death-injuries-2021-4\">child in its advertisements</a> for the treadmill. More than 39 people were injured on the Tread+ treadmill before it was recalled in May, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/peloton-tread-customers-report-injury-malfunction-as-early-as-2019-2021-4\">according to Insider</a>. Despite this, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pelotons-treadmill-recall-unlikely-to-hurt-the-company-long-term-2021-5?r=fitness-lp\">the demand for Peloton remains strong</a>.</p><p>Since the start of the coronavirus pandemic, the at-home fitness market grew substantially as gyms closed and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/12-ways-pandemic-has-changed-fitness-as-we-know-it-2020-8\">people exercised at home.</a> Peloton made $1.8 billion in revenue in 2020 and has over <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/peloton-cfo-shares-how-digital-subscriptions-drive-sales-2020-12?r=fitness-lp\">4.4 million subscribers</a> across its exercise platforms, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/complete-guide-to-the-rise-of-the-digital-fitness-industry-2021-8\">Insider reported.</a> In 2021, Peloton <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/peloton-power-players-meet-18-execs-behind-meteoric-rise-2020-12?r=fitness-lp#jon-adee-chief-supply-chain-officer-1\">hopes to make $4 billion in revenue</a>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/peloton-sued-charging-customers-with-a-sales-tax-2021-8'>Business kids","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/schools-reopening-covid-cases-rising-quarantine-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60e9a6c261b8600019f167a8?format=jpeg\" class=\"copyright\">Carolyn Cole/Los Angeles Times/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Days into the school year, COVID-19 outbreaks have already forced thousands of students to quarantine.</li>\n<li>Experts predict that pediatric infections will continue to rise, leading to more school closures. </li>\n<li>Bans on mask mandates while young kids wait on vaccine authorization make it tough to protect students.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Mere days into the new school year, thousands of kids across the US are already being asked to quarantine following exposure to COVID-19. </p><p>In Mississippi, where daily cases have doubled in the last two weeks, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/over-4000-mississippi-students-quarantine-school-covid-2021-8\">more than 4,400 students</a> were quarantined from August 2 to 6, <a href=\"https://msdh.ms.gov/msdhsite/_static/resources/15292.pdf\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"70376d4a1ac6b9df5486cd6beae5a6dd\">according to state data</a>. One Mississippi school, Pearl River Central High School, has <a href=\"https://www.mississippifreepress.org/14689/pearl-river-high-school-quarantines-40-of-students-in-first-week-district-going-virtual/\">quarantined nearly 40% of its student body</a> since August 5. The entire school district opted to go virtual for at least two weeks to be safe, the <a href=\"https://www.mississippifreepress.org/14689/pearl-river-high-school-quarantines-40-of-students-in-first-week-district-going-virtual/\">Mississippi Free Press reported</a>.</p><p>And in Reno, Nevada, more than <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nevada-student-positive-covid-exposed-students-2021-8\">80 students were likely exposed to COVID-19</a> on Monday after a parent knowingly sent their infected child to school. </p><p>&#34;I think this fall is going to be really challenging for schools,&#34; Richard Besser, former acting director of the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention, <a href=\"https://www.today.com/video/more-schools-may-shut-down-this-year-than-last-due-to-covid-19-doctor-says-118263877842\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"a44f464e9d3dbd99b8856910b4c7017e\">told NBC&#39;s &#34;Today&#34; show</a> on Tuesday. &#34;I think children belong in the classroom. But what we&#39;re going to see is little outbreaks, clusters in different schools, schools shutting down, reopening.&#34;</p><p>Besser said he expected <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/schools-shut-down-more-this-year-former-cdc-official-2021-8\">schools to shut down more often this year</a> than they did last year.</p><p>Already, pediatric infections are on the rise: The US recorded nearly 94,000 child COVID-19 cases between July 30 and August 5 - more than double the number of pediatric cases recorded during the two weeks prior. Pediatric hospitalizations have risen 27%, on average, in the last week, as shown in the chart below.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6116d6333dd01000199dafa8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"children covid-19 hospitalizations\" height=\"872\" width=\"1086\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>New COVID-19 hospital admissions for children under 18.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Scientists agree that the Delta variant has made school outbreaks more likely. The variant is two to three times as contagious as the original version of the virus, <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/sections/goatsandsoda/2021/08/11/1026190062/covid-delta-variant-transmission-cdc-chickenpox\">according to one estimate</a>, and vaccinated people can still spread Delta to others.</p><p>&#34;The Delta variant has created a new and pressing risk to children and adolescents across this country, as it has also done for unvaccinated adults,&#34; Dr. Lee Savio Beers, president of the American Academy of Pediatrics, <a href=\"https://downloads.aap.org/DOFA/AAP%20Letter%20to%20FDA%20on%20Timeline%20for%20Authorization%20of%20COVID-19%20Vaccine%20for%20Children_08_05_21.pdf\">wrote in a recent letter</a> to the Food and Drug Administration. </p><p>The letter called upon the FDA to &#34;ensure that COVID-19 vaccines for children can be authorized as swiftly as possible.&#34;</p><h2>Bans on mask mandates make it difficult to control transmission in Texas and Florida</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606dc78130004b0019b2664b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"school covid\" height=\"2675\" width=\"4013\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Freshman Hugo Bautista eats lunch separated from classmates by plastic dividers at Wyandotte County High School in Kansas City, Kansas on March 31, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Charlie Riedel</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Studies of school transmission last fall indicated that <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/mmwr/volumes/70/wr/mm7021e1.htm\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"ef669c97333dc2d6fedb9030dfd322f8\">masks and social distancing</a> <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/mmwr/volumes/70/wr/mm7012e2.htm#T2_down\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"674f6ccae5ba1ba4e5f0ef80eb626539\">lowered the spread of COVID-19</a>. That science hasn&#39;t changed, but Delta leaves even less room for error.</p><p>&#34;Masking and distancing still works for Delta. It&#39;s just that you have to be more meticulous,&#34; Hilary Babcock, the medical director of infection prevention at Barnes-Jewish Hospital and St. Louis Children&#39;s Hospital in Missouri, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/risky-activities-vaccinated-people-breakthrough-case-delta-2021-7\">recently told Insider</a>.</p><p>But both Texas Gov. Greg Abbott and Florida Gov. Ron DeSantis recently banned mask mandates in schools. DeSantis even threatened on Monday to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/florida-governor-desantis-disavow-ways-to-save-lives-covid-2021-8\">withhold funding for schools that require masks</a>. </p><p>Florida and Texas are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/under-18-hospitalized-covid-19-florida-texas-2021-8\">seeing more daily pediatric hospitalizations</a> than any other US state: On average, Texas recorded 54 pediatric hospitalizations per day between August 1 and 9 (the most recent data available). Florida, meanwhile, recorded 40 pediatric hospitalizations per day over the same period. The national average was just five daily pediatric hospitalizations per state during that time.</p><p>Several Florida and Texas counties are pushing back on their state&#39;s anti-mask policies, though. In Texas, officials in Dallas and Bexar counties recently won court orders challenging Abbott&#39;s school mask ban. And some Florida counties, including Palm Beach, continue to require face coverings inside school buildings and on school transportation, contrary to DeSantis&#39; rule.</p><p>As of Wednesday afternoon, however, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/over-400-florida-students-quarantine-covid-2021-8\">nearly 500 students in Palm Beach were quarantined</a> after being exposed to COVID-19 just two days into the school year. Up to 6,400 Palm Beach students didn&#39;t wear masks during the first few days of class, despite the mandate, the <a href=\"https://cbs12.com/news/local/hundreds-of-palm-beach-county-students-quarantined-in-2-days-superintendent-says\">local CBS12 station reported</a>.</p><p>Some Texas schools have found it similarly difficult to enforce mask requirements.</p><p>&#34;You can&#39;t ask people to wear a mask. You can&#39;t require people to stay home. You can&#39;t require people to get tested. I felt safer last year coming back to school than I do this year,&#34; Becca Harkleroad, a school nurse in Central Texas, <a href=\"https://19thnews.org/2021/08/covid-delta-school-nurses-burned-out/?utm_source=The+19th&utm_campaign=21ae0fa0e0-19th-newsletters-daily-0812&utm_medium=email&utm_term=0_a35c3279be-21ae0fa0e0-382787845e0-382787845\">told the 19th</a> on Thursday.</p><p>One glimmer of hope is that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/when-can-young-kids-get-vaccinated-timeline-2021-7\">vaccines may soon be available to kids ages 5 to 11</a>: Pfizer expects to have data about its vaccine&#39;s efficacy among this age group by the end of September. That would put the US on track to start administering vaccines to young kids sometime in October, assuming the FDA authorizes them.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"Fast carbs don't necessarily make you fat, a new study suggests","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/study-fast-carbs-weight-gain-health-glycemic-index-nutrition-bmi-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/601adb4dee136f00183aa144?format=jpeg\" alt=\"white bread refined grains carbs\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1885\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Processed foods like white bread have long been vilified for leading to weight gain. A new study claims that theory is wrong.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Capelle.r/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><strong>High-GI carbs like white bread are not more likely to cause weight gain than their low-GI counterparts, a study found.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Researchers analyzed data on 2 million adults with high-glycemic and low-glycemic diets.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Other qualities like nutrient density and dietary fiber are more important, according to the study.</strong></li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>High-glycemic foods are no more likely than low-glycemic ones to lead to weight gain, according to a study published this week in &#34;Advances in Nutrition,&#34; a peer-reviewed journal from the American Society for Nutrition.</p><p>The glycemic index (GI) was introduced in 1981 by David Jenkins, a professor at the University of Toronto. Jenkins assigned a number from 0 to 100 to a food as a measurement of how quickly the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/harvard-nutrition-expert-suggests-a-high-fat-high-carb-breakfast-2019-8\">body breaks down carbohydrates.</a></p><p>Consumers have since been told that too much high-glycemic foods - like processed foods, candy, and sodas - <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/healthy-lifestyle-diet-save-money-personal-finances-insurance-planning-2021-8\">can make them fat,</a> leading them to swap the white bread for brown and Frosted Flakes for oatmeal. These foods have been dubbed &#34;fast carbs&#34; or &#34;simple carbs&#34; for how quickly they raise blood sugar levels, which can promote fat storage and increase the risk of diabetes and obesity.</p><p>After analyzing data on nearly 2 million adults from 43 cohort studies, scientists <a href=\"https://academic.oup.com/advances/advance-article/doi/10.1093/advances/nmab093/6342518?searchresult=1\">concluded</a> that there were no consistent differences in body-mass index, or BMI, between adults who consumed more fast carbs and those who had lower GI diets.</p><p>70% of the 27 cohort studies that compared the differences between low-GI and high-GI diets for weight loss either showed that they had similar BMIs, or that BMI was actually lower in the groups with the highest GI, according to the study.</p><p>&#34;Contrary to popular belief, those who consume a diet of high-GI foods are no more likely to be obese or gain weight than those who consume a diet of low-GI foods. Furthermore, they are no less likely to lose weight,&#34; Glenn Gaesser, one of the study&#39;s co-authors and professor of exercise science at Arizona State University, said.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/neanderthals-human-ancestors-low-carb-paleo-diet-study-2021-5\">Other qualities of carbs</a>, like nutrient density, dietary fiber, and amount of added sugar, are more important than its glycemic index, the researchers contended.</p><p>&#34;The key takeaway is that carbohydrates, regardless of type, can be part of a healthy diet and have a place on a healthy plate,&#34; co-author Julie Miller Jones, a professor at St. Catherine University, said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a in January 2020.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>If the ruling is upheld, some of Google&#39;s products could be banned from import.</strong></li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a trade judge said that Google infringed on five of Sonos&#39; patents.</p><p>The preliminary ruling from judge Charles Bullock of the US International Trade Commission could deal a significant blow to Google. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-assistant-now-available-with-bose-sonos-lenovo-2019-5\">Some of its products,</a> like its Pixel smartphones and Nest speakers, could be banned from import.</p><p>Sonos first sued Google in California federal court and with the commission in January 2020. The audio manufacturer alleged that Google infringed on its patents related to home speaker technology.</p><p>In addition to seeking financial damages in federal court, Sonos asked the commission, which is tasked with investigating unfair trade practices that harm US businesses, to ban imports of Google products that are made in China.</p><p>Google not only denied the claims -<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-countersues-sonos-over-alleged-patent-infringement-2020-6\"> the tech giant also lodged a countersuit</a>, arguing that Sonos was actually infringing on Google&#39;s patents. In September last year, Sonos filed another lawsuit against Google, adding five more patents to the list of alleged infringements.</p><p>The patent dispute between Sonos and Google is unfolding at a time when <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-wants-your-palm-prints-lawmakers-are-asking-why-2021-8\">Big Tech companies are under heightened scrutiny</a> by lawmakers for anti-competitive behavior.</p><p>&#34;This decision re-affirms the strength and breadth of our portfolio, marking a promising milestone in our long-term pursuit to defend our innovation against misappropriation by Big Tech monopolies,&#34; Eddie Lazarus, Sonos&#39; chief legal officer, said in a statement.</p><p>The case isn&#39;t over yet. The trade commission will review Judge Bullock&#39;s decision for a final ruling, which is scheduled to take place on December 13. </p><p>&#34;We disagree with this preliminary ruling and will continue to make our case in the upcoming review process,&#34; JosÃ© CastaÃ±eda, a Google spokesperson, said in a statement.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a positive for COVID-19.</li>\n<li>One passenger and 26 crew members were among the positive cases, the company told CNN. </li>\n<li>The cruise line has implemented additional protocols aboard the sailing from Galveston, Texas, to Belize, according to a <a href=\"https://belizetourismboard.org/carnival-vista-port-call-to-belize-city/\">Belize Tourism Board press release</a>. </p><p>The positive cases included 26 crew members and one passenger on the ship, which was carrying more than 4,000 people. All those infected were vaccinated, according to the release.</p><p>Most had very mild symptoms or no symptoms and were in isolation, it added.</p><p>Everyone on the ship was notified of the positive tests, according to the board. The guests who tested positive did not pose a threat to the other guests, crew, or frontline workers in Belize, it added. </p><p>Following the tests, Carnival upgraded protocols aboard the ship, including increased mask-wearing indoors, the use of N95 masks by the crew, and closing of crew social areas. </p><p>&#34;The health, safety and wellbeing of our guests, crew and the destinations we visit is our priority. All activities on the ship are taking place and our guests have been terrific at adapting to our new protocols,&#34; Carnival said in a statement on Friday as reported by <a href=\"https://edition.cnn.com/travel/article/carnival-cruise-ship-vista-covid-cases/index.html?utm_source=twCNN&utm_medium=social&utm_content=2021-08-13T22%3A16%3A04&utm_term=linktm_term=link\">CNN</a>.</p><p>It added that it was managing &#34;a small number of positive COVID cases,&#34; but did not say an exact number.</p><p><a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/lifestyle-business-health-travel-caribbean-4dd34f14b6a6365f48b3375c57ba4fb4\">AP reported</a> that the company said in a statement: &#34;We have managed the situation utilizing stringent health protocols which included placing those who tested positive in isolation and close contacts in quarantine.&#34;</p><p>The company said it had notified all passengers on the current trip and the prior one. It said Belize health officials had randomly tested 68 Vista passengers as they disembarked and all were negative, per the statement.</p><p>Carnival did not immediately respond to Insider&#39;s request for comment.</p><p>On Carnival ships, guests are required to be <a href=\"https://www.carnival.com/legal/covid-19-legal-notices/covid-19-guest-protocols\">fully vaccinated</a>, though there are exemptions for children and people with medical issues. </p><p>Carnival Vista isn&#39;t the first cruise to see positive COVID-19 cases. On July 30, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/6-passengers-royal-caribbean-cruise-tested-positive-coronavirus-2021-7?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">six guests - four of whom were vaccinated - tested positive onboard a Royal Caribbean cruise in the Bahamas</a>. </p><p>On an American Cruise Lines cruise in Alaska, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/alaska-cruise-covid-3-people-positive-2021-7\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"4dcf311c39d4fe8cbd2394216bd3099c\">two guests and one crew member test positive</a> on July 12. </p><p> </p><div 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"A Florida school board member says Gov. Ron DeSantis has banned school mask mandates and threatened to withhold funding.</li> \n <li>One school official, from the seventh-largest district in the US, told Insider DeSantis has caused chaos and panic among parents.</li> \n <li>\"We should have the ability to make decisions for the people who elected us,\" she said.</li> \n <li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider's business page</a>.</li> \n</ul>\n<p>A school board member at the seventh-largest school district in the nation said Florida Gov. Ron DeSantis's handling of COVID-19 has caused \"panic\" and \"chaos\" among parents and school staff.</p>\n<p>\"Our governor is the mad king of the COVID era,\" Jessica Vaughn told Insider. \"It feels like a nightmare I can't wake up from.\"</p>\n<p>Vaughn has served on the board of Hillsborough County Public Schools, headquartered in Tampa, Florida, since 2020. It's the third-largest district in the state of Florida, where school officials are swept up in a battle with the governor over masks.</p>\n<p>DeSantis <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-administration-offers-aid-to-florida-schools-defying-desantis-2021-8\">banned mask mandates</a> in schools just weeks before students were set to go back, threatening to withhold state funding to schools that had mask requirements. The order runs contrary to current guidance from the <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/community/schools-childcare/k-12-guidance.html\">CDC</a>, which recommends all students and staff wear masks indoors regardless of vaccination status.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ron-desantis-people-issues-problems-presidential-run-2021-8\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">11 feuds and controversies threatening to sink Florida Gov. Ron DeSantis' rise toward a 2024 White House run</a></em></p>\n<p>On Monday, days before many Florida kids returned to the classroom, DeSantis doubled down on his anti-mask crusade, threatening to withhold paychecks of school leaders flouting his ban.</p>\n<p>Vaughn said the ban and the timing of the announcement left the school district scrambling to return kids to the classroom in the safest possible way, especially as the Delta variant tears through the state. She said parents have been \"hysterical\" trying to decide if it's safe for their kids to be in school.</p>\n<p>\"You have panicked parents, people who feel, 'what are my choices: either sending my child into a potentially threatening, dangerous environment where they could get very sick or bring home sickness, or not send them to school?'\" she said.</p>\n<p>In July the school wasn't considering a mask mandate, Vaughn said, but in the past few weeks the more transmissible Delta variant, which is causing a huge <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/schools-reopening-covid-cases-rising-quarantine-2021-8\">spike in infections among children</a>, changed everything.</p>\n<p>She said the pressure from parents to mandate masks made it obvious it would be the right thing to do, \"but before we really had a chance to pivot, the governor came down pretty hard and early with his threats.\"</p>\n<p>Some parents in the district oppose masks, resulting in heated school board meetings where members are called \"Nazis\" and \"fascists\" and accused of child abuse for recommending masks, Vaughn said.</p>\n<p>But she added the board receives twice as many emails from pro-mask parents who are afraid to come to the meetings and be in tight indoor spaces with anti-maskers who are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/father-threatened-by-anti-maskers-at-school-board-meeting-still-scared\">sometimes aggressive</a>.</p>\n<p>Vaughn said DeSantis is not only ignoring the concerns of parents and healthcare providers in her community but also making it impossible for officials like her to govern at the local level.</p>\n<p>\"We should have the ability to make decisions for the people who elected us,\" she said, adding that his ban represents an overreach of state government, preventing local communities from making the best decisions for themselves. She said it's the same thing DeSantis lashes out at the federal government for doing to states.</p>\n<p>DeSantis has fought especially hard for Florida to make its own decisions during the pandemic, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/travel/2021/04/08/florida-desantis-cdc-cruise-lawsuit/\">suing the Biden administration and the CDC</a> over cruise ship restrictions.</p>\n<p>Insider has reached out to DeSantis's office for comment.</p>\n<p>Vaughn said the disconnect between what the state is doing and what her local community wants is unbearable, prompting some parents to ask: \"How is this even happening?\"</p>\n<p>She shares their desperation: \"I don't know how we got to a place where it's okay to gamble with our children's health and safety,\" Vaughn said.</p>\n<p>Parents in her district have begged the board to fight against the state, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/florida-school-officials-battle-governor-ron-desantis-over-mask-mandates-2021-8\">as other districts have done</a>, but the superintendent has said the district <a href=\"https://twitter.com/WFLAJustin/status/1423725626104627203?s=20\">cannot risk losing even a cent of state funding</a>. For now, the district is trying its best to mitigate COVID-19 transmission without defying the governor.</p>\n<p>However, if the first week back was any indication, it's going to be an uphill battle: After just four days, nearly <a href=\"https://www.smore.com/h5pc6\">4,500 students were under isolation or quarantine orders</a> after a positive test or exposure, and nearly 500 people - students and teachers - reported they had <a href=\"https://www.hillsboroughschools.org/coviddashboard\">tested positive for COVID-19</a>.</p>\n<p><em>Have a news tip? src=\"https://i.insider.com/611879ff3dd01000199dbe06?format=jpeg\" alt=\"In this July 13, 2021 file photo radio talk show host Larry Elder speaks to supporters during a campaign stop in Norwalk, class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Marcio Jose Sanchez, File</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>If elected, Elder would declare a &#34;homeless emergency&#34; to suspend the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), which reduces the environmental impacts of proposed projects.</li>\n<li>Elder said homeless individuals with schizophrenia should be institutionalized for safety reasons.</li>\n<li>By removing rules and regulations, Elder said building cost-effective housing would only take months.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>In an <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oQWc_ttA4n8\">August 2 interview</a> with the Sacramento Bee, Republican candidate for California governor Larry Elder said that, if elected, he would implement a plan to house homeless Californians created by former Department of Housing and Urban Development Secretary Ben Carson and Los Angeles Mayor Eric Garcetti.</p><p>Elder said he would declare a &#34;homeless emergency&#34; in which he would suspend the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) so that he can &#34;unleash&#34; developers and contractors who would be able to build low-cost housing and apartments on government land.</p><p>The California Department of General Services evaluated over 44,000 parcels of land and developed a map of <a href=\"https://cadgs.maps.arcgis.com/apps/webappviewer/index.html?id=392e5e687e9041bb8f20e3acc5b211c7\">suitable sites for affordable housing</a> throughout the state.</p><p>&#34;I&#39;ve talked to a lot of developers, and a lot of them are completely demoralized, disillusioned, and many of them are building outside of California precisely because of [CEQA].&#34;</p><p>Elder said that the government also needs to deal with the underlying reasons that cause homelessness in addition to building cost-effective housing.</p><p>&#34;We have a certain percentage of people who are on the streets who are simply schizophrenic. By that, I mean a danger to themselves or others,&#34; Elder said. &#34;Some percentage - I&#39;m not sure how many - literally have to be removed from the street and put in a mental institution for their own safety and for the safety of the rest of the homeless population.&#34; </p><p>Additionally, Elder said the rest of the homeless population is &#34;probably alcoholics, mentally ill, or have substance abuse problems,&#34; and needs treatment.</p><p>Asked by Sacramento Bee columnist Marcos Breton about the timeline it would take to implement the plan, Elder said he thinks it would only take a matter of months to build cost-effective housing if burdensome rules and regulations were removed.</p><p>Although Carson said Garcetti had signed off on the plan, it did not go forward because Donald Trump did not win a second term.</p><p>&#34;If I am elected governor, if I&#39;m lucky enough to be put in that position, and I fail to solve the homeless problem, then I will have been a failure. I&#39;m going to make it one of my top priorities,&#34; Elder said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a week's vacation to the Greek island of Santorini and was met with five expensive COVID-19 tests that cost more than the $300 flights.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img to enter Greece.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6111493538aff700189084b6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Cliff coastline of Fira, the capital city of Santorini, Greece.\" height=\"4000\" width=\"6000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Coastline of Fira, the capital city of Santorini, Greece.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Duffy/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Greek authorities require arrivals to take a COVID-19 test three days before they travel there, the UK government <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/foreign-travel-advice/greece/entry-requirements\">website</a> says.&#160;</p><p>These tests have to be done privately, not through the UK's National Health Service (NHS), so people have to pay for them.</p><p>People from the UK, who have been fully vaccinated with an NHS administered vaccine, don't need to test to enter Greece. They just have to show proof of of being fully vaccinated at least 14 days before their trip.</p><p>&#160;</p>\n\tI took a rapid antigen test, which cost $42, within 48 hours of arriving in Santorini and tested negative.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/610c02f338aff700189005c1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Insider&#39;s Kate Duffy waiting in an airport queue\" height=\"4032\" width=\"3024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Insider&#39;s Kate Duffy waiting in line to board the aircraft.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Duffy/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>There was also the option to take a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-test-rapid-antigen-test-lateral-flow-pcr-explained-2021-1?r=US&#38;IR=T\">PCR test</a> 72 hours before arrival &#8212; this test costs around &#163;75 ($105).</p><p>Having caught COVID-19 a week before my first vaccine appointment and one month before my flight to Santorini, I wasn't able to get the first shot in time for my vacation.</p>\n\tAfter showing my negative test result to airport staff, I got a slip of paper indicating I was safe to travel.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6113f4c13dd01000199d2234?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Picture of passport and slip of paper saying &#34;good to travel&#34; This time, the test was free.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/610c03e338aff7001890062f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The front of Santorini airport.\" height=\"3024\" width=\"4032\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Departures at Santorini airport.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Duffy/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>One person from every group on the flight had to have a free rapid antigen test at the airport. I got my negative result within five minutes and was free to go.</p>\n\tSix days into my chilled vacation, I had to pay $117 for a PCR test to return to the UK.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/610c04052a24d0001861dd64?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Coastline of Fira, the capital city of Santorini, Greece.\" height=\"3024\" width=\"4032\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The coastline of Fira, the capital city of Santorini, Greece.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Duffy/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>I had to test negative for COVID-19 within 72 hours of landing in the UK.</p>\n\tMy $117 COVID-19 test in Santorini got me onto an empty plane back to London.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/610c03bc2a24d0001861dd3d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A selfie of Insider&#39;s Kate Duffy sat on an empty plane\" height=\"2316\" width=\"3088\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Insider&#39;s Kate Duffy sat on an empty plane back to the UK.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Duffy/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tAs soon as I arrived in the UK, I had to isolate for 10 days and pay $208 for COVID-19 PCR tests on day two and day eight of quarantine.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6111458b38aff70018908371?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The COVID-19 test center in London where Insider&#39;s Kate Duffy went to get tested.\" height=\"2274\" width=\"3024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The COVID-19 test center in London, where Insider&#39;s Kate Duffy went to get tested.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Duffy/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The UK currently classes countries as green, amber, and red on its traffic light system, spawned from the pandemic. Green countries are deemed safer to travel to compared to red countries, therefore they have less restrictions.</p><p>Most of the rules depends on whether you're fully vaccinated.</p><p>Greece is classed as amber. This means people traveling back to the UK must quarantine for 10 days when they return.</p><p>Fully vaccinated travelers don't need to quarantine, the UK government <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/news/quarantine-free-travel-to-resume-on-19-july-for-fully-vaccinated-passengers-returning-from-amber-list-countries\">announced</a> in July. They still have to take a COVID-19 test on or before day two of their return.</p>\n\tI went to the test center and took my first PCR test in the morning of day two. I received a certificate of my negative result by 6pm the same day.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/610c03d22a24d0001861dd49?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Selfie of Insider&#39;s Kate Duffy holding a COVID-19 test tube\" height=\"2316\" width=\"3088\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>First day of COVID-19 testing in quarantine.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Duffy/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tI chose to pay another $105 for a test on Day 5, which allowed me to come out of isolation so long as I tested negative. This is called the Test to Release scheme.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61112e2b2a24d0001862582a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Selfie of Insider&#39;s Kate Duffy holding COVID-19 test tube\" height=\"3088\" width=\"2316\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An optional, second test on day five.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Duffy/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\t\"Test to Release\" is optional and cuts the quarantine period in half, but I still had to take a test on day eight.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/610d51be38aff70018903bc9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Test tube for COVID-19 test\" height=\"2274\" width=\"3024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Test to Release COVID-19 test tube for day five.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kate Duffy/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tI had my sixth and final PCR test on day eight and tested negative. Overall, the three quarantine tests after my vacation cost $312.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61112ea838aff70018907e56?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Picture of COVID-19 test tube\" totalling $470, were more expensive than the $300 return flights to Santorini, but it was still worth the money after such a turbulent year!\n\t<figure>\n\t<img 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"A pro-Trump county clerk is accused of helping to leak sensitive election data to one of QAnon's leaders: reports","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/colorado-pro-trump-official-accused-of-leaking-election-data-qanon-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6117a43ec040ad0018ce56d7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tina Peters, left, and Ron Watkins, right.\" height=\"1000\" width=\"1333\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tina Peters, a Mesa County clerk, is accused of allowing information to be leaked to Ron Watkins.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mesa County, OAN/Youtube</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Colorado&#39;s secretary of state said that a county clerk is accused of &#34;assisting&#34; in a security breach.</li>\n<li>Sensitive election data collected during the breach was leaked to Ron Watkins, Vice reported.</li>\n<li>Watkins, who is believed by some to be &#39;Q,&#39; shared information from the leak on his Telegram channel.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A pro-Trump election official in Colorado is accused of assisting in the compromising of voting machines and allowing someone to leak sensitive data to a prominent <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/qanon-history-who-is-q-conspiracy-theory-what-does-believe-2021-2\">QAnon</a> influencer, according to <a href=\"https://www.vice.com/en/article/88nbza/elections-official-accused-of-helping-leak-data-to-qanon-leader\">Vice.</a></p><p>Tina Peters, a county clerk in Mesa, Colorado, and so-called <a href=\"https://coloradosun.com/2021/08/11/mesa-county-voting-littwin-opinion/\">&#34;Trump Truther,&#34;</a>  permitted surveillance cameras to be turned off for up to two months, it is alleged. During that time, she has allowed someone to steal information that was then leaked to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/qanon-into-the-storm-cullen-hoback-ron-jim-watkins-2021-4\">QAnon figurehead Ron Watkins,</a> the media outlet reported.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/federal-appointees-supported-trumps-election-lies-2021-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Dozens of people who supported radical right-wing efforts to overturn the 2020 election currently sit on government boards running places like the Holocaust Memorial and the Kennedy Center</a></em></p><p>At some point in May, Peters&#39;s office reportedly ordered officials to turn off the surveillance cameras monitoring Mesa County&#39;s voting equipment, according to evidence from Colorado&#39;s Democratic Secretary of State Jenna Griswold.</p><p>The cameras were not turned on again until this month, Vice reported, which broke the equipment&#39;s &#34;chain of custody&#34; and means that the machines cannot be used in November&#39;s city, town, and school district elections.</p><p>&#34;This is troubling for the entire state of Colorado to have someone in a trusted position, literally trusted to protect democracy, allow this type of situation to occur,&#34; Griswold said during a Thursday press conference. &#34;To be very clear, Mesa County Clerk and Recorder allowed a security breach and by all evidence at this point assisted it.&#34;</p><p>On May 23, an unknown person gained access to one of the Election Management Systems machines from <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-oan-one-america-news-election-conspiracy-theories-2021-3\">Dominion Voting Systems</a> used by Mesa County, Vice reported. That person was then able to download an image of the machine&#39;s hard drive, a process repeated on May 26, a cybersecurity expert told Vice.</p><p>On May 25, Dominion employees visited the country to conduct a highly-regulated &#34;trusted build&#34; upgrade to the voting machines&#39; software, the media outlet said.</p><p>According to state law, only staff from Griswold&#39;s office, Mesa County, and Dominion are permitted to be in the room during a &#34;trusted build.&#34;</p><p>Peters, however, invited an unauthorized non-employee into the room during the process, the <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/technology-colorado-business-biden-cabinet-voting-rights-99f2e469d109f758254fe145bacb24e8\">Associated Press</a> reported. She misled Griswold about his employment status, <a href=\"https://denver.cbslocal.com/2021/08/12/security-breach-mesa-county-elections-office-secretary-state-colorado-tina-peters/\">CBS Denver</a> said.</p><p>While the unauthorized man was there, he allegedly illegally captured footage of the machines being updated.</p><p>On August 2, this footage was posted to Watkin&#39;s Telegram channel. The former 8chan owner and administrator has fervently promoted the QAnon conspiracy theory, and some people believe that <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/who-is-q-why-people-think-jim-watkins-qanon-8chan-2020-10\">him and his father could be the infamous &#39;Q.&#39;</a></p><p>According to Griswold&#39;s team, the footage included an image that accidentally linked the leak to Mesa County.</p><p>Griswold issued an order last week authorizing her staff to travel to Mesa County to inspect the election system, but when they arrived, Peters was nowhere to be seen.</p><p>Peters was on her way to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-oan-one-america-news-election-conspiracy-theories-2021-3\">MyPillow CEO Mike Lindell&#39;s</a> <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/mike-lindell-antifa-things-people-singing-hymns-in-parking-lot-2021-8\">&#34;cyber symposium&#34;</a> in South Dakota, Vice reported.</p><p>While speaking at the event, the <a href=\"https://coloradonewsline.com/2021/08/12/mesa-county-clerk-allegedly-allowed-unauthorized-person-to-attend-election-software-upgrade/\">Colorado Newsline</a> reported that Peters accused Griswold&#39;s office of &#34;raiding&#34; her county&#39;s office.</p><p>At the South Dakota symposium, Vice said that Watkins showed the audience images that appear to have been taken from the Mesa County machines on May 23 and May 26.</p><p>Griswold&#39;s office is investigating the security breach, Colorado Newsline reported. An investigator with 21st Judicial District Attorney Dan Rubinstein&#39;s office is also looking into related potential criminal conduct, according to the local paper.</p><div
