11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"The US economy might've reached peak recovery","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-economic-recovery-hit-peak-delta-variant-cases-economic-data-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6116c0a73dd01000199da79a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"vacant mall oculus\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Oculus transportation hub and mall stands nearly deserted in lower Manhattan on March 29, 2020 in New York City.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Spencer Platt/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Recent economic data suggests the US recovery is slowing from the rapid pace of early summer.</li>\n<li>Americans are spending less, unemployment filings are flatlining, and confidence in the recovery plummeted in August.</li>\n<li>Americans are bracing for a slower rebound as the Delta variant sends case counts skyrocketing.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The US economy is still getting better. But the pace of recovery might be slowing down.</p><p>After a summer of reopening, vaccination, and lower cases, the coronavirus is bouncing back. The Delta variant&#39;s spread lifted daily case counts to their highest levels since January, and authorities have since reinstated some restrictions to counter contagion.</p><p>The booming recovery of the summer - fueled by fresh stimulus and a surge of consumer spending - is fading. Second-quarter economic growth has already proved disappointing, coming in at an annualized rate of 6.5% compared to the median estimate of 8.5%. And as August data comes in, the virus resurgence is likely to slow activity.</p><p>Early indicators suggest the recovery has already peaked. Whether growth rebounds depends on Americans accepting jobs and continuing to spend.</p><h2>Spending fueled by reopenings is starting to slow down</h2><p>Chase credit- and debit-card spending data tracked by JPMorgan shows a sharp decline in spending on categories most affected by reopening since mid-July. Spending at restaurants sits slightly below the highs seen last month. Activity at hotels and other lodging businesses, however, is down notably from its summer peak. And spending on airlines has plunged before even returning to its pre-pandemic levels.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6116c897c040ad0018ce4875?format=jpeg\" alt=\"JPM\" height=\"693\" width=\"1157\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chart via JPMorgan\n<p class=\"copyright\">JPMorgan</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>The broad drop in spending corresponds with daily case counts, which started to swing higher early last month. Taken together, it seems virus fears and the return of some mask-wearing rules led Americans to pull back on reopening.<h2>Unemployment filings are flatlining</h2><p>While just a fraction of the highs seen earlier in the crisis, weekly filings for unemployment benefits have hovered around 370,000 after sliding through most of the year. The latest reading <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/weekly-jobless-claims-375000-labor-market-recovery-unemployment-benefits-hiring-2021-8\">came in at 375,000</a>, matching forecasts but still above the pandemic-era low.</p><p>To be sure, continuing claims, which track Americans receiving benefits, staged a more promising recovery through the end of July. Yet both weekly and continuing claims are roughly double their pre-pandemic levels, and recent reports hint at a plodding recovery as Delta cases climb.</p><div class=\"insider-raw-embed\"><iframe title=\"Initial unemployment claims\" aria-label=\"Interactive area chart\" id=\"datawrapper-chart-fKAO5\" src=\"https://datawrapper.dwcdn.net/fKAO5/58/\" scrolling=\"no\" frameborder=\"0\" style=\"width: 0; min-width: 100% ; border: none;\" height=\"450\"></iframe><script type=\"text/javascript\">!function(){&#34;use strict&#34;;window.addEventListener(&#34;message&#34;,(function(e){if(void 0!==e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;]){var t=document.querySelectorAll(&#34;iframe&#34;);for(var a in e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;])for(var r=0;r&#60;t.length;r++){if(t[r].contentWindow===e.source)t[r].style.height=e.data[&#34;datawrapper-height&#34;][a]+&#34;px&#34;}}}))}();</script></div><h2>Americans are bracing for the worst</h2><p>Consumer sentiment <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/university-michigan-sentiment-delta-fear-lockdown-cases-rising-july-report-2021-8\">plummeted to 70.2</a> in early August from 81.2, according to the University of Michigan&#39;s Surveys of Consumers. That&#39;s the lowest reading since 2011 and the largest one-month drop since confidence evaporated at the start of the pandemic. The only steeper drops came when virus lockdowns began in April 2020 and at the worst period of the Great Recession in December 2008. </p><p>The souring of economic hopes was broad-based. Americans cited increased concerns around inflation, unemployment, and their personal finances. Losses were spread across age, income, educational, and geographical lines, according to the university. And measures of current and future conditions also tanked, suggesting people were prepared for the Delta variant to pose a lingering threat.</p><p>The sentiment metric can stage a quick recovery and even shift toward optimism if the country can get a handle on the virus&#39;s spread, Richard Curtin, chief economist at the Surveys of Consumers, said in the report. Still, with spending on the decline, Americans still leaning on unemployment, and recovery hopes worsening, it seems the country is getting ready for a steeper climb ahead.</p><div Kiersz)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/6116c0a73dd01000199da79a?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn16@2020_6/2021/08/15/03-53-29-267_cd65d3c169f34566.webp","https://i.insider.com/6116c897c040ad0018ce4875?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn9@2020_6/2021/08/15/03-53-31-937_3b3b7e4c5499d86a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn49@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-32-122_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=d-UvWmkSG5s:Ds2z6TR1LkU:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn46@2020_3/2021/08/15/03-53-31-713_4df3b4b59afb34bc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=d-UvWmkSG5s:Ds2z6TR1LkU:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn31@2020_3/2021/08/15/03-53-30-355_1779bd58416a3e9b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn27@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-30-405_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=d-UvWmkSG5s:Ds2z6TR1LkU:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn78@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-32-986_270c25b1eacc3c45.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/d-UvWmkSG5s":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn88@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-29-945_b6f457426b8a040f.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1628999590246},{"createdTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"A fragment of a mysterious 8th continent is hiding under New Zealand - and it's twice as old as scientists thought","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/hidden-continent-zealandia-under-new-zealand-age-map-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ef25d52f34d05343f6fe848?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Zealandia_topography\" height=\"1617\" width=\"1391\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A map of New Zealandia, outlined in gray.\n<p class=\"copyright\">World Data Center for Geophysics &#38; Marine Geology / National Geophysical Data Center, NOAA</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>An eighth continent, called <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/zealandia-continent-new-zealand-australia-2017-2\">Zealandia</a>, is hidden under New Zealand and the surrounding Pacific.</li>\n<li>Since 94% of Zealandia is submerged, discerning the continent&#39;s age and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/maps-reveal-eighth-continent-zealandia-underwater-2020-6\">mapping it</a> is difficult.</li>\n<li>New research suggests Zealandia is 1 billion years old, about twice as old as geologists thought.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>About 3,500 feet under the south Pacific sits a piece of land 2 million square miles in size - about half as big as Australia.</p><p>But scientists can&#39;t agree on whether this submerged land mass, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/zealandia-continent-new-zealand-australia-2017-2\">called Zealandia</a>, is a continent or not. A team of geologists <a href=\"https://www.geosociety.org/gsatoday/archive/27/3/article/GSATG321A.1.htm\">declared it one</a> in 2017, but not all researchers are convinced. </p><p>&#34;It&#39;s not like a mountain, country, or planet. There is no formal body to approve a continent,&#34;  Nick Mortimer, a geologist from New Zealand&#39;s GNS Science who led 2017 group, told Insider.</p><p>While the definition of a continent is contentious, Mortimer&#39;s group suggested that a continent should have clearly defined boundaries, occupy an area greater than 386,000 square miles (1 million square kilometers), be elevated above the surrounding ocean crust, and have a continental crust thicker than that oceanic crust.</p><p>Zealandia meets all those stipulations.</p><p>&#34;If you were to drain the oceans, Zealandia would stand out as a well-defined, high-standing plateau above the ocean floor,&#34; Mortimer said.</p><p>He considers it &#34;the thinnest, most submerged and smallest continent.&#34;</p><p>The problem, however, was that until recently, the oldest crust and rock ever sampled from Zealandia was just 500 million years old, whereas all the other continents contain crust that is 1 billion years old or more. <a href=\"https://pubs.geoscienceworld.org/gsa/geology/article/49/8/1009/598229/A-hidden-Rodinian-lithospheric-keel-beneath\">But a recent study</a> found that part of the submerged continent is twice as old as geologists previously thought, which could boost Mortimer&#39;s argument.</p><p>&#34;This new study ticks that final continental box,&#34; Rose Turnbull, a New Zealand geologist who co-authored the study, said <a href=\"https://www.gns.cri.nz/Home/News-and-Events/Media-Releases-and-News/Continent-of-Zealandia-older-than-previously-thought-study-finds-18-05-2021\">in a press release</a>. &#34;There is no longer any doubt that we live on top of a continent.&#34;</p><h2>How to date a continent</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60d5df13df1db80018f3a2e7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A view of Fiordland National Park\" height=\"2680\" width=\"4020\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A view of Fiordland National Park on New Zealand&#39;s South Island.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Aaron Choi/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Zealandia, a term geophysicist Bruce Luyendyk coined in 1995, is made up of New Zealand and a collection of submerged chunks of crust that broke off an ancient supercontinent called Gondwana <a href=\"https://www.nsf.gov/discoveries/disc_summ.jsp?cntn_id=300018&org=NSF&from=newsrom=news\">about 85 million years ago</a>.</p><p>About 94% of it is underwater - Zealandia sunk under the waves about 30 million to 50 million years after it broke off Gondwana. So it&#39;s a challenging land mass to study. </p><p>The geologists behind the recent research looked at 169 chunks of Zealandia granite, which were found under New Zealand&#39;s South and Stewart Islands. Granite forms when magma crystallizes deep within the Earth&#39;s crust.</p><p>By extracting microscopic crystals from the granite, the team was able to determine both the age of the crystals themselves and of the crust in which they formed. The results showed that crust was once part of another supercontinent known as Rodinia, which formed between 1.3 billion and 900 million years ago.</p><p>In other words, Zealandia&#39;s geologic history starts far earlier than 500 million years ago.</p><h2>Mapping Zealandia in unprecedented detail</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ef25c982618b92d4620cc97?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Bathymetric\" height=\"865\" width=\"716\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A bathymetric map of New Zealandia, which shows the shape of the continent under the water.\n<p class=\"copyright\">GNS Science</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Part of <a href=\"https://www.royalsociety.org.nz/what-we-do/funds-and-opportunities/marsden/celebrating-marsden-research/photo-gallery/zircons-in-zealandia/\">Turnbull&#39;s mission</a> is to create a 4D map of Zealandia&#39;s western coast - to visualize what that boundary looks like in three dimensions and how it has changed over time. </p><p>Last year, Mortimer helped map the shape and depth of the ocean floor surrounding Zealandia - what&#39;s known as a bathymetric map.</p><p>The map, part of a global initiative to survey the planet&#39;s entire ocean floor by 2030, also revealed Zealandia&#39;s size and coastlines in unprecedented detail. In addition, Mortimer&#39;s team created a tectonic map showing the locations of the continental and oceanic crusts that make up the submerged land mass.</p><p>These new, detailed maps, paired with the discovery that parts of Zealandia are older than geologists realized, offer further evidence that it should be considered the eighth continent, according to Mortimer.</p><p>&#34;We hope that Zealandia will eventually make its way onto general world maps, be taught in schools, and become as familiar a name as Antarctica,&#34; he said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"How creator economy companies are helping influencers grow their businesses","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-creator-economy-companies-and-trends-list-of-examples-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60fb15a70729770012b9ac80?format=jpeg\" alt=\"TikTok influencer Yusuf Panseri.\" height=\"3554\" width=\"4740\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>TikTok influencer Yusuf Panseri.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Miguel Medina/AFP via Getty Images.</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The creator economy has surged in 2021, and a new crop of startups has emerged to cash in.</li>\n<li>These upstarts are launching tools to help creators connect with fans, film content, and earn money.</li>\n<li>Here&#39;s a breakdown of Insider&#39;s recent coverage on up-and-coming creator companies.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>From gamers to beauty influencers, interest in building a career as a content creator has spiked in the past year, with over 50 million people now considering themselves creators, according to investment firm SignalFire.</p><p>And a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-creator-economy-startups-to-watch-in-2021-vc-investors-2021-8?r=creator-startups-lp\">new crop of startups</a> has emerged to service the various needs of these digital stars.</p><p>These companies are reimagining the ways influencers connect to fans, produce content, and run their businesses. And they&#39;ve <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-creator-economy-startups-to-watch-in-2021-vc-investors-2021-8?r=creator-startups-lp\">caught the attention</a> of venture-capital investors who have poured hundreds of millions of dollars into content creator startups in the past year, according to data from Crunchbase. </p><p>&#34;The creator economy will comprise a vast percentage of the workforce of the future, and those creators will need financial services to meet their needs - both as businesses and individuals,&#34; Alexa von Tobel, founding partner at Inspired Capital, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-creator-economy-startups-to-watch-in-2021-vc-investors-2021-8?r=creator-startups-lp\">told Insider</a>. </p><p><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-creator-economy-startups-to-watch-in-2021-vc-investors-2021-8?r=creator-startups-lp\">Check out Insider&#39;s list of 20 creator economy startups to watch, according to top VCs</a></strong></p><h2><strong>Startups building new monetization tools for creators</strong></h2><p>Many of the new startups in the influencer industry are developing products to help creators make money. </p><p>One such company, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pearpop-raises-10-million-to-help-influencers-earn-from-collabs-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\">Pearpop</a>, runs a marketplace for TikTok and Instagram creators to pay - or get paid - to collaborate on content with other users, brands, and marketers. </p><p>The company got its start by building a platform to make TikTok &#34;duets&#34; and sounds monetizable, and it has since expanded to Instagram.</p><p>&#34;The goal here is to be the epicenter for opportunities to scale and monetize as creators,&#34; said Spencer Markel, Pearpop&#39;s president.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pearpop-raises-10-million-to-help-influencers-earn-from-collabs-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\"><strong>Read more about how Pearpop&#39;s marketplace helps creators make money through collaborations</strong></a></p><p>Other startups are building creator marketplaces designed to service a particular niche within the creator economy.</p><p>Agnes Kozera and Dave Kierzkowski cofounded <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/famebit-founder-explains-new-podcast-startup-podcorn-ad-rates-2020-12?r=creator-startups-lp\">Podcorn</a> to help connect podcast creators with brands, selling the tool to audio giant Entercom (now Audacy) earlier this year for $22.5 million.</p><p>Another upstart called <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/startup-kollyde-helps-chinese-brands-with-influencer-marketing-abroad-2021-1?r=creator-startups-lp\">Kollyde</a> launched a tool to help Asian multinational brands run influencer campaigns in other markets.</p><p>&#34;China has its own internet ecosystem,&#34; Amy Vida, Kollyde&#39;s cofounder and managing director, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/startup-kollyde-helps-chinese-brands-with-influencer-marketing-abroad-2021-1?r=creator-startups-lp\">told Insider</a>. &#34;They have their own local video platforms, social media, ecommerce, and live video ecommerce ... But when it comes to cross-border marketing, it&#39;s an entirely different set of platforms and also a different set of creators.&#34;</p><p><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/startup-kollyde-helps-chinese-brands-with-influencer-marketing-abroad-2021-1?r=creator-startups-lp\">Learn more about how Kollyde is helping Chinese companies hire influencers in the US and other regions</a></strong></p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/601189586dfbe10018e0037d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Amy Vida - Kollyde\" height=\"1200\" width=\"1600\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Amy Vida, cofounder and managing director at Kollyde\n<p class=\"copyright\">Maxwell Poth/Kollyde.</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Other startups in the creator economy are building tools to help influencers launch their own direct-to-consumer brands.</p><p>One company called <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pietra-launches-platform-for-influencers-to-create-their-own-products-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\">Pietra</a> built a platform to connect creators with product designers, manufacturers, and warehouse companies in order to launch their own consumer goods. Users of the tool can choose to create products in a variety of categories, including coffee, clothing, and fragrances. Pietra charges a handling fee for any samples ordered, a production fee, and fees for product assembly, quality assurance, warehouse work, and additional services such as shipping and fulfillment.</p><p>&#34;Anyone with the drive and motivation to bring their idea to life can get access to the same infrastructure that the top creators historically have gotten,&#34; Pietra cofounder Ronak Trivedi <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pietra-launches-platform-for-influencers-to-create-their-own-products-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\">told Insider</a>. &#34;You no longer need to fly around the world, find a factory, beg them to work with you, plead for low minimums. We&#39;re trying to build a world where a creator, a single creator, can create the next best-selling brand.&#34;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pietra-launches-platform-for-influencers-to-create-their-own-products-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\"><strong>Read more about how Pietra is helping influencers design and manufacture their own products</strong></a></p><h2><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6074374c3e3fe7001882a108?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Ronak Trivedi\" height=\"810\" width=\"1080\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ronak Trivedi.</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></h2><p>Another company in the space, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mrbeast-burger-team-on-influencer-ghost-kitchens-and-expansion-plans-2021-2?r=creator-startups-lp\">Virtual Dining Concepts</a>, has worked with creators like YouTube star MrBeast (Jimmy Donaldson) to launch influencer-branded restaurants. Virtual Dining Concepts recently helped the MrBeast team design a menu and create a network of hundreds of &#34;ghost kitchens&#34; (some that it owned), which paid an all-inclusive platform fee to cook and sell MrBeast Burger menu items in the US and Canada.</p><p><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mrbeast-burger-team-on-influencer-ghost-kitchens-and-expansion-plans-2021-2?r=creator-startups-lp\">Read more about the startup behind the ghost kitchen chain MrBeast Burger</a></strong></p><h2><strong>Helping creators optimize their finances and the backend of their businesses</strong></h2><p>Another focus among creator economy startups is helping influencers manage their finances.</p><p>While these companies are &#34;underhyped,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/creator-economy-investor-interview-uta-ventures-caroline-jacobs-2021-6?r=creator-startups-lp\">says</a> UTA Ventures&#39; Caroline Jacobs, they are key to providing the &#34;picks-and-shovels backend of the creator economy.&#34;</p><p>One startup, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-creator-economy-startups-to-watch-in-2021-vc-investors-2021-8#stir-17?r=creator-startups-lp\">Stir</a>, created a payments network that lets creators track their finances, and compensate employees and collaborators directly. Another upstart, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fintech-startup-karat-charge-card-for-youtube-instagram-tiktok-influencers-2020-6?r=creator-startups-lp\">Karat,</a> launched a custom charge card designed to meet the spending needs of YouTube, Instagram, and TikTok stars. It looks at a creator&#39;s social metrics, like follower count and engagement rates, rather than their FICO score to assess whether they qualify for its card.</p><p>&#34;For typical consumers, using social ranking or grading generally is not a good idea and doesn&#39;t work,&#34; Karat cofounder Will Kim said. &#34;However, what we&#39;re focused on is a segment of businesses that are driven by creative metrics. These are all leading indicators for exactly how your business works.&#34;</p><p><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fintech-startup-karat-charge-card-for-youtube-instagram-tiktok-influencers-2020-6?r=creator-startups-lp\">Read more about how fintech startup Karat designed a charge card for influencers</a> </strong></p><p>Other companies are building tools to support creators financially. Influencer-tech company ChannelMeter launched a cash payment app called &#34;<a href=\"https://creator.cash/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"57ba448978697fe4c0ccd120d7c5ae04\">Creator Cash</a>,&#34; that gives YouTube stars a cash advance on their advertising earnings.</p><p>&#34;A lot of these creators are credit thin,&#34; ChannelMeter CEO Eugene Lee <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/influencer-fintech-channelmeter-launches-youtuber-early-payment-app-2020-7?r=creator-startups-lp\">told Insider</a>. &#34;They&#39;re underbanked. As these creators grow, they&#39;re going to need the support of financial institutions.&#34;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/influencer-fintech-channelmeter-launches-youtuber-early-payment-app-2020-7?r=creator-startups-lp\"><strong>Learn more about how finance startups are launching new products designed for influencers</strong></a></p><h2><strong>Companies developing new ways for creators to distribute content</strong></h2><p>Another category of creator startups are finding new ways for influencers to connect with fans and distribute content. </p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mrbeast-and-pewdiepie-eye-facebook-in-new-partnerships-with-jellysmack-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\">Jellysmack,</a> for example, helps YouTube stars like PewDiePie redistribute their videos onto other apps like Facebook and Snapchat where they can earn additional ad revenue.</p><section data-track-content=\"\" data-post-type=\"post\"><p>&#34;A lot of creators realize that their time is better spent when they focus on creating content instead of trying to optimize for every platform,&#34; Jellysmack cofounder Michael Philippe <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mrbeast-and-pewdiepie-eye-facebook-in-new-partnerships-with-jellysmack-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\">told Insider</a>. &#34;Number one - it&#39;s really difficult. And even when they do it themselves, it&#39;s obviously very time consuming.&#34;</p><p><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mrbeast-and-pewdiepie-eye-facebook-in-new-partnerships-with-jellysmack-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\">Read more about Jellysmack&#39;s content redistribution strategy here</a></strong></p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/creator-plus-startup-making-movies-starring-creators-influencers-2021-4\">Creator+</a>, meanwhile, looks for new ways to distribute long-form content that features internet stars. The upstart, which functions as a production company, raised $12 million to produce movies starring digital talent that it will release to fans on a pay-per-view basis. </p><p>&#34;Our intention is that the movies that we&#39;re going to be working on and bringing to the market, we want to be perceived and stand up to any other movie that is being released today,&#34; Creator+ cofounder Benjamin Grubbs <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/creator-plus-startup-making-movies-starring-creators-influencers-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\">told Insider</a>.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/creator-plus-startup-making-movies-starring-creators-influencers-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\"><strong>Learn more about Creator+ and its plans to produce pay-per-view movies with digital stars</strong></a></p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6081a5c94becb800190f68ed?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Creator&#43; team\" height=\"1397\" width=\"1867\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Creator&#43; leadership team.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Creator&#43;</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></section><p>And some startups are building tools for creators that focus on a particular content category.   </p><p>The company <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tradingtv-is-a-new-livestreaming-app-focused-on-stock-trading-2021-8?r=creator-startups-lp\">Trading.TV</a> launched a new Twitch-style platform focused specifically on finance influencers. Creators who join the platform can stream about stocks, ETFs, cryptocurrencies, and other assets like NFTs and playing cards. They can also upload on-demand content to a Trading.TV video library. The company plans to introduce a feature that will let users trade stocks in real-time as they watch livestreams.</p><p>&#34;You could be like a trading card guru or you could be like a sneakerhead that&#39;s just been crazy about collecting sneakers forever,&#34; Trading.TV CEO Tobias Heaslip <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tradingtv-is-a-new-livestreaming-app-focused-on-stock-trading-2021-8?r=creator-startups-lp\">told Insider</a>. &#34;It&#39;s not just about being a stock analyst or a bitcoin expert or something like that.&#34;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tradingtv-is-a-new-livestreaming-app-focused-on-stock-trading-2021-8?r=creator-startups-lp\"><strong>Read more about Trading.TV&#39;s invite-only platform for</strong> <strong>finance livestreams</strong></a></p><p><strong>Here&#39;s a list of the creator economy companies we&#39;ve covered recently:</strong></p><p><em><strong>New startups helping creators make money:</strong></em></p><ul><li><strong>Pearpop</strong> helps TikTok and Instagram creators get paid to collaborate with other users and brands. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pearpop-raises-10-million-to-help-influencers-earn-from-collabs-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\">Here&#39;s how it works.</a></li><li><strong>Pietra</strong> is a startup that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pietra-launches-platform-for-influencers-to-create-their-own-products-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\">connects influencers with designers and manufacturers</a> to create their own products.</li><li><strong>Virtual Dining Concepts</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mrbeast-burger-team-on-influencer-ghost-kitchens-and-expansion-plans-2021-2?r=creator-startups-lp\">works with influencers like MrBeast to launch &#34;ghost kitchen&#34; restaurant brands</a>.</li><li><strong>Podcorn</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/famebit-founder-explains-new-podcast-startup-podcorn-ad-rates-2020-12?r=creator-startups-lp\">created a marketplace to connect podcasters and marketers</a>.</li><li><strong>Kollyde</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/startup-kollyde-helps-chinese-brands-with-influencer-marketing-abroad-2021-1?r=creator-startups-lp\">helps Asian multinational brands connect with influencers in other markets</a>.</li><li><strong>ProGuides</strong> is a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-much-money-esports-coaches-make-on-proguides-2021-7?r=creator-startups-lp\">platform that allows gamers to purchase coaching from high-level players</a>.</li></ul><p><em><strong>New companies helping creators optimize their finances and the backend of their businesses:</strong></em></p><ul><li><strong>Karat</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fintech-startup-karat-charge-card-for-youtube-instagram-tiktok-influencers-2020-6?r=creator-startups-lp\">created a custom charge card designed to meet the spending needs of YouTube, Instagram, and TikTok stars</a>.</li><li><strong>ChannelMeter</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/influencer-fintech-channelmeter-launches-youtuber-early-payment-app-2020-7?r=creator-startups-lp\">created a payment app to give cash advances to YouTube stars</a>.</li><li><strong>Stir</strong> is a payments network that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/top-creator-economy-startups-to-watch-in-2021-vc-investors-2021-8#stir-17?r=creator-startups-lp\">helps creators track their finances and compensate employees and collaborators directly</a>.</li></ul><p><em><strong>New upstarts helping creators make and distribute their content:</strong></em></p><ul><li><strong>Jellysmack</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mrbeast-and-pewdiepie-eye-facebook-in-new-partnerships-with-jellysmack-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\">works with creators to repurpose content from YouTube onto other ad-supported apps like Facebook and Snapchat.</a></li><li><strong>Creator+</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/creator-plus-startup-making-movies-starring-creators-influencers-2021-4?r=creator-startups-lp\">produces long-form movies featuring internet stars</a>. </li><li><strong>Community</strong> and <strong>Subtext</strong> are betting that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-text-messaging-helps-influencers-media-brands-reach-fans-customers-2021-1?r=creator-startups-lp\">text messaging will surge as a way for influencers to reach fans.</a></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spore-pitch-deck-helped-creator-economy-startup-get-investment-2021-7?r=creator-startups-lp\">Spore</a></strong>, <strong>Linktree</strong>, and <strong>Beacons </strong>are link-in-bio startups <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/startups-like-linktree-beacons-and-koji-eye-creator-monetization-2021-5?r=creator-startups-lp\">offering webpage tools and money-making features for creators</a>.</li><li><strong>Trading.TV</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tradingtv-is-a-new-livestreaming-app-focused-on-stock-trading-2021-8?r=creator-startups-lp\">built a new Twitch-style platform focused specifically on finance influencers</a>.</li></ul><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"More small houses are starting to hit the market, and it's another sign that the bonkers housing market is starting to get a little better","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/small-house-listings-increasing-amid-improving-housing-market-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/611156052a24d00018626453?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Open House sign remax getty\" height=\"2248\" width=\"2997\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An &#34;Open House&#34; sign is seen outside of a house for sale.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tim Boyle/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The real estate market is slowly getting better, particularly for anyone looking for a small house.</li>\n<li>The share of small houses for sale jumped in July 2021, according to Realtor.com data.</li>\n<li>Plus, new listings are up 6.5%, homes are getting more affordable, and competition has slowed.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>House-hunters, rejoice: The wild real estate market <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/housing-market-prices-getting-better-sales-affordability-crisis-3-signs-2021-8\">might finally be getting better</a>, particularly for first-time buyers or anyone looking for a small house. </p><p>Yes, inventory is still low nationwide, down 33.5% in July compared to the year prior, according to <a href=\"https://www.realtor.com/research/july-2021-data/\">new Realtor.com data</a>. But the decline is less than the drop in June (43.1%), new listings have risen 6.5% nationwide compared to the same period last year, and the inventory coming on the market could spell some good news for buyers looking for an affordable home: Smaller homes are slowly gaining a larger share of the inventory, according to the data.</p><p>When it comes to single-family homes, the share of houses for sale between 750 and 1,750 square feet jumped to 36.3% in July 2021, up from 30.2% during the same time last year. Meanwhile, the inventory of homes between 3,000 and 6,000 square feet dropped to 20.1%, down from 24.2% in July 2020.</p><p>At the same time, houses are getting more affordable. While the median home price for active listings in the US stayed the same between June and July this year - $385,000 - the median listing price increased at a slower rate in July than in the month prior, according to Realtor.com.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-suburbs-america-affordable-home-prices-low-crime-good-schools-2021-8\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">The 7 best suburbs worth moving to right now, where people earn more money and homes are cheaper</a></em></p><p>Overall, this means a rosier outlook for homebuyers, according to Sabrina Speianu, a senior economic research analyst at Realtor.com and the report&#39;s author. </p><p>&#34;For homebuyers, this means that there may be more affordable inventory available depending on their metro-area,&#34; she wrote. &#34;For home sellers, this means that while their home values are still growing, they may need to consider pricing more competitively than they have in the past.&#34; </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a58270e25d05001880c945?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Home for sale open house\" height=\"1660\" width=\"2213\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Xinhua/Wang Ying via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>Less competition and dropping prices</h2><p>When people <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/realtors-working-nonstop-amid-surging-buyer-demand-2021-5\">began snapping up homes in 2020</a> due to a pandemic-induced desire for more space and low interest rates, it led to soaring prices and aggressive bidding wares that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/homebuyers-need-lots-of-cash-to-buy-realtors-say-2021-6\">boxed many buyers out of the market</a>. While the craze has led to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stories-homeowners-sold-houses-real-estate-agent-reached-out-2021-5\">some homeowners making big money</a>, it&#39;s also led to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/millennial-homebuyers-biggest-regrets-after-buying-house-2021-6\">regrets among homebuyers</a> who snapped up homes too quickly. </p><p>According to <a href=\"https://www.redfin.com/news/housing-market-update-buying-conditions-improve/\">a recent report</a> from from real estate website Redfin, there&#39;s less competition now than there was a few months ago. Homes are spending slightly longer on the market - 16 days on average - and, for the first time since 2018, people no longer cite bidding wars as the main reason they weren&#39;t able to get the home they wanted, according to the <a href=\"https://nahbnow.com/2021/07/buyers-outlook-on-housing-availability-and-affordability-declines-in-first-half-of-2021/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"a2b83b7ffdb948e9e481bf100455c07a\">Housing Trends Report</a> released by the National Association of Home Builders.</p><p>Sellers are have also started dropping their prices, with the share of listings that had price drops in July rising to 4.7%, the highest percentage since 2019, according to Redfin. </p><p>Fewer people are also <a href=\"https://www.mba.org/2021-press-releases/august/mortgage-applications-decrease-in-latest-mba-weekly-survey\">applying for mortgages</a>: The Mortgage Bankers Association reported that applications dropped 1.7% week-over-week during the week ending July 30, hitting their lowest level since May 2020.</p><p>Plus, while people requesting home tours was up 14% from January 1 to August 3, that&#39;s a smaller spike than the 39% jump during the same period in 2020, Redfin reported, citing data from home tour technology company <a href=\"https://www.showingtime.com/impact-of-coronavirus/\">ShowingTime</a>.</p><p>So while these shifts may be meager, they&#39;re positive signs that buying a house is slowly but surely getting a bit easier.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/small-house-listings-increasing-amid-improving-housing-market-2021-8'>Business 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"Lumber prices have tumbled 70% in the last 14 weeks following a blistering rally as record-setting demand slows","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/lumber-price-today-now-commodity-sawmill-housing-market-homebuilding-delta-2021-08","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6116ca4c3dd01000199dab63?format=jpeg\" alt=\"lumber and building materials store\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shannon Stapleton/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The last 14 weeks have seen lumber fall to around $500 per thousand board feet, down 70% from its all-time high in May.</li>\n<li>Now some analysts are calling a bottom while projecting flatter prices in the months ahead.</li>\n<li>Even if lumber prices normalize around $500, that&#39;s still elevated compared to pre-pandemic levels.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong><strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\">.</strong></a></li>\n</ul><p>For how steep the run-up was, lumber&#39;s plunge has been even more disorienting.</p><p>Starting its ascent in late October 2020, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/lumber-price\">lumber</a> climbed to a peak of $1,711 over the course of seven months. But it took just 14 weeks to see all those gains erased.</p><p>The last 14 weeks have seen lumber swiftly give back its gains, with the latest prices - near $500 per thousand board foot - down 70% from its all-time high in May. Now, some analysts are calling a bottom while projecting flatter prices in the months ahead.</p><p>&#34;We&#39;re going to see a stabilization,&#34; Mace McCain, CIO at Frost Investment Advisors, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/commodities/lumber-outlook-price-futures-bottom-upside-rangebound-homebuying-demand-15-2021-8\">told Insider previously</a>. &#34;We&#39;re out of the panic buying. We&#39;re out of the massive industry shortages. We&#39;re out of the extremes.&#34;</p><p>McCain said that the housing market has been behind much of the movement in lumber. As a homebuilding boom swept the US, construction firms scrambled to get their hands on lumber, sometimes buying more than was necessary for fear of running out.</p><p>But now, higher prices have cured high prices in other areas. Expensive houses have dissuaded house-buying, putting downward pressure on lumber. </p><p>On the production side, a recent survey of lumber brokers and manufacturers, who once hoarded the commodity, found that <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/commodities/lumber-market-trends-price-today-dealers-excess-inventory-supply-conditions-2021-08\">49% are now facing excess inventory</a> - another downward signal. No surveyed lumber producers reported &#34;very tight&#34; inventory in July. </p><p>Ed Egilinsky, managing director and head of alternative assets at Direxion, previously <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/commodities/lumber-price-outlook-futures-bottom-stabilize-housing-shortage-delta-variant-2021-8\">told Insider</a> that he expects $500 to be lumber&#39;s price floor and that it could even experience a rebound into the $600 region in the next 24 months. </p><p>To be sure, bouncing back to $1,700 is probably not on the cards, but Egilinsky said the combination of sawmill labor shortages, wildfires, and possible Delta variant shutdowns could crimp supply and give lumber a modest boost.</p><p>Other analysts are shooting a bit below $500. The commodities team at BMO Capital Markets looked at the share prices of three Canadian sawmill firms to derive a market-expected lumber price of $447 in 2022. Their result was first reported by the <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/lumber-prices-are-falling-fast-turning-hoarders-into-sellers-11623749401\">Wall Street Journal</a>.</p><p>Yet even if lumber prices normalize a touch above or below $500, that is still a ways away from the old, pre-pandemic normal. By contrast, the average weekly lumber price in 2019 was $372. Between 2011 and 2019 - after the financial crisis housing bust had largely passed - the average was just $337.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reopening-stock-picks-to-buy-covid-delta-variant-goldman-sachs-2021-8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Goldman Sachs names 31 stocks to buy as the economy reopens despite the looming threat of the COVID-19 Delta variant</a></em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/lguQurnMN2s\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sat, 14 Aug 2021 12:44:51 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/6116ca46c040ad0018ce4900?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"f74cbe80e040b14f81fb649a90c00e78","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn1@2020_4/2021/08/15/03-53-33-485_7327ff88615c710c.webp","destWidth":1765,"destHeight":1324,"sourceBytes":231584,"destBytes":231584,"author":"ewu@insider.com Wu)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/6116ca4c3dd01000199dab63?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn1@2020_3/2021/08/15/03-53-32-173_487ad4c352386703.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn49@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-32-122_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lguQurnMN2s:QXu_lfMPmK8:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn74@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-31-684_03536b8703f349a0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lguQurnMN2s:QXu_lfMPmK8:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn18@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-32-456_cb2fdfe91047cbb9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn27@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-30-405_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lguQurnMN2s:QXu_lfMPmK8:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn52@2020_6/2021/08/15/03-53-30-534_468db1c3ca40f723.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/lguQurnMN2s":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn55@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-29-323_580c241036c2821e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1628999590229},{"createdTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"Olivia Rodrigo's 'Driver's License' sits atop Spotify's Billions Club. The playlist reads as a who's who of the highest-earning artists, while smaller artists ask for better payouts.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/olivia-rodrigo-drivers-license-spotify-royalties-billions-club-playlist-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6116b6f43dd01000199da41d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Olivia Rodrigo&#39;s debut album &#34;Sour&#34;\" height=\"1124\" width=\"1500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Geffin/Interscope Records</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Spotify&#39;s <a href=\"https://open.spotify.com/playlist/37i9dQZF1DX7iB3RCnBnN4\">Billions Club</a> playlist compiles every song with over 1 billion streams on the platform.</li>\n<li>So far, 167 songs have hit the benchmark, which equals around $3 million in streaming royalties.</li>\n<li>Spotify accounted for more than 20% of recorded music revenue in 2020, and many artists are asking for better payouts.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Olivia Rodrigo&#39;s hit single &#34;Driver&#39;s License&#34; is the newest addition to Spotify&#39;s Billions Club playlist, an initiative launched by the company &#34;to celebrate the world&#39;s most listened to tracks and the artists behind them.&#34;</p><p>The playlist released in late May includes every song with over 1 billion streams on Spotify, a benchmark currently met by 167 songs. For context, more than <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Vvo-2MrSgFE\">60,000 new songs</a> are uploaded to Spotify every day. </p><p>Spotify said members of the growing club receive a silver plaque that takes inspiration from the &#34;iconic framed record&#34; award given to artists when a song or album is certified platinum or gold.</p><p>The Billions Club serves as a who&#39;s-who of the highest-earning artists, featuring pop singers Harry Styles, Dua Lipa, and Post Malone, as well as Vance Joy, Bad Bunny, and Foster the People, among others. </p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Olivia Rodrigo Philippines ðŸ‡µðŸ‡­  (@OliviaRodrigoPH) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1425644444875776005?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 12, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>While some of the music industry&#39;s top players are breaking into the Billions Club, smaller artists are asking the streaming platform to raise its streaming royalties. </p><p>Streaming represents over half of global recorded music revenue, according to Spotify&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iExPc11FWUc&t=2st=2s\">&#34;</a><a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iExPc11FWUc&t=2st=2s\">How the Money Flows&#34;</a> video explainer, and Spotify accounted for more than 20% of recorded music revenue in 2020, a company spokesperson told Insider. </p><p>Spotify, which has 155 million paying subscribers, generally pays between <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-much-does-spotify-pay-per-stream\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"a7bda69fde86dd4c85b734078cdb8506\">$.003 and $.005 per stream</a>. Artists need about 326 streams to make $1, and 1 billion streams equals roughly $3 million in royalties. </p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.unionofmusicians.org/justice-at-spotify\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"4752a42acd4ca38205a19f5a495af2b0\">Union of Musicians and Allied Workers</a>, a group of more than 27,000 members of the music industry, are calling on Spotify to increase its royalty payment to at least a penny per stream. </p><p>In response to recent pressure, the Spotify founder and CEO Daniel Ek launched the <a href=\"https://loudandclear.byspotify.com/daniel-eks-perspective-on-transparency-in-the-industry/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"dd39628ea6759046191a14be2418fc39\">company initiative Loud and Clear</a> to &#34;shed light on the complicated economics of music streaming.&#34; </p><p>According to the site, <a href=\"https://www.musicbusinessworldwide.com/how-many-artists-are-generating-more-than-50k-a-year-on-spotify-over-13000/\">13,400 rights holders</a> are making over $50,000 a year - the median salary in the US - from Spotify streaming royalties. Rights holders who made more than $100,000 per year totaled 7,800, while 1,820 made more than $500,ooo per year, according to the site. </p><p>Competitor <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/soundcloud-to-pay-artists-royalties-based-on-listening-habits-2021-3\">SoundCloud announced this March</a> that the platform will pay artists royalties based on overall listening time through &#34;fan-powered royalties&#34; as opposed to the &#34;pro-rata&#34; system commonly used.</p><p>In April, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/spotify-pays-artists-half-apple-penny-per-stream-2021-4#:~:text=Apple%20Music%20said%20it%20will,stream%20%E2%80%94%20double%20what%20Spotify%20pays&text=Apple%20told%20artists%20that%20it,every%20stream%20from%20a%20listener.&text=A%20movement%20has%20launched%20in,stories%20on%20Insider's%20business%20page.ness%20page.\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"a945d418bf1008c930aeb04e4670ce74\">Apple Music said</a> its streaming royalties pay double <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-much-does-spotify-pay-per-stream\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"a7bda69fde86dd4c85b734078cdb8506\">what Spotify pays</a>. Both platforms, though, calculate royalty rates on <a href=\"https://variety.com/2021/digital/news/apple-music-pays-twice-stream-spotify-1234953590/\">a streamshare basis</a>, not a per-stream basis. As <a href=\"https://loudandclear.byspotify.com/?question=how-is-stream-share-calculated\">Spotify explains</a>, it calculates &#34;streamshare by adding up how many times music owned or controlled by a particular rights holder was streamed and dividing it by the total number of streams in that market.&#34;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"none\">-Union of Musicians and Allied Workers  (@UMAW_) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1424813492796854276?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 9, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>The World Intellectual Property Organization, a specialized agency within the UN, last month <a href=\"https://www.wipo.int/edocs/mdocs/copyright/en/sccr_41/sccr_41_3.pdf\">released a report investigating the economic and legal considerations facing artists</a> in the digital music marketplace. The report included a comparison of streaming royalties across platforms like Spotify, Apple Music, Tidal, Amazon, and more, and found &#34;royalty payments are both unsustainable and out of balance compared to the value transferred to the streaming services.&#34;</p><p>A Spotify spokesperson told Insider the royalty pool paid to music rights holders from Spotify has grown by 50%, while the number of artists generating $10,000 or $50,000 has grown by more than 80% since 2017. </p><p>&#34;That means the number of artists achieving these levels is growing significantly faster than the overall size of the royalty pool, which we think is great for the industry and is enabling even more artists to make a living from music,&#34; Spotify added. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"From all-night gaming sessions to a life-changing epiphany: Inside the college years of 29-year-old crypto billionaire Sam Bankman-Fried","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/sam-bankman-fried-profile-details-college-years-cryptocurrency-billionaire-ftx-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ba159693c6fa00195e51d7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Screenshot 2021 06 04 at 12.57.45\" height=\"1297\" width=\"2595\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sam Bankman-Fried, founder and CEO of crypto exchange FTX.\n<p class=\"copyright\">FTX Official/YouTube</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Sam Bankman Fried, the 29-year-old billionaire founder of crypto derivatives exchange FTX, wasn&#39;t always the expert he is today.</li>\n<li>Back at MIT, he was struggling to find his direction in life, according to an exclusive profile by Yahoo Finance.</li>\n<li>But one altruistic movement changed his life forever, nudging him to become the person he is today. </li>\n<li><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\"><strong>Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong></a><strong>.</strong>    </li>\n</ul><p>Sam Bankman-Fried - the 29-year-old billionaire founder of FTX, one of the most valuable cryptocurrency derivative changes in the world - has quickly become one of the most successful entrepreneurs of the modern era.</p><p>But he wasn&#39;t always so laser-focused, according to an <a href=\"https://news.yahoo.com/ftx-ceo-sam-bankman-fried-profile-085444366.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">exclusive profile by Yahoo Finance</a>. In fact, he had no plans to enter the cryptocurrency space until he discovered an altruistic movement that would change his life forever.</p><p>It all began when Bankman-Fried went to MIT - a decision decided by a flip of a coin, with Cal Tech as the other option - where he met his friends in a group house known as Epsilon Theta. </p><p>Bankman-Fried enjoyed his time at ET, pulling all-nighter game sessions that involved time pressure, something the then-freshman student enjoyed and excelled in, according to friends who spoke with <a href=\"https://news.yahoo.com/ftx-ceo-sam-bankman-fried-profile-085444366.html\">Yahoo Finance</a>. For games without the same constraint, such as chess, Bankman-Fried would insist on playing with a timer, they said.</p><p>&#34;Think of a fraternity but replace all the alcohol with the nerdiest stuff you can imagine,&#34; Adam Yedidia, who met Bankman-Fried at ET, told <a href=\"https://news.yahoo.com/ftx-ceo-sam-bankman-fried-profile-085444366.html\">Yahoo Finance</a>. </p><p>Bankman-Fried majored in physics in college, with a minor in math. But he generally found college life boring.</p><p>&#34;Nothing I learned in college ended up being useful ... other than, like, social development,&#34; Bankman-Fried told <a href=\"https://news.yahoo.com/ftx-ceo-sam-bankman-fried-profile-085444366.html\">Yahoo Finance</a>. &#34;On the academic side, though, it&#39;s all f***ing useless.&#34;</p><p>Things started to change when he was a sophomore. That year, Bankman-Fried stumbled upon &#34;<a href=\"https://www.centreforeffectivealtruism.org/\">effective altruism</a>,&#34; a movement founded by two Oxford philosophy professors, which aims to use &#34;evidence and reason to figure out how to benefit others as much as possible,&#34; according to its website.</p><p>This includes, for instance, choosing an organization to direct one&#39;s effort using empirical analysis and research.</p><p>New to the concept, Bankman-Fried had lunch with one of the founders, <a href=\"https://www.effectivealtruism.org/people/will-macaskill/]\">Will MacAskill</a>, to learn more.</p><p>&#34;That was sort of the point at which I started to think in a more principled way about what I should do with my life,&#34; Bankman-Fried told <a href=\"https://news.yahoo.com/ftx-ceo-sam-bankman-fried-profile-085444366.html\">Yahoo Finance</a>. Until then, he was leaning towards becoming an academic, but had doubts about the size of the impact he could make as a professor.</p><p>He then considered &#34;<a href=\"https://forum.effectivealtruism.org/tag/earning-to-give\">earning to give</a>,&#34; according to <a href=\"https://news.yahoo.com/ftx-ceo-sam-bankman-fried-profile-085444366.html\">Yahoo Finance</a>. This approach encourages &#34;the pursuit of a lucrative career with the purpose of donating a significant portion of the earnings to cost-effective organizations,&#34; the movement&#39;s website said.</p><p>Come his junior year, Bankman-Fried was torn between working two options, <a href=\"https://news.yahoo.com/ftx-ceo-sam-bankman-fried-profile-085444366.html\">Yahoo Finance</a> reported: working for the Center for Effective Altruism itself or at finding a job at Wall Street to pursue the earning-to-give route.</p><p>The young Bankman-Fried said he felt a gentle nudge towards the latter, <a href=\"https://news.yahoo.com/ftx-ceo-sam-bankman-fried-profile-085444366.html\">Yahoo Finance</a> said.</p><p>That summer, he interned at Jane Street Capital, a quantitative firm on Wall Street. It was there that he discovered his love for trading - finally a pursuit that didn&#39;t bore him. </p><p>The rest is history.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/crypto-trading-tips-ethereum-outlook-young-billionaire-sam-bankman-fried-2021-5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">A 29-year-old crypto billionaire who&#39;s perfected digital-currency arbitrage shares 2 tips for investors looking to get started in trading - and explains why ether is unlikely to surpass bitcoin</a></em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read Joe Biden.</li>\n<li>The election technology companies are now suing the people who spread those claims.</li>\n<li>Here&#39;s who&#39;s being sued so far.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit the Business section of Insider for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Dominion and Smartmatic have launched a series of defamation lawsuits against individuals and groups who spread election fraud conspiracy theories related to their voting machines during the 2020 presidential election.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-defamation-lawsuit-against-fox-news-election-2021-2\">Dominion filed a $1.6 billion defamation suit against Fox News</a> on Friday, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-voting-systems-machines-mike-lindell-giuliani-election-conspiracy-theory-2021-2\">more could be on their way.</a>  Dominion has sent cease-and-desist notices and warnings to preserve documents to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-trump-fox-news-newsmax-oan-sidney-powell-defamation-lawsuits-2021-1\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"bf3f9fc8e3606bac2b1cdf7c8fdaa6ed\">more than 150 people</a>, and its CEO previously told CNBC that the company was &#34;not ruling anyone out.&#34;</p><p>Because of the coronavirus pandemic, people turned to alternative ways to vote in the election, and voter fraud conspiracy theories quickly sprung up.</p><p>One posited that Dominion and Smartmatic developed technology that &#34;flipped&#34; votes from Donald Trump to Joe Biden through a method developed with the regime of the late Venezuelan dictator Hugo ChÃ¡vez.</p><p>The theory has been thoroughly debunked. That didn&#39;t stop pro-Trump attorney Sidney Powell and Trump&#39;s former personal lawyer Rudy Giuliani from <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-rudy-giuliani-13-billion-over-election-fraud-claim-2021-1\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"2367932335b168161b2790d8be5e43ec\">pushing elements of the theory</a> while filing a series of failed lawsuits seeking to overturn the results of the election. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-mypillow-ceo-mike-lindell-election-fraud-claims-voting-2021-2\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"335770bef39fa100cc7c4ca9c39c5e11\">Lindell has also spread misinformation about the machines</a>, saying Dominion &#34;built them to cheat.&#34;</p><p>As well as making the brand &#34;radioactive&#34; and putting its multiyear contracts in jeopardy, according to its attorney Tom Clare, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-rudy-giuliani-13-billion-over-election-fraud-claim-2021-1\">the allegations about Dominion also put its employees in danger</a>, the company wrote in a lawsuit.</p><p>Its customer support number received a voicemail message saying &#34;we&#39;re bringing back the firing squad,&#34; it wrote <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-rudy-giuliani-13-billion-over-election-fraud-claim-2021-1\">in the suit</a> in January. The need for heightened personal security cost Dominion <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-rudy-giuliani-13-billion-over-election-fraud-claim-2021-1\">$565,000</a>, according to the lawsuit, bringing its total costs attributed to the vote fraud claims to almost $1.2 million.</p><p>Here&#39;s a list of everyone is being sued so far.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tSidney Powell by Dominion and Smartmatic\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60390e2605ddb100195f6613?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Sidney Powell\" height=\"953\" width=\"1271\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Attorney Sidney Powell at a Trump Campaign press conference.\n<p class=\"copyright\">MANDEL NGAN/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Dominion was the first to snap.</p><p>On January 8, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-sidney-powell-libel-billion-damages-2021-1\">it filed a defamation suit against pro-Trump attorney Sidney Powell</a>, seeking $1.3 billion in damages.</p><p>Powell was one of the faces of the Trump campaign's legal team in November, but <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-campaign-purges-conspiracy-theorist-attorney-sidney-powell-2020-11\">Trump&#160;kicked her off the team</a> after she floated her conspiracy theory at a press conference.</p><p>Despite being purged from Trump's \"Elite Strike Force\" legal team Powell used her false theories as the premise of four federal lawsuits seeking to overturn the election result. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/sidney-powell-lawsuits-dismissed-michigan-georgia-arizona-wisconsin-2020-12\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"ef7c059369aa1b65032ba35e7efb76ce\">All of them failed</a>, and some have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/michigan-dems-disbar-pro-trump-lawyers-sidney-powell-lin-wood-2021-1\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"bbef9f928eba6e1b3df5f494476d5a45\">resulted in motions for her to be disbarred</a>.</p><p>Dominion's lawsuit alleges that Powell's claims caused the company business losses after she baselessly accused the company of fraud, election rigging, and bribery.</p><p>\"Powell's statements were calculated to &#8212; and did in fact &#8212; provoke outrage and cause Dominion enormous harm,\" Tom Clare, the attorney representing Dominion, wrote in the lawsuit.</p><p>The 124-page defamation lawsuit also outlines how Powell raised money from her media tour peddling her conspiracy theory through a corporate vehicle called \"Defending the Republic,\" also named as a party in the lawsuit.</p><p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/SidneyPowell1/status/1347592364366438400\">Powell</a> responded by tweeting that&#160;the lawsuit \"is baseless &#38; filed to harass, intimidate, &#38; to drain our resources as we seek the truth of&#160;<a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/DominionVotingSystems?src=hashtag_click\" data-focusable=\"true\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"038cbd49a67b527d55c8b188c459b53b\">#DominionVotingSystems</a>' role in this fraudulent election.\"</p><p>Smartmatic <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/smartmatic-sues-fox-news-over-election-conspiracy-theories-2021-2\">filed a defamation lawsuit against Powell a month later</a>, suing her at the same time it sued Rudy Giuliani, a fellow conspiracy theorist, and Fox News.</p><p>The company claimed that Powell and Giuliani used right-wing media outlets like Fox News to make their conspiracy theories go viral.</p><p>\"These defendants are primary sources of much of the false information,\"&#160;<a href=\"https://www.smartmatic.com/us/media/article/faq-defamation-lawsuit-against-fox-corporation\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"7d306634788c817e7e8766429c5f73e8\">the company said</a>. \"Their unfounded accusations were repeated by other media outlets, journalists, bloggers and influencers the world over.\"</p><p>A federal judge Wednesday <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/federal-judge-rejects-dismissals-of-dominions-defamation-lawsuits-2021-8?r=US&#38;IR=T\">denied Powell's motion to dismiss the lawsuit</a>.</p>\n\tRudy Giuliani by Dominion and Smartmatic\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6039101405ddb100195f6621?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Rudy Giuliani\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2223\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Former New York City mayor Rudy Giuliani at a Trump Campaign press conference.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jacquelyn Martin/AP Photos</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>On January 26, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-rudy-giuliani-13-billion-over-election-fraud-claim-2021-1\">Dominion filed a defamation suit against </a><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-rudy-giuliani-13-billion-over-election-fraud-claim-2021-1\">Rudy Giuliani</a><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-rudy-giuliani-13-billion-over-election-fraud-claim-2021-1\">, Trump's now-former personal lawyer</a>, again seeking $1.3 billion in damages.</p><p>In&#160;<a href=\"https://beta.documentcloud.org/documents/20463221-dominion-v-giuliani-complaint\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"7305dcf4b3665d3cc4b1bbb0717c946d\">the lawsuit</a>, Dominion accused Giuliani of creating \"a viral disinformation campaign about Dominion,\" referring to more than 50 of his statements.</p><p>Through hearings, television appearances, Twitter, and his own YouTube show, it said, Giuliani repeatedly accused Dominion of election fraud and misrepresented the company's security measures while doing so.</p><p>He \"cashed in by hosting a podcast where he exploited election falsehoods to market gold coins, supplements, cigars and protection from 'cyberthieves,'\" Dominion wrote in the lawsuit.</p><p>The 107-page document also cited numerous other people who said they believed Giuliani's claims, which it argued demonstrated the scope of the damage.</p><p>\"Rudy Giuliani actively propagated disinformation to purposefully mislead voters,\" Dominion CEO John Poulos said in a statement. \"Because Giuliani and others incessantly repeated the false claims about my company on a range of media platforms, some of our own family and friends are among the Americans who were duped.\"</p><p>In&#160;<a href=\"https://twitter.com/NYTnickc/status/1353738214532636676\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"5f3e059ddd16c1ca8e420b5d4e8bd1ab\">a statement</a>, Giuliani said he welcomed the lawsuit and suggested he had not previously done a thorough investigation of Dominion's practices.</p><p>A federal judge Wednesday&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/federal-judge-rejects-dismissals-of-dominions-defamation-lawsuits-2021-8?r=US&#38;IR=T\">denied Giuliani's motion to dismiss the lawsuit</a>.</p><p>Smartmatic also <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/smartmatic-sues-fox-news-over-election-conspiracy-theories-2021-2\">included Giuliani as a defendant in its lawsuit filed in February</a>.</p><p>The company said Giuliani used the conspiracy theories to enrich himself.</p><p>\"He reportedly would seek thousands of dollars ($20,000/day) in fees from President Trump to spread the story and file frivolous lawsuits,\" Smartmatic wrote in its lawsuit.</p><p>\"He would also use the attention brought to him as one of the primary storytellers to sell various products &#8211; from coins to supplements to title fraud protection.\"</p>\n\tMike Lindell by Dominion\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6033a4b1623bd30012bcc7e0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"mike lindell trump\" height=\"2371\" width=\"3161\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>MyPillow CEO Mike Lindell.\n<p class=\"copyright\">MANDEL NGAN/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>On February 22, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-voting-systems-machines-mike-lindell-giuliani-election-conspiracy-theory-2021-2\">Dominion filed a defamation suit against MyPillow CEO Mike Lindell</a>, also seeking $1.3 billion in damages.</p><p>Lindell is a&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/my-pillow-ceo-mike-lindell-trump-final-days-2021-1\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"bf55d00bbea2f4da5f66475507d0c135\">staunch ally of former president Donald Trump</a> and <a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/donor-lookup/results?name=mike+lindell\">a major GOP donor</a>, who has repeatedly supported Trump's claims challenging the integrity of the election.</p><p>Dominion's lawsuit accused Lindell of repeatedly making false allegations while knowing there was no credible evidence to support his claims. As well as rallies, interviews, and a&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mypillow-made-three-hour-film-about-election-trump-2021-2\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"ef7aef34517beaee4332a8ac8d5c69b8\">two-hour movie</a>, Lindell used his social-media profiles to spread his baseless claims of voter fraud.</p><p>In the lawsuit, Dominion claimed Lindell used the claims as <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-voting-systems-machines-mike-lindell-giuliani-election-conspiracy-theory-2021-2\">a way to ramp up his pillow sales</a>, advertising on far-right media outlets that parroted his claims and sponsoring a bus tour that sought to overturn the election results. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mypillow-ceo-mike-lindell-dominion-lawsuit-losing-money-2021-2\">Lindell told Insider that retailer boycotts of MyPillow following the insurrection have cost him tens of millions of dollars in business</a>.</p><p>He \"knowingly lied about Dominion to sell more pillows to people who continued tuning in to hear what they wanted to hear about the election,\" Dominion wrote.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mike-lindell-mypillow-responds-experts-may-lose-dominion-defamation-lawsuit-2021-2\">Lindell told Insider Dominion had \"zero, zero, zero\" chance of winning</a>. The lawsuits were part of cancel culture's attempts at silencing voices, he said.</p><p>\"I looked at it as a great day for America when they sued me,\" Lindell added. \"I can put the evidence for the whole world to see, and it'll be public record, and the media will quit trying to suppress it.\"</p><p>A federal judge Wednesday <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/federal-judge-rejects-dismissals-of-dominions-defamation-lawsuits-2021-8?r=US&#38;IR=T\">denied Lindell's motion to dismiss the lawsuit</a>.</p>\n\tFox News by Smartmatic and Dominion\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60392b7f05ddb100195f66d0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Donald Trump Fox News\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1777\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A close-up of the Fox News Channel website with a picture of President Donald Trump displayed on a smartphone.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Rafael Henrique/SOPA Images/LightRocket via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>On February 4, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/smartmatic-sues-fox-news-over-election-conspiracy-theories-2021-2\">Smartmatic filed a $2.7 billion lawsuit against Fox News</a>, accusing it of waging disinformation campaigns about the company's role in the 2020 election.</p><p>\"In November and December 2020, Fox News broadcast multiple reports stating and implying that Smartmatic had fixed and rigged the 2020 election,\" the company said.</p><p>\"They repeated the false claims and accusations on air and in articles and social media postings that were together seen by millions in the US and even more around the world.\"</p><p>Fox called the lawsuit \"meritless\" and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fox-news-asks-court-to-dismiss-smartmatic-defamation-lawsuit-2021-2\">asked a judge to&#160;dismiss the&#160;case</a>.</p><p>On March 26, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-defamation-lawsuit-against-fox-news-election-2021-2\">Dominion also filed a lawsuit against Fox News</a>. The $1.6 billion suit &#8211; its biggest yet &#8211; claimed that the network gave prominence to the election-fraud claims as a tactic to revive viewership as ratings dropped after President Donald Trump's loss.</p><p>The voting-technology company said that Fox News \"sold a false story of election fraud in order to serve its own commercial purposes, severely injuring Dominion in the process.\"</p><p>In a statement, Fox News said: \"Fox News Media is proud of our 2020 election coverage, which stands in the highest tradition of American journalism, and will vigorously defend against this baseless lawsuit in court.\"</p><p>A&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-lawyer-letters-facebook-youtube-twitter-parler-fox-defamation-lawsuit-2021-2\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"1d0f300cb7b0afce51269d47e68374b3\">Fox News representative told Insider in February</a>&#160;that the network ran several \"fact-check\" segments \"prior to any lawsuit chatter.\"</p><p>While several of its news shows reported that there was no evidence of Dominion's systems changing votes, Fox News, in particular its opinion hosts, \"questioned the results of the election or pushed conspiracy theories about it at least 774 times\" in the two weeks after the network called the race, according to&#160;<a href=\"https://www.mediamatters.org/fox-news/fox-news-has-cast-doubt-or-pushed-conspiracy-theories-about-election-results-nearly-600\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-stringify-link=\"https://www.mediamatters.org/fox-news/fox-news-has-cast-doubt-or-pushed-conspiracy-theories-about-election-results-nearly-600\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\" data-remove-tab-index=\"true\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"356d43c6cb8a98c6cc89152c39f1d113\">Media Matters</a><em>.</em></p>\n\tJeanine Pirro, Maria Bartiromo, and Lou Dobbs by Smartmatic\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/603929cd05ddb100195f66c6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Jeanine Pirro, Maria Bartiromo, Lou Dobbs\" height=\"2250\"
