data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"c7dbfcfb505df2918064942fbad0eb28\">Smartmatic's 285-page lawsuit</a> against Fox News also named the hosts Lou Dobbs, Maria Bartiromo, and Jeanine Pirro as defendants.</p><p>Smartmatic said the hosts had offered Powell and Giuliani a platform and endorsed their falsehoods.</p><p>Bartiromo, Pirro, and Dobbs all filed separate motions to dismiss the lawsuit.</p><p>Fox News&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/lou-dobbs-tonight-canceled-by-fox-news-2021-2\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"5bf901d35c6239f0415a83cacc004110\">canceled Dobbs' show days after the lawsuit was filed</a> and said he would no longer have a relationship with the network. It added that the move had been planned.</p>\n\tNewsmax by Dominion\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ed5b4fca74780018ae9053?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Rudy Giuliani on Newsmax.\" height=\"1250\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Newsmax hosted Powell and Giuliani on its shows.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/watch/?v=900245397229583\" target=\"_blank\">Newsmax</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-oan-one-america-news-election-conspiracy-theories-2021-3?r=US&#38;IR=T\">Dominion filed a $1.6 billion defamation lawsuit against Newsmax</a>, the right-wing outlet owned and run by Trump's friend Chris Ruddy, on Tuesday.</p><p>Newsmax was slow to acknowledge the reality of Biden's victory in the November 2020 election. Dominion accused Newsmax of promoting falsehoods about the company in order to compete with Fox News, which had correctly recognized Biden's victory in November.</p><p>\"Newsmax chose to prioritize its profits over the truth,\" the lawsuit said. \"For Ruddy and Newsmax, the facts did not matter. What mattered was feeding the audience what it wanted &#8212; even if it was spreading false information. And the race to the bottom began in earnest, dragging Dominion down with it.\"</p><p>After the election, the network also hosted Powell and Giuliani. By allowing them to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-trump-fox-news-newsmax-oan-sidney-powell-defamation-lawsuits-2021-1\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"bf3f9fc8e3606bac2b1cdf7c8fdaa6ed\"></a>spout their false theories unchallenged on Newsmax's programs, this amounted to defamation, Dominion said.</p><p>Newsmax representative Brian Peterson told Insider that the media organization was simply reporting on what notable figures said.</p><p>\"While Newsmax has not reviewed the Dominion filing, in its coverage of the 2020 Presidential elections, Newsmax simply reported on allegations made by well-known public figures, including the President, his advisors and members of Congress &#8212; Dominion's action today is a clear attempt to squelch such reporting and undermine a free press,\" Peterson said.</p>\n\tOne America News by Dominion\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/611653fc3dd01000199d83ed?format=jpeg\" alt=\"one america news oan\" height=\"2000\" width=\"2666\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A One America News reported.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Drew Angerer/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-sues-oan-one-america-news-election-conspiracy-theories-2021-3?r=US&#38;IR=T\">Dominion filed a $1.6 billion defamation lawsuit against One America News (OAN)</a> Tuesday, accusing&#160;it of engaging \"in a race to the bottom with Fox and other outlets such as Newsmax to spread false and manufactured stories about election fraud.\"</p><p>OAN refused to acknowledge Biden's victory in the 2020 election even as&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-trump-fox-news-newsmax-oan-sidney-powell-defamation-lawsuits-2021-1\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"bf3f9fc8e3606bac2b1cdf7c8fdaa6ed\">Fox News and Newsmax pulled back on far-fetched election claims</a> and aired videos attesting to the legitimacy of the results.</p><p>Dominion said that OAN's falsehoods contributed toward the insurrection at the Capitol on January 6 and that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/dominion-lawsuit-oan-mike-lindell-absolute-proof-election-video-2021-8?r=US&#38;IR=T\">it defamed Dominion by broadcasting \"Absolute Proof,\"</a> Lindell's conspiracy theory-filled documentary about voter fraud.</p><p>Dominion also accused OAN hosts Chanel Rion and Christina Bobb of amplifying and spreading false claims about Dominion.</p><p>After Dominion threatened to sue OAN for defamation in December, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/oann-doubles-down-on-election-conspiracy-theories-amid-lawsuit-threats-2020-12?r=US&#38;IR=T\">OAN They have also not disrupted air travel, NBC reported.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.insider.com/man-deserted-in-alaska-fended-off-bear-sos-spotted-chance-2021-7\" chance</a></em></p><p>It is not unusual for this area, also known as the &#34;Ring of Fire,&#34; to experience volcanic eruptions since it is located along the rim of the Pacific Ocean, where many of the world&#39;s earthquakes and volcanic eruptions occur.</p><p>&#34;Alaska has a lot of volcanoes, and we typically see maybe one eruption every year, on average,&#34; Matthew Loewen, a research geologist with the Alaska Volcano Observatory, told NBC News. &#34;To have three erupting at once is less common, but it does happen.&#34;</p><p>Scientists continue to closely monitor the volcanoes Saturday evening that at least 304 people have been killed and 1,800 injured after a 7.2-magnitude earthquake struck the country, <a a.m. local time, some 7.5 miles northeast of Saint-Louis-du-Sud, and more than 90 miles west of the capital, Port-au-Prince, the United States Geological Survey (USGS) said.</p><p>Then, 20 minutes after the first quake, a 5.2-magnitude tremor struck the island.</p><p>Videos from social media show destroyed buildings and distressed voices shouting as the population reels from the disaster. </p><p>&#34;High casualties are probable and the disaster is likely widespread,&#34; according to the USGS.</p><p>Flooding appears to have started in the country, raising the risk for more damage to follow the quake, which was felt as far as Cuba and Jamaica.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Mundo en Conflicto ðŸŒŽ There were 52 aftershocks that followed the 2010 quake, which raises the question of how much damage is still yet to come from today&#39;s tremor. </p><p>In 2017, the United Nations (UN) stated that 2.5 million Haitians still needed aid following the quake that devastated the country seven years earlier.</p><p>At the time, UN Humanitarian Coordinator Mourad Wahba gave a harrowing account of the challenges that the country continued to face.</p><p>&#34;There are still about 55,000 people in camps and makeshift camps,&#34; he said. &#34;Many are still living in unsanitary conditions due to displacement caused by the earthquake. We have a very long way to go.&#34;</p><p>The quake also comes amid unrest <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/haiti-president-wife-says-survived-because-assassins-thought-dead-2021-7\">following the assassination</a> of President Jovenel MoÃ¯se in his home last month.</p><p>President Joe Biden and Vice President Kamala Harris were briefed on the quake by National Security Advisor Jake Sullivan and the Secretary of State Antony Blinken on Saturday morning, according to a White House official.</p><p>The president has authorized an immediate response and tapped Samantha Power, the United States Agency for International Development (USAID) administrator, weeks after being sent to hospital with the virus, according to his family.</p><p>Yu&#39;s sister, Julie Yu-Meier, on Tuesday announced on a <a href=\"https://www.gofundme.com/f/fundraiser-for-jin-yu-wolfxlion-hospital-stay\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"(opens new window)\" rel=\"noopener\" aria-describedby=\"external-disclaimer\">GoFundMe afternoon Jin passed almost immediately after the ECMO was stopped,&#34; Yu-Meier wrote in a post. &#34;He was surrounded by his entire family and passed as peacefully as possible.&#34;</p><p>It was unclear whether Yu was vaccinated against the virus. <a href=\"https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#vaccinations_vacc-people-onedose-pop-pop18\">Data</a> from the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention showed that just over half of the US population is now fully vaccinated against COVID-19. </p><p>Yu-Meier posted daily updates of Yu&#39;s condition on the site, which she created on July 31 to raise money for Yu&#39;s medical treatment. Since then, the fund has reached more than $135,000, with the highest donation being $25,000. </p><p>Yu, who had more than 120,000 followers on Clubhouse, was taken to hospital on August 1, according to his sister&#39;s post. She said that Yu was put in an intensive care unit  and was transferred to a ECMO machine, which pumps blood outside the body to oxygenate it, replacing the role of the heart and lungs.</p><p>Nine days later, Yu-Meier said that his lungs took &#34;a turn for the worst&#34; and there were more complications. </p><p>On Tuesday, she announced that Yu had died. &#34;I am at a loss of words as my heart is shattered in this moment but we wanted all of you to know,&#34; she said in a post.</p><p>Yu was the cofounder of the <a href=\"https://www.clubhouse.com/club/TalkNerdyToMe\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"(opens new window)\" rel=\"noopener\" aria-describedby=\"external-disclaimer\">Talk Nerdy to Me</a> Clubhouse room, which has more than 246,000 members. src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=L5kSMI5hGBY:fl4VQQ7Nonk:gIN9vFwOqvQ\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/L5kSMI5hGBY\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sat, 14 Aug 2021 11:59:14 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/61178e2a3dd01000199db850?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"b8a5c818045469fee5d44bc22b83723e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn30@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-33-678_77bab2627a96d372.webp","destWidth":2400,"destHeight":1800,"sourceBytes":117898,"destBytes":117898,"author":"ashoaib@insider.com (Alia Shoaib)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/61178e0d3dd01000199db84a?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn17@2020_3/2021/08/15/03-53-29-740_1dacf940c2efed23.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn49@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-32-122_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=L5kSMI5hGBY:fl4VQQ7Nonk:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn11@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-30-379_786eb4adef5e59cf.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=L5kSMI5hGBY:fl4VQQ7Nonk:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn42@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-31-878_e27769c19b30904a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn27@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-30-405_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=L5kSMI5hGBY:fl4VQQ7Nonk:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn36@2020_4/2021/08/15/03-53-29-506_fe380c1c8d3ba349.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/L5kSMI5hGBY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn61@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-40-377_a893905a9f7ecdf2.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1628999590233},{"createdTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"A global immune system that spots new diseases and curbs their spread could stop the next pandemic - here's how","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-global-immune-system-stop-next-pandemic-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6115527bc040ad0018cdfea0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"grocery store empty shelves nyc\" height=\"2924\" width=\"3899\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>There are signs a pandemic is coming before anyone even gets sick.\n<p class=\"copyright\">John Lamparski / Echoes Wire/Barcroft Media via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>There are often warning signs before a pandemic, like an increase in the price of garlic in China.</li>\n<li>Author David Bray says these signs can be used to build a system to spot diseases faster and curb their spread sooner.</li>\n<li>This &#39;immune system for the planet&#39; would search for signs of new infections and identify potential therapies.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>In 2002, when I was working at the Bioterrorism Preparedness and Response Program at the US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention, we noticed something unusual: In China, the price of garlic - which is viewed as a cure-all by many Asian cultures - had risen tenfold. This was the first sign of SARS, the predecessor to COVID-19, and we spotted it five months before China revealed that it was experiencing an outbreak of a new respiratory coronavirus.</p><p>In late 2019, satellite images from China showed cars were heading to hospitals more often than usual. In early 2020, <a href=\"https://www.wbur.org/hereandnow/2020/02/20/covid-19-garlic-coronavirus-china\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the price of garlic rose again</a>. These were among the early signs of COVID-19.</p><p>Often, we see the signs of a new outbreak before we see people getting sick. These early warnings can be invaluable if we learn to pay attention to and act on them. But they&#39;re not enough - we need to incorporate them as part of a larger system that synthesizes information from many different sources to enable us to spot new diseases faster and curb their spread sooner.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-build-resilient-global-food-system-after-covid-2021-3\">COVID-19 exposed many weaknesses in food supply chains. Here&#39;s how we can build a more resilient system for future generations.</a></em></p><p>We need, in short, an immune system for the planet - a network of tools that search for signs of new infections, directly detect and analyze new pathogens right when they appear, and identify, develop and, ideally, deploy effective therapies (and perhaps vaccines).</p><p>The &#34;immune system&#34; would continue to rely on existing tools, such as monitoring demand and prices for medicinal therapies as well as satellite images of traffic patterns, and step up <a href=\"https://ucmerced.maps.arcgis.com/apps/dashboards/c778145ea5bb4daeb58d31afee389082\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">our efforts to monitor public sewers</a>, as <a href=\"https://undark.org/2021/04/21/covid-19-data-down-the-drain/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">pathogens often first appear in wastewater</a>. But it would also incorporate additional strategies that enable us to intervene much earlier in the life of a new pathogen. These tools would look for novel pathogens in the air, water, or soil, sequence their DNA or RNA, then use high-performance computers to analyze the molecules and search through an index of known therapies that might be able to neutralize the pathogen.</p><p>These early warning and detection tools could consist of biosensors that can detect pathogens embedded into organisms such as animals and plants living in tropical regions rich in biodiversity, where new infectious diseases often originate. Transmissions from these sensors would link to a supercomputing network that characterizes new pathogens. Not all detected microbes are harmful, so the system would have to develop computational models based on known pathogens to predict whether or not newly discovered microbes could cause problems for humans.</p><p>Once a harmful pathogen was discovered, the supercomputer could scan libraries of existing treatments that might fight it. Ideally, the system could one day automatically produce a customized mRNA vaccine that targets the pathogen, like some of the COVID-19 vaccines currently being deployed.</p><p>This future isn&#39;t as far away as you might think. This past year, supercomputers <a href=\"https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/covid-19-high-performance-computing-consortium-enters-new-phase-focused-on-helping-researchers-to-identify-potential-therapies-for-patients-301173253.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">played a key role in the fight against COVID-19</a>, illuminating many details about COVID-19 and how the virus behaves, including how long droplets can linger in the air, and pinpointed a gene ( <a href=\"https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC8110974/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">F8A2</a>) that may partly explain why some people may be more vulnerable to COVID-19 than others. Research teams using supercomputers have even identified two existing drugs that might fight COVID-19, after scanning a library of about 1,600, as well as compounds in medicinal plants that may have antiviral properties.</p><p>Once future supercomputer models identify potential treatments to quell a future outbreak, they can help identify the best way to respond - either via conventional means, such as oral medicines or vaccines, or more experimental approaches. To distribute treatments quickly and equitably, it may one day be more efficient to add them to rain or drinking water, along with chemicals to time-limit the therapy. This, too, isn&#39;t so far-fetched, at least within a five to 10-year time horizon: Several US states are <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/environment/2021/mar/23/us-stated-cloud-seeding-weather-modification\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">trying so-called cloud seeding</a> - in which they add small particles of silver iodide to clouds - to boost rainfall. Most Americans drink <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/fluoridation/statistics/index.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">water with added fluoride</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/ncbddd/folicacid/faqs/faqs-fortification.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">cereal grain products are often enriched with folate</a>. These automated solutions take humans out of the loop, and, in the case of COVID-19, could exponentially reduce the time it takes to mitigate a biothreat, thus saving lives, property, and national economies.</p><p>Of course, such a dramatic scaling up of monitoring and therapeutics could raise concerns about privacy and personal choice, so we&#39;ll need to take steps to ensure this planetary immune system doesn&#39;t create a surveillance state. One possibility is to start with a pilot, perhaps monitoring future outbreaks of COVID-19 in one community that buys into the idea. The project would be completely transparent, specifying standards for the ethical use of data, with perhaps a citizen group that oversees all decisions. If the pilot works and people feel comfortable, it could expand to other communities.</p><p>This future isn&#39;t as far away as you might think.</p><p>If this kind of global monitoring system works for disease outbreaks, it could be used to tackle other global health concerns, such as food shortages. Why not use artificial intelligence to develop indicators, warnings, and plans to spot vulnerabilities in global food production, such as wheat, and help make the system more resilient and sustainable?</p><p>What I&#39;m proposing is a massive undertaking, I know. But just imagine if something like this had been in place during COVID-19 - how much suffering and loss could have been avoided. COVID-19 isn&#39;t over yet, and <a href=\"https://knowablemagazine.org/article/health-disease/2020/7-ways-fix-pandemic--and-stop-next-one\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">we know the next pandemic is coming</a> - we just don&#39;t know when or from where. If we start small, working in one area and expanding from there, we can show that this planetary immune system can work, and keep us safe.</p><p><em>This article is part of </em><a href=\"https://knowablemagazine.org/report/reset\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>Reset: The Science of Crisis &#38; Recovery</em></a> <em>, an ongoing series exploring how the world is navigating the coronavirus pandemic, its consequences and the way forward. Reset is supported by a grant from the Alfred P. Sloan Foundation.</em></p><aside></aside><p><em>David Bray is an expert in information systems and decision analyses, the inaugural director of the GeoTech Center, and the executive director of the Commission on the Geopolitical Impacts of New Technologies and Data at the Atlantic Council.</em></p><p>This article originally appeared in <a href=\"https://www.knowablemagazine.org/\"><em>Knowable Magazine</em></a>, an independent journalistic endeavor from Annual Reviews. src=\"https://i.insider.com/6109400e372268001a595c23?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A FedEx delivery person takes a box out of a truck.\" height=\"2658\" width=\"3545\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>FedEx SameDay City delivers time-sensitive packages in 34 major metro areas.\n<p class=\"copyright\">FedEx</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>FedEx hit big shippers with a new round of surcharges ahead of the busy holiday season.</li>\n<li>The surcharge cycle will start with hikes on the cost for special deliveries, but continue with sweeping charges that extend in Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>FedEx is gearing up for a busy holiday season after a year of labor shortages and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/future-fedex-new-class-leaders-fred-smith-step-back-2021-7\">increased demand,</a> and to help deal with the rush, the shipping and logistics company has rolled out a new round of delivery surcharges.</p><p>The main surcharge season kicks in on Nov. 1 with a $1.50-per-piece price hike for FedEx&#39;s Ground Economy deliveries. This applies to outbound residential deliveries for small and medium-sized businesses and covers low-weight, low-value, non urgent deliveries - the majority of typical consumer packages.</p><p>This first surcharge expires on November 28, but will be upped to $3 per package the following day and will last until Dec. 12 to compensate for Black Friday and Cyber Monday purchases. The surcharge will then return to the original $1.50 from Dec. 13 to Jan. 16.</p><p>The company also announced a 60-cents-per-piece charge starting Jan. 17, 2022 for retailers whose shipment volumes qualified for holiday surcharges. So far, there is no expected date for the end of this cycle.</p><p>The move comes days after <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/holiday-shipping-usps-raising-prices-2021-8\">the United States Postal Service announced similar price hikes</a> to cover &#34;extra costs&#34; that occur during the holidays. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-delivery-partners-join-forces-launch-the-front-door-collective-2021-8\">FedEx&#39;s private carrier competitor,</a> United Parcel Service, has also <a href=\"https://www.ups.com/assets/resources/media/en_US/2021_UPS_Peak_Surcharges.pdf\">rolled out new &#34;peak&#34;</a> surcharges. </p><p>The new delivery surcharges could add extra pressures to merchants and retailers&#39; operating costs because businesses must either absorb the increases or pass them on to their customers. A spike in transportation costs have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cpi-inflation-may-supply-bottlenecks-shortages-price-growth-reopening-demand-2021-6\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"47969d3007305aeb0837032a91559a66\">pushed consumer prices higher</a> at stores and restaurants as major companies struggle to maintain their margins. </p><p>Delivery giants like UPS, DHL, FedEx and USPS have been slammed by a litany of issues since the start of the coronavirus pandemic last year. With people on lockdown, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/online-sales-surge-holiday-shopping-shipageddon-chart-2020-11?r=ts-sub\">ordering spiked.</a> Meantime, as the US economy began to reopen this year, companies have dealt with labor shortages, including a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/truckers-pay-hike-salary-truck-driver-shortage-2021-6\">critical shortage of truck drivers,</a> as well as rising fuel and commodity costs.  </p><p>FedEx has turned to offering pay raises and perks for its current logistics employees. Last year, FedEx was forced to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fedex-shipping-limits-surprising-small-businesses-pandemic-peak-holiday-season-2020-12\">place daily package limits</a> on some businesses as its shipping network faces capacity issues around the holidays. </p><p>&#34;If we assume that labor&#39;s going to stay tight for a prolonged period of time, it is absolutely going to be more expensive to ship,&#34; Ravi Shanker, a Morgan Stanley analyst, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ups-fedex-dhl-logistics-compensate-for-labor-crunch-2021-7\">previously told</a> Insider. said on Friday that he believes the coronavirus pandemic will morph into an endemic.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.who.int/director-general/speeches/detail/who-director-general-s-opening-remarks-at-the-media-briefing-on-covid-19---11-march-2020\">A pandemic is classified by the World Health Organization</a> as a fast-spreading disease outbreak that covers wide swaths of the world. An endemic is an outbreak in particular regions that&#39;s always present but far easier to predict and control, like the common cold or <a href=\"https://apic.org/monthly_alerts/outbreaks-epidemics-and-pandemics-what-you-need-to-know/\">malaria</a>. </p><p>&#34;We&#39;re transitioning from this being a pandemic to being more of an endemic virus, at least here in the United States and probably other western markets,&#34; Gottlieb said on <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2021/08/13/dr-scott-gottlieb-expects-coronavirus-to-be-an-endemic-virus-in-us-after-delta-surge.html\">CNBC&#39;s</a> &#34;Squawk Box.&#34;</p><p>Still, Gottlieb warned that other parts of the world will continue to have difficulty containing the coronavirus. &#34;There&#39;s still going to be a pandemic in a lot of parts of the world where you don&#39;t have high vaccination rates,&#34; he said. </p><p>A Duke University researcher recently told Nature, a British scientific journal, that they forecast poorer countries will have to <a href=\"https://www.nature.com/articles/d41586-021-01762-w\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-sk=\"tooltip_parent\">wait two years</a> to have enough vaccines for their populations to reach sufficient immunity. Our World in Data, an online scientific publication, says only about <a href=\"https://ourworldindata.org/covid-vaccinations\">1.2% of people</a> living in low-income countries have received at least one dose against the coronavirus.</p><p>&#34;It&#39;s not a binary point in time, but I think after we get through this Delta wave, this is going to become more of an endemic illness where you just see sort of a persistent infection through the winter,&#34; Gottlieb added. &#34;But not at the levels we&#39;re experiencing right now.&#34;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Squawk Box  (@SquawkCNBC) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1426155618885414919?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 13, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>Officials are still urging all Americans to get vaccinated against the coronavirus, especially as the Delta variant continues to spike in various parts of the country. About 52% of the US population is fully vaccinated, according to <a href=\"https://coronavirus.jhu.edu/vaccines/international\">data</a> compiled by Johns Hopkins University. </p><p>Gottlieb has recently raised the alarm for the US <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gottlieb-northeast-likely-to-see-another-coronavirus-case-surge-2020-8\">Northeast</a>, saying the region is particularly susceptible to another surge in positive COVID-19 cases. </p><p>In an interview aired last week with <a href=\"https://twitter.com/FaceTheNation/status/1424398384597770250\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"438b7bbb8bb4f5daea7290bf515ee9f3\">CBS&#39; &#34;Face the Nation,&#34;</a> Gottlieb said the pandemic is &#34;certainly getting worse&#34; in the US with additional concerns stemming from the upcoming school year. </p><p>&#34;I think the northern states are more impervious to the kind of spread we saw in the South, but they&#39;re not completely impervious,&#34; Gottlieb said. &#34;They have higher vaccination rates. There&#39;s been more prior infection. But there&#39;s still people who are vulnerable in those states. And the challenge right now is that the infection is going to start to collide with the opening of school.&#34;</p><p>Gottlieb served as FDA commissioner from 2017 to 2019 under the Trump administration. He is now a board member at vaccine manufacturer Pfizer, among other companies.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a northern stronghold fell to the Taliban on Saturday, as insurgents have carried out a sweeping military campaign in capturing provincial capitals over the past few days.</p><p>With the fall of Mazar-i-Sharif, the capital of Balkh Province, the only two major cities left under government control are Kabul and Jalalabad, the capital of Nangarhar Province, in the eastern part of the country.</p><p>The Taliban took over the northern city in &#34;barely an hour after breaking through the front lines at the city&#39;s edge,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/08/14/world/asia/Taliban-afghanistan-mazar-i-sharif.html\">according to The New York Times</a>.</p><p>After the Taliban overran the city, government security forces and militias quickly departed, ceding control to the insurgents.</p><p>&#34;Government forces and popular uprisings all left the city,&#34; Hashim Ahmadzai, a pro-government militia commander, told The New York Times. &#34;The Taliban seized government and military buildings. There was no resistance.&#34;</p><p>With the capture of Mazar-i-Sharif, insurgents now effectively oversee the northern, southern, and western parts of the country, with their eye on Kabul, the country&#39;s capital.</p><p>While the Taliban accelerated their insurgency in May, they have been successful at gaining control of most of Afghanistan&#39;s provincial capitals in less than two weeks.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-conflicts-wealth-corporate-clients-ethics-2021-8\">We&#39;ve got your guidebook to the wealth - and potential ethical conflicts -of 31 top Biden appointees</a></em></p><p>According to The Times, the fall of the northern region to the Taliban &#34;offered a devastating blow to morale for a country gripped with panic.&#34;</p><p>After the United States invaded Afghanistan in 2001, the Balkh Province morphed into &#34;one of the most stable provinces in the country,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/08/14/world/asia/Taliban-afghanistan-mazar-i-sharif.html\">according to The Times</a>.</p><p>The region&#39;s strategic location near the border with Uzbekistan gave the economy a boost, but in recent years, the stability that was once prevalent in the region deteriorated as Kabul had difficulties with managing provincial leadership and providing the area with an adequate amount of security forces.</p><p>President Joe Biden has long sought to end the war in Afghanistan, which has been ongoing for nearly 20 years.</p><p>The president on Tuesday stressed that Afghans must &#34;fight for themselves&#34; as the US military remains on track for a full withdrawal by the end of the month.</p><p>&#34;Look, we spent over a trillion dollars over twenty years, we trained and equipped with modern equipment over 300,000 Afghan forces,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2021/08/10/biden-says-afghans-must-fight-for-themselves-as-taliban-advances.html\">Biden said</a> at the White House. &#34;Afghan leaders have to come together. They&#39;ve got to fight for themselves, fight for their nation.&#34;</p><p>The Pentagon on Thursday said that an additional 3,000 troops <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-start-embassy-evacuation-in-kabul-will-send-in-troops-to-help-2021-8\">would be temporarily sent</a> to Hamid Karzai International Airport to safely evacuate Americans and personnel from the US embassy in Kabul.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2021/08/13/1027520899/afghanistan-humanitarian-crisis-un-agencies\" data-metrics=\"{\"category\":\"Story to Lindsey Graham of South Carolina.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/Manuel Balce Ceneta</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Lindsey Graham was censured by the Aiken County Republican Party over his support of the $1.2 trillion bipartisan infrastructure bill.</li>\n<li>The local GOP said the bill &#34;dramatically degrades the rights of existing American businesses.&#34;</li>\n<li>Graham was one of 19 Republicans who joined all 50 Senate Democrats in endorsing the bill.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>GOP Sen. Lindsey Graham of South Carolina was censured by the Aiken County Republican Party this week, with the organization highlighting his support of the $1.2 trillion bipartisan infrastructure bill, <a href=\"https://www.postandcourier.com/aikenstandard/news/aiken-county-gop-censures-sen-lindsey-graham-following-infrastructure-vote/article_51f6d15e-fc84-11eb-a754-231e0c066da7.html\">according to the Aiken Standard</a>.</p><p>The local party, which is based in one of the most solidly Republican counties in the state, said Graham &#34;consciously violated the platform of the South Carolina Republican Party&#34; in censuring the four-term senator, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/demarest_colin/status/1426313968990277634\">alleging</a> that he &#34;opened the door for additional Chinese investment in American projects&#34; which would heighten &#34;the threat to our national security.&#34;</p><p>The landmark legislation, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/senate-approves-biden-bipartisan-1-trillion-infrastructure-bill-mitch-mcconnell-2021-8\">which will infuse federal money</a> into some of the country&#39;s most pressing road, highway, and bridge projects, passed in a 69-30 vote on Tuesday, garnering the support of all 50 Senate Democrats and 19 Republicans.</p><p>After the bill passed, Graham <a href=\"https://twitter.com/LindseyGrahamSC/status/1425123875021541376\">praised the legislation</a> as beneficial to the citizens of the Palmetto State.</p><p>&#34;The bipartisan infrastructure bill is good for South Carolina,&#34; he said in a statement on Tuesday. &#34;It provides much-needed help for our roads, bridges, ports, and expands broadband internet access. I have always been supportive of infrastructure investment and wish we had passed this years ago.&#34;</p><p>He added: &#34;This bill provides American infrastructure with a much-needed face lift.&#34;</p><p><strong><em>Read more: </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-conflicts-wealth-corporate-clients-ethics-2021-8\"><em>We&#39;ve got your guidebook to the wealth - and potential ethical conflicts -of 31 top Biden appointees</em></a></p><p>While high-profile Republicans like Graham and Senate Minority Leader Mitch McConnell of Kentucky <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mitch-mcconnell-votes-for-infrastructure-biden-bipartisan-1-trillion-bill-2021-8\">voted in support</a> of the bill, former President Donald Trump <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-bipartisan-infrastructure-bill-mcconnell-republicans-key-vote-2021-8\">has spent weeks criticizing the legislation</a>, calling it &#34;a disgrace&#34; despite entreaties by GOP Sen. Rob Portman of Ohio for him to back the legislation, which was carefully crafted by the White House and a bipartisan group of senators.</p><p>The Aiken County GOP said Graham&#39;s support of the bill was akin to endorsing the policy platform of the Democratic Party.</p><p>&#34;Support of the &#39;Invest in America Act&#39; is tantamount to supporting the Socialist Marxist agenda of the House and Senate Democrats who are using climate change as a way to force businesses and private citizens into tyrannical government compliance against our free enterprise system,&#34; <a href=\"https://twitter.com/demarest_colin/status/1426313968990277634\">the party said</a> in their censure of the senator.</p><p>They added: &#34;This bill fails to address border security, sets no limits to the fiscal impact of &#39;Green infrastructure,&#39; and dramatically degrades the rights of existing American businesses. He willfully neglected to act within the fiscal conservative agenda we elected him to diligently uphold.&#34;</p><p>Sen. Tim Scott, Graham&#39;s home state colleague and a potential 2024 presidential candidate, took a different tack and <a href=\"https://www.scott.senate.gov/media-center/press-releases/scott-votes-no-on-12-trillion-spending-bill\">sided against the legislation</a>.</p><p>&#34;I support targeted investment in upgrading our nation&#39;s roads, bridges, ports, broadband, and other real infrastructure needs,&#34; he said in a statement. &#34;But I cannot support more reckless spending on unrelated pet projects that will suffocate our future generations with mountains of debt.&#34;</p><p>He added: &#34;Rather than taking a common sense approach to investing in infrastructure, this bill has been rushed through so Democrats can spend trillions more dollars we don&#39;t have on liberal policies we don&#39;t need - all amid record inflation. American families cannot afford to foot the bill for this &#39;spend now, tax later&#39; plan, which is why I voted no.&#34;</p><p>The bill now goes to the House, where it is likely to be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/senate-democrats-reach-deal-reconciliation-package-2021-7\">linked</a> to a separate $3.5 trillion &#34;human infrastructure&#34; reconciliation package which Democrats hope to approve in a party-line vote that would only require a simply majority for passage.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/lindsey-graham-aiken-county-republican-party-censure-bipartisan-infrastructure-bill-2021-8'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=uzJprPBqYcU:cMgPzBQ1IfE:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=uzJprPBqYcU:cMgPzBQ1IfE:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=uzJprPBqYcU:cMgPzBQ1IfE:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=uzJprPBqYcU:cMgPzBQ1IfE:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=uzJprPBqYcU:cMgPzBQ1IfE:V_sGLiPBpWU\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=uzJprPBqYcU:cMgPzBQ1IfE:qj6IDK7rITs\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=uzJprPBqYcU:cMgPzBQ1IfE:gIN9vFwOqvQ\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=uzJprPBqYcU:cMgPzBQ1IfE:gIN9vFwOqvQ\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/uzJprPBqYcU\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sat, 14 Aug 2021 15:09:49 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/6117d87fc040ad0018ce58f6?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"458b52b8e82402833aaf6b392d6dc00e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn76@2020_4/2021/08/15/03-53-28-857_c61074a2394855c7.webp","destWidth":4179,"destHeight":3134,"sourceBytes":1025732,"destBytes":1025732,"author":"insider@insider.com (John L. 23, 2018.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kin Cheung/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Shou Zi Chew is TikTok&#39;s CEO and the CFO of its parent company, video-sharing platform is used by millions across the world, got a new chief executive in May, eight months after <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tiktok-ceo-kevin-mayer-resigns-control-acquisition-bytedance-zhang-yiming-2020-8\">Kevin Mayer walked out.</a></p><p>So who is he?</p><p>Shou Zi Chew is 39 years old, from Singapore, and has been <a href=\"https://businesschief.asia/corporate-finance/bytedance-cfo-tiktok-ceo-5-weeks-who-shou-zi-chew\">speculated to maybe lead TikTok&#39;s parent company to a blockbuster IPO.</a></p><p>TikTok and Chew did not immediately respond to requests for comment for this story.</p><p>Here&#39;s a rundown on TikTok&#39;s head honcho. </p><h2>Chew worked for Facebook when it was still a startup</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61168a293dd01000199d90c8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"facebook mark zuckerberg\" height=\"1064\" width=\"1419\" bachelor&#39;s degree in economics at the University College London before heading to Harvard Business School for his MBA in 2010. </p><p>While a student there, Chew worked for a startup that &#34;was called Facebook,&#34; he said in a post on <a href=\"https://www.alumni.hbs.edu/stories/Pages/story-bulletin.aspx?num=7824\">Harvard&#39;s Alumni website</a>. Facebook went public in mid-2012.</p><p>Chew met his now-wife, Vivian Kao, via email when they were both students at Harvard. They are &#34;a couple who often finish each other&#39;s sentences,&#34; according to the school&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.alumni.hbs.edu/stories/Pages/story-bulletin.aspx?num=7824\">alumni page</a>, and have two kids.</p><h2>Chew was CFO of Xiaomi before joining Bytedance</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61168a40c040ad0018ce2d8d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Shou Zi Chew and Xiaomi CEO give thumbs up at the listing of Xiaomi at the Hong Kong Exchanges on July 9, 2018\" height=\"1326\" width=\"1768\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Shou Zi Chew and Xiaomi&#39;s founder and CEO, Lei Jun.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Bobby Yip</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>He became chief financial officer of the Chinese smartphone giant, which competes with Apple, in 2015. Chew helped secure crucial financing and led the company through its 2018 public listing, which would become one of the nation&#39;s largest tech IPOs in history. </p><p>He became Xiaomi&#39;s international business president in 2019, too.</p><p>Before joining Xiaomi, Chew also worked as an investment banker at Goldman Sachs for two years, according to his <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/shouzichew/?originalSubdomain=sg\">LinkedIn</a> profile.</p><p>He also worked at investment firm DST, founded by Russian IT billionaire Yuri Milner, for five years. It was during his time there in 2013 that he led a team that became early investors in Bytedance, as the <a href=\"https://businesschief.asia/corporate-finance/bytedance-cfo-tiktok-ceo-5-weeks-who-shou-zi-chew\">Business Chief</a> and <a href=\"https://theindependent.sg/singaporean-shou-zi-chew-the-new-ceo-of-tiktok/\">The Independent</a> reported.</p><h2>He&#39;s both TikTok CEO and CFO of its parent company, Bytedance</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61168ad7c040ad0018ce2dff?format=jpeg\" alt=\"zhang yiming bytedance\" height=\"1094\" width=\"1459\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>ByteDance founder and CEO Zhang Yiming.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Zheng Shuai/VCG via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Chew joined Bytedance&#39;s C-suite first in March, the first person to fill the role of chief financial officer at the media giant.</p><p>He also <a href=\"https://newsroom.tiktok.com/en-us/tiktok-names-ceo-and-coo\">became CEO of TikTok in May</a> at the same time as Vanessa Pappas was named COO. Bytedance founder and CEO Zhang Yiming <a href=\"https://newsroom.tiktok.com/en-us/tiktok-names-ceo-and-coo\">said</a> Chew &#34;brings deep knowledge of the company and industry, having led a team that was among our earliest investors, and having worked in the technology sector for a decade.&#34;</p><p>Chew&#39;s predecessor, Kevin Mayer, had left Walt Disney for the position in May 2020 and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tiktok-ceo-kevin-mayer-resigns-control-acquisition-bytedance-zhang-yiming-2020-8\">quit after three months</a> as the company faced pressure from lawmakers over security risks. Some officials were concerned that American user data could be shared with the Chinese Communist Party.</p><p>Former President Donald Trump&#39;s administration issued executive orders designed to force Bytedance into divesting its TikTok US operations, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-rescindsing-trump-bans-tiktok-wechat-2021-6\">though nothing ever happened - </a>President Joe Biden signed an executive order in June that threw out Trump&#39;s proposed bans on the app.</p><h2>Chew wants to buy a $64 million home in Singapore, reports say</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61078766ea74d40019ba1101?format=jpeg\" alt=\"tiktok ceo singapore bungalow\" height=\"1670\" width=\"2226\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Singapore street where the property is located.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Katie Warren/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tiktok-ceo-singapore-real-estate-bungalow-photos-2021-8\">He&#39;s &#34;in the early stage&#34; of purchasing the bungalow</a> in Singapore&#39;s ritzy 10th district, as the Business Times reported earlier this month. He would have to redevelop the dilapidated home that sits on the 31,800-square-foot property.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/who-is-tiktok-ceo-shou-zi-chew-bytedance-cfo-xiaomi-2021-8'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Canales)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/61167a303dd01000199d8996?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn26@2020_4/2021/08/15/03-53-22-613_9bc54cae0b6c317a.webp","https://i.insider.com/61168a293dd01000199d90c8?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn48@2020_2/2021/08/15/03-53-30-984_da0ec16364473cce.webp","https://i.insider.com/61168a40c040ad0018ce2d8d?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn20@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-30-672_7a77df9272aa5983.webp","https://i.insider.com/61168ad7c040ad0018ce2dff?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn76@2020_4/2021/08/15/03-53-30-907_a7ab574d4cb12622.webp","https://i.insider.com/61078766ea74d40019ba1101?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn52@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-29-148_ce2506bb96d75592.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn49@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-32-122_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=5zbZlR0_rU8:sPBqzXztp1g:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn9@2020_6/2021/08/15/03-53-31-392_2d4f503648faf50d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=5zbZlR0_rU8:sPBqzXztp1g:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn100@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-30-721_826afc701f64aa18.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn27@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-30-405_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=5zbZlR0_rU8:sPBqzXztp1g:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn54@2020_2/2021/08/15/03-53-33-412_12ba81daedca5c58.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/5zbZlR0_rU8":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn64@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-29-159_fc90967cf4c4b40f.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1628999590244},{"createdTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"I'm living all over the US for free by pet-sitting for strangers - here's what it's like","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/trusted-housesitters-free-pet-sitting-for-strangers-what-its-like-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61030ed2ea74d40019b9beca?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Meagan Drillinger\" height=\"384\" width=\"512\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Meagan Drillinger and one of her house-sitting pets, Maxwell.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Meagan Drillinger</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Meagan Drillinger is a freelance travel writer who gave up her apartment in NYC to search for the next place she wanted to live.</li>\n<li>She and her partner signed up for Trusted Housesitters so they could experience life in multiple places before they put down roots.</li>\n<li>They pet-sit in exchange for free places to stay. Although it can feel strange, Drillinger says it&#39;s been a great way to travel.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>My partner and I are rich in many ways, but money isn&#39;t one of them.</p><p>So when we made the decision to ditch our NYC apartment and drive cross-country in search of the next place we wanted to call home, we had to be very, very practical about how we planned the trip. A week in an Airbnb could easily blow our entire $2,000 monthly accommodation budget.</p><p>We quickly realized that on our incomes - I&#39;m a freelance travel writer and he&#39;s retired military - we&#39;d have to spend the majority of our journey camping (which, in your mid-30s isn&#39;t as enticing or romantic as it is in your 20s), or the trip would have to be much shorter than we intended.</p><h2>It wouldn&#39;t have been the trip we envisioned - truly experiencing what it would be like to live in each location - at all </h2><p>But then we found Trusted Housesitters. It&#39;s an online database of homeowners who are going on vacation and need trusted people to come stay at their homes and take care of their pets. The best part: The housesitters stay for free. </p><p>It seemed too good to be true. <em>There has to be a catch</em>, we kept repeating to each other. But as we dug more into it, it didn&#39;t seem like there was any fine print other than the overt principle: You apply for house-sits and if you get accepted, you&#39;re invited to stay for free in someone&#39;s home. </p><h2><strong>We made a profile and started applying</strong></h2><p><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61030feeea74d40019b9bf2e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Meagan Drillinger.\" height=\"288\" width=\"384\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Kai the dog.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Meagan Drillinger</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></p><p>In lots of ways, Trusted Housesitters is kind of like Airbnb:</p><ul><li aria-level=\"1\">You create a profile.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">You input dates and location for when and where you&#39;d like to travel.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">You see what&#39;s available. There are homes listed all over the world.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">You send your profile and a note to the owners explaining why you&#39;re a great fit.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">If selected, you have a place to stay at no cost.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">You as the housesitter are reviewed by the homeowner, and vice versa. You want to get good reviews and keep your satisfaction rating high.</li></ul><p>But in many ways, Trusted Housesitters is not at all like Airbnb:</p><ul><li aria-level=\"1\">You pay an annual fee of $119 to be a member, whether you&#39;re a homeowner or a potential house sitter (and an additional $29 to be both).</li><li aria-level=\"1\">You get more housesits if you upload your official documents and become verified.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">You&#39;re staying in someone&#39;s primary residence with all of their day-to-day belongings.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">You&#39;re responsible for their pets while you stay, and all that that entails.</li><li aria-level=\"1\">Other than the annual fee, your stays are completely free.</li></ul><p>The week we started applying for housesits (from a Seattle Airbnb, where we were paying $1,000 for a week, mind you - half our monthly budget) we were able to line up two immediately. It took a matter of days. </p><h2><strong>It turns out, we were in high demand</strong></h2><p><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61030fcbea74d40019b9bf21?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Meagan Drillinger.\" height=\"384\" width=\"512\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Drillinger working at one of the pet sits with dog Genny.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Meagan Drillinger</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></p><p>As a freelance writer and an Army veteran, it was appealing to hosts that we had plenty of time to spend with their pets. We also advertised that we have our own car; some homes offer their car to sitters, but many ask that you bring your own. Posting pictures on our profile of us spending time with our friends&#39; pets was a wise move, too - it helped to show that animals feel comfortable around us.</p><p>Our first house sit was over Memorial Day Weekend in Buffalo, New York for an English Mastiff named Dolly. Buffalo may not have been our first choice on our &#34;where to live next&#34; road trip, but seeing as we didn&#39;t have any reviews yet, we were grateful to be given a blind opportunity. </p><h2>It ended up being the best introduction to Trusted Housesitters</h2><p>We were welcomed into a gorgeously renovated Victorian home in Buffalo by our hosts - a couple who were longtime users of Trusted Housesitters and thus didn&#39;t feel the need to hover. We were watching Dolly, who could have been intimidating upon first encounter, seeing as her head could tower over my shoulder blades. But her size was the only thing daunting about her. By day David would sprawl out on the couch with her, as she tried her best to convince him that she was a lapdog. By night, the three of us would squeeze into a king-sized bed. (Yes, squeeze - she was that big.)</p><p>By the end of the weekend, we had not only fallen in love with Dolly, but we had really had a feel for Buffalo. There was ample time to go out to dinners, see the sights, go to the gym. The experience offered what we were seeking from Airbnb - the opportunity to &#34;live like a local&#34; in a place, minus the outrageous taxes and fees that seemed to increase exponentially during the pandemic.</p><p>Our second sit took us to Raleigh, NC, where we cared for a small menagerie of animals, including two chihuahua mixes, two cats, two hamsters (one of which had gotten loose before we arrived), and a bunny. Again, our hosts were incredibly laidback. It seemed like a zoo to care for at first, but once we got into the swing of things, it was the dogs we spent the most time with - and happily so. In fact, saying goodbye to the dogs was the most difficult part of this entire experience.</p><h2><strong>A great choice for remote work</strong></h2><p><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6103104aaedf2100190f0a01?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Maxwell the dog enjoying a workday nap. Meagan Drillinger\" height=\"2278\" width=\"3038\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Maxwell the dog enjoying a workday nap.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Meagan Drillinger</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></p><p>The pandemic taught many of us that working remotely isn&#39;t as challenging as previously thought. Luckily, I&#39;ve always been able to be nomadic and earn an income - I&#39;ve been a freelance writer for almost seven years. Working from home or in remote corners of places like Mexico or Southeast Asia has been my routine for quite some time. In fact, while we&#39;ve been on the road I&#39;ve picked up thousands of dollars in new travel assignments from publications focusing on US travel. (My partner has been pensioned from the Army for seven years, as well, which frees him up to travel as he wishes.) </p><h2><strong>Reality check: It&#39;s still a little strange</strong></h2><p><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6103106fea74d40019b9c026?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Meagan Drillinger\" height=\"288\" width=\"384\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Drillinger and Kenny.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Meagan Drillinger</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></p><p>When  my uncle heard we were pet-sitting around the country in exchange for free places to stay he said, &#34;That&#39;s the weirdest thing I&#39;ve ever heard.&#34; Truthfully, he has a point.</p><p>It&#39;s definitely strange to be in someone else&#39;s home, complete with their things, their bedroom, their family photos, and, sometimes, their mess. Even though an Airbnb rental is technically someone else&#39;s property, these days there&#39;s anonymity to Airbnb that makes it feel a whole lot more like a hotel. </p><p>It&#39;s also strange to take someone else&#39;s keys from them and wave goodbye to them in their own driveway, but the second they&#39;re gone, we find we relax and feel less like a guest in someone&#39;s home and more like we&#39;ve checked in for a week of local immersion. It&#39;s great for our main goal, which is to see what it&#39;s really like to live in a place. When you throw pets into the mix, the reality factor increases even more.</p><h2><strong>This gig is not for everyone</strong></h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61031169aedf2100190f0abb?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Meagan Drillinger\" height=\"288\" width=\"384\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Kai checking in on Drillinger&#39;s remote work progress.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Meagan Drillinger</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>You have to be adventurous. You have to be able to go with the flow. And, at the bare minimum, you need to like animals. As much as this can feel like a vacation, you are still here, mostly, for the pets: massive poops, slimy drool, runaway hamsters, and all. </p><p>That said, everyone we&#39;ve met through Trusted Housesitters has been exactly &#34;our kind&#34; of people: world travelers themselves, with great stories to tell. It&#39;s a laid-back, trusting community, and one that is deeply respectful of each other. It&#39;s also one that is, truly, all over the world. </p><p>Currently we&#39;re in Arlington, Virginia on our third house-sit caring for two gorgeous Great Dane pups, and from here we&#39;ve got gigs lined up in Minnesota, Denver, and Petaluma in California. </p><p>In between house-sits we find time to do the road trip things that we want to do, like hiking the National Parks, visiting friends we haven&#39;t seen since pre-pandemic, and exploring the romantic two-lane highways that criss-cross the country. (During those times, we *gasp* splurge on Airbnbs and hotels.)</p><p>What started as a way to get us across the country this summer has changed us and our style of travel dramatically. Pending the state of the world, we plan to take this show on the road to Southeast Asia, Europe, and Australia soon.</p><p>While I don&#39;t <em>love</em> picking up poop or sleeping in someone else&#39;s master bedroom, it helps that the savings are kind of unbelievable. In July, for example, we will only need to spend money on five nights&#39; accommodation. The rest of our budget we stash in a savings account so that when we do eventually find our next home, we can buy something special. </p><p>Although, at this rate, I don&#39;t think either of us is in any hurry to land anywhere anytime soon.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Drillinger)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/61030ed2ea74d40019b9beca?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn28@2020_6/2021/08/15/03-53-26-480_1fd887ddb9005053.webp","https://i.insider.com/61030feeea74d40019b9bf2e?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn90@2020_6/2021/08/15/03-53-32-274_b349d2443023ed96.webp","https://i.insider.com/61030fcbea74d40019b9bf21?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn53@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-31-159_a436b0bbd536c277.webp","https://i.insider.com/6103104aaedf2100190f0a01?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn18@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-31-408_84dc5beb776aa51f.webp","https://i.insider.com/6103106fea74d40019b9c026?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn19@2020_6/2021/08/15/03-53-30-575_f45b13e44a01b875.webp","https://i.insider.com/61031169aedf2100190f0abb?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn36@2020_4/2021/08/15/03-53-29-303_2488996347240ba5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn49@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-32-122_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=swKgNA9sDRs:8FstCnFmJas:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn30@2020_6/2021/08/15/03-53-32-784_2fd0bd1ff617dbec.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=swKgNA9sDRs:8FstCnFmJas:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn30@2020_6/2021/08/15/03-53-31-607_1ecba57008431ef1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn27@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-30-405_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=swKgNA9sDRs:8FstCnFmJas:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn61@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-31-902_67a938b81649c1db.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/swKgNA9sDRs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn45@2020_3/2021/08/15/03-53-33-451_1cddf7fdb497c191.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1628999590239},{"createdTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"Only in America is filing taxes such a complicated mess. Here's how other countries do it better.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/filing-taxes-america-system-how-other-countries-do-better-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61152ae53dd01000199d4efa?format=jpeg\" alt=\"couple filing taxes\" height=\"1343\" width=\"1791\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Many Americans can spend hundreds of dollars paying a professional to file their personal taxes.\n<p class=\"copyright\">ljubaphoto/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Paul Constant is a writer at Civic Ventures and cohost of the &#34;<a href=\"http://www.pitchforkeconomics.com/\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"ed5e1fdb0ab821395f2994ad12556b95\">Pitchfork Economics</a>&#34; podcast with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/nick-hanauer\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"9bdab3d29610f63f46b962d5a22738bb\">Nick Hanauer</a> and David Goldstein.</li>\n<li>In the latest episode, they discussed why lobbyists want to keep the US tax process so complicated.</li>\n<li>In other countries, the government sends people an estimated tax filing rather than making them guess what they owe. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>&#34;Everybody I know wants a simpler tax process,&#34; a caller to the <a href=\"https://pitchforkeconomics.com/episode/ask-nick-anything-continued/\">latest episode of &#34;Pitchfork Economics</a>&#34; asked. &#34;So why isn&#39;t it happening?&#34;</p><p>It&#39;s a great question. Filing taxes in the United States is so incredibly complex that many people feel compelled to hire highly-trained experts to complete and file their taxes on their behalf. In a country that encourages home ownership, actually owning a house makes filing taxes exponentially more difficult. Many Americans pay more in taxes than they have to because they don&#39;t realize they qualify for various credits and deductions.</p><p>If you&#39;re a freelancer or an independent contractor, you&#39;re encouraged to file with the Internal Revenue Service on a quarterly basis, keep a big bin of paper receipts to track your write-offs, and set aside a huge chunk of your earnings for payment at a later date. </p><h2><strong>Filing taxes doesn&#39;t have to be a complicated and demoralizing mess</strong></h2><p>In fact, in many countries, you don&#39;t have to do your taxes at all. As Jessica Huseman <a href=\"https://www.propublica.org/article/filing-taxes-could-be-free-simple-hr-block-intuit-lobbying-against-it\">noted in a ProPublica investigation in 2017</a>, in countries across Europe, the government sends each citizen an estimated tax filing, which itemizes their deductions, earnings, and charges. And before you complain about big government overreach in those European countries, understand that anyone can dispute their government&#39;s estimated filing and prepare their own returns if they like. </p><p>We could do this here in the US. Before you even begin filling out your tax returns every year, the IRS already has a good idea of what you should be paying. All your earnings and property are already tied to your personal information, and that information has been reported to the tax agency, so estimated filings would be a trivial amount of extra work for the IRS. Is tax law so dull that the IRS has to score cheap thrills by forcing us to do complicated math under the threat of imprisonment for tax fraud - even though they already know exactly how much we owe them?  </p><h2><strong>To find the real reason for all this unnecessary math, you have to follow the money</strong></h2><p>Huseman reports that &#34;Intuit - the makers of TurboTax - and H&#38;R Block have lobbied for years to derail any move toward such a system.&#34; Between them, those two companies spend millions of dollars every year to convince lawmakers to keep the tax system complicated and confusing, so consumers are forced to purchase their products every year. </p><p>In addition to lobbyists making hefty donations to their campaigns, some politicians also enjoy second-order benefits from the fight to keep your taxes complicated. Trickle-down politicians love to use American frustration on tax day as a mechanism to promote their anti-government crusade. When you absolutely loathe filing and paying your taxes, it makes you more likely to see the government as a too-complex system that always takes and fails to produce meaningful benefits.</p><p>Every few years, you&#39;ll see a Republican presidential candidate grab some attention for their attempts to &#34;simplify the tax code&#34; by promoting a so-called &#34;flat tax&#34; in which every adult American pays the same percentage of their income. (Two presidential hopefuls from Texas, Ted Cruz and Rick Perry, both ran on flat tax platforms in the last decade or so.)</p><p>On the surface, this sounds fair, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/posteverything/wp/2015/05/26/the-flat-tax-falls-flat-for-good-reasons/\">until you realize</a> that middle-class families would pay a few hundred dollars more per year under the flat taxes that have been proposed in the past, and that millionaires would pay several hundred thousand dollars less. </p><h2><strong>Worse still, exceptionally wealthy people like billionaires don&#39;t make income in the same way that you or I do</strong></h2><p>Instead of weekly or bi-monthly paychecks, many of them borrow money against their unrealized wealth from stocks at very low interest rates, and none of that wealth would be addressed by a flat tax. So even as we strive to simplify the tax process, it&#39;s vital to remember that not all simplification is a good thing.</p><p>Until we finally convince our lawmakers to forego the lobbying arm of the tax preparation industry and create an easier tax filing process, &#34;Pitchfork Economics&#34; co-host David Goldstein has some advice for ordinary American taxpayers: &#34;For all of you folks out there who are not itemizing, who are still paying people to do your own taxes: Stop! There are a lot of free services out there that the vast majority of American taxpayers qualify for.&#34; </p><p>&#34;Go online, Google it. I&#39;ve never paid anybody to do my own taxes, and I do itemize because I&#39;m a homeowner,&#34; Goldstein said. Workarounds like that are the reality for American taxpayers until we push hard enough for reform that ensures a simple and stress-free tax filing process.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"Why the US-trained Afghan National Army have been defeated with ease by the Taliban","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/afghan-forces-havent-been-able-to-hold-off-the-taliban-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6117af73c040ad0018ce5745?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A Taliban fighter looks on as he stands at the city of Ghazni, Afghanistan.\" height=\"2592\" width=\"3859\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A Taliban fighter looks on as he stands at the city of Ghazni, Afghanistan on 14 August, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The Taliban now control two-thirds of Afghanistan, including half of its provincial capitals.</li>\n<li>Experts say that Afghan forces have adequate training and equipment, but often lack the will to fight.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Demoralized Afghan soldiers often abandon posts to defend their families rather than the government.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Since US-led forces began their withdrawal from Afghanistan, The Taliban have gained ground at an astonishing pace.</p><p>The insurgents have seized half of the country&#39;s 34 provincial capitals, including it&#39;s second and third-largest cities, and now control <a href=\"https://www.abc.net.au/news/2021-08-14/taliban-nears-kabul-as-insurgents-take-more-cities/100377048\">two-thirds of the entire country.</a></p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-AFP News Agency  (@AFP) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1425365528269365254?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">August 11, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p> </p><p>U.S. officials previously said they didn&#39;t expect any provincial capital to be seized until fall at the earliest, according to <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/how-the-taliban-takeover-of-afghanistans-provincial-capitals-is-unfolding-11628890519\">The Wall Street Journal.</a> Now, reports suggest that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/afghanistan-taliban-expected-reach-kabul-in-7-days-report-says-2021-8\">Kabul could fall within a matter of days</a> or weeks.</p><p>The Afghan forces should have the upper hand in numbers, funding and arms. So how have the Taliban gained ground so quickly in Afghanistan?</p><p>Since its invasion in 2001, the US has invested almost $83 billion on training and arming Afghanistan&#39;s defense forces, according to <a href=\"https://foreignpolicy.com/2021/08/11/taliban-afghanistan-defense-forces-army-militias-kabul/\">Foreign Policy</a>.</p><p>&#34;We provided our Afghan partners with all the tools - let me emphasize: all the tools,&#34; US President Joe Biden said while defending the decision to withdraw American forces.</p><p>Experts told the magazine that the problem lies not in the training or equipment provided to Afghanistan, but in local mismanagement, corruption, and demoralized soldiers who often lack the will to fight.</p><p>Sources said that Afghan police have not been paid for months by the Ministry of Interior and that the same is true for the Ministry of Defense, Foreign Policy reported.</p><p>They added that Afghan forces are often not supplied with adequate arms, or even food or water.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6117ec14c040ad0018ce59e4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"An Afghan soldier wearing a headset stands next to equipment at Bagram.\" height=\"632\" width=\"842\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An Afghan National Army soldier stands watch at Bagram after the departure of US forces\n<p class=\"copyright\">Haroon Sabawoon/Anadolu Agency via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Many soldiers and police are also posted to areas far from their homes, to which they have no connection, and some choose to abandon their posts and return home to defend their families, the magazine said.</p><p>There is also a widespread lack of faith in the government, with officials across the country stating they will not fight to defend President Ashraf Ghani&#39;s government. </p><p>&#34;The issue of legitimacy is very important,&#34; said Enayat Najafizada, founder of Kabul-based think tank the Institute of War and Peace Studies, told Foreign Policy. </p><p>He said the 2020 presidential election that returned Ghani for a second term was seen as corrupt, which has been capitalized on by the Taliban.</p><p>That fact combined with corrupt officials pilfering funds has led to widespread distrust of the government.</p><p>Residents in Herat and Kandahar told <a href=\"https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2021/8/13/they-sold-us-out-afghans-in-disbelief-over-taliban-gains\">Al Jazeera</a> that they were shocked at how quickly their cities fell and said government forces did not put up a fight.</p><p>While official records state that the Afghan security forces number over 300,000, the <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-58187410\">BBC</a> reported that the true number is likely to be lower.</p><p>Afghan forces have a difficult history of high casualties and desertions, according to the outlet, and corrupt officials often claim salaries of non-existent troops, called &#34;ghost soldiers.&#34;</p><p>Comparatively, the US Combating Terrorism Center at West Point, estimates that the Taliban have 60,000 core fighters, with additional militia groups and supporters that could swell that number to 200,000.</p><p>Afghan forces are overstretched, and <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2021/jul/13/afghanistan-stunned-by-scale-and-speed-of-security-forces-collapse\">reports say</a> the Taliban have been shooting down air force planes and assassinating pilots, who often have years of training and are difficult to replace.</p><p>Although lower in numbers, the Taliban has gained momentum after a series of successes. </p><p>The Taliban have also been <a href=\"https://www.france24.com/en/live-news/20210814-weapon-seizures-massive-boon-for-taliban-as-cities-fall\">seizing weapon caches from Afghan forces</a>, which are often Western supplied.</p><p>Although US forces left with their &#34;sophisticated&#34; equipment, the Taliban offensive has allowed the group to seize &#34;vehicles, humvees, small arms, and light weapons, as well as ammunition&#34;, Justine Fleischner of weapons-tracking group Conflict Armament Research, told <a href=\"https://www.france24.com/en/live-news/20210814-weapon-seizures-massive-boon-for-taliban-as-cities-fall\">AFP</a>.</p><p>On Saturday, Afghanistan president Ashraf Ghani finally acknowledged the Taliban&#39;s gains in a televised address.</p><p>&#34;Remobilising the security and defense force is our top priority and required measures are underway for this purpose,&#34; Ghani said. &#34;My focus is to prevent further instability, violence, and displacement of my people.&#34;</p><p>On Friday staff at the US embassy in Kabul were told Friday to destroy sensitive material in case the Taliban seized the capital, as <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-embassy-staff-kabul-afghanistan-shred-documents-2021-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"6c2ebb4f4581babf1f7c11ea5545bee1\">Insider </a>reported.</p><p>The United States also announced it would send 3,000 troops to evacuate personnel from its embassy in Kabul, and the United Kingdom has sent 600 troops.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
