charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Elon Musk in Germany on Friday.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Patrick Pleul/Pool via Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Tesla cut CEO Elon Musk&#39;s salary to zero for 2020.</li>\n<li>In 2019, the company said it eliminated altogether the earning and accrual of his base salary.</li>\n<li>Musk&#39;s official salary was listed as $23,760 in 2019 and $56,380 in 2018.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Tesla CEO Elon Musk didn&#39;t receive a paycheck from the electric-vehicle maker in 2020.</p><p>Musk&#39;s 2020 salary dropped to zero, according to an update filed with the SEC on Friday.</p><p>His salary in 2019 had been $23,760. In 2018, it was $56,380. </p><p>&#34;However, he has never accepted his salary,&#34; the company said. &#34;Commencing in May 2019 at Mr. Musk&#39;s request, we eliminated altogether the earning and accrual of this base salary.&#34; </p><p>Under his <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tesla-compensation-package-tranches-explainer?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">2018 compensation agreement</a>, Musk&#39;s total compensation package is stock-based. His options vest based on his ability to push the company to hit certain operating metrics.</p><p>The 10-year agreement included 16 operational milestones. If Tesla hits 12 of those milestones, and the company&#39;s market cap hits $650 billion, Musk&#39;s shares will vest on schedule, according to the company.</p><p>Tesla had hit six of those milestones as of Friday, the company said.</p><p>The company&#39;s market cap <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/tesla-stock-price-record-high-ahead-unprecedented-inclusion-sp500-index-2020-12\">surged past $650 billion</a> in 2020. It was <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/tsla-stock\">$704.81 billion</a> as of Friday&#39;s close. </p><p>In 2019, Musk paid cash for vested options that were valued at $30.5 million, but didn&#39;t sell any of the shares bought in that transaction, according to Friday&#39;s filing. The filing didn&#39;t list a vested-option purchase for 2020. </p><p>Under the 2018 agreement, Musk&#39;s exercise price was $70.01 per share, SEC filings said. Tesla stock ended the week at $716.70 per share.  </p><p>&#34;Only time I sell Tesla stock is when my stock options are expiring &#38; I have no choice,&#34; Musk said on <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1402686934900633607?s=20\">Twitter</a> in June.</p><p>Bloomberg last week estimated Musk&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-highest-paid-ceo-6-7-billion-in-2020-2021-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">total 2020 compensation</a> to be $6.7 billion, the highest of any US chief executive.</p><p>Musk has often said he&#39;s earmarked his Tesla stock to help humans reach Mars. When asked about his 2018 compensation plan in November, he said he &#34;didn&#39;t expect the stock to rise so much so soon.&#34;</p><p>&#34;The reason for the stock options is that they&#39;re needed to help pay for humanity to get to Mars in 10 to 20 years,&#34; he said on <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1323643630997917697?s=20\">Twitter</a>.</p><div Valdez had been leaving a grocery store last Saturday morning when a stranger shot him six times in the neck and shoulder. </p><p>Three of those shots left one of his shoulders broken, the body part on which he&#39;s waiting to get surgery.</p><p>&#34;Having broken bones and bullets in me for over a week now, it&#39;s a little frustrating,&#34; Valdez said.</p><p>Ben Taub&#39;s ICU is at 98% capacity, a spokesperson told Fox 26. About a third of those ICU patients are being treated for the coronavirus, the spokesperson said. </p><p>When reached for comment, the Harris Health System, which operates Ben Taub Hospital, told Insider the doctors at Ben Taub prioritize cases each day because of spiking COVID-19 numbers driven by the Delta variant. </p><p>&#34;In response to the increase in COVID-19 cases overwhelming the hospitals of Harris Health System, our medical experts review all surgical cases throughout the day to determine the acuity level and patient&#39;s overall condition,&#34; said Amanda Callaway, spokesperson with the Harris Health System.</p><p>&#34;Due to strained resources, surgical patients are being prioritized based on several factors, which unfortunately may result in a delay of non-emergent surgical procedures. Harris Health and its medical partners are working diligently to provide the best possible care during these difficult times,&#34; Callaway continued.</p><p>Valdez&#39;s case comes as the Delta variant surges in Texas. Compared to the past week, that figure reflects an increase of nearly 3,000 patients. </p><p>Texas Gov. Greg Abbott in June issued an executive order <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gov-abbott-banned-covid-19-vaccine-mask-mandates-in-texas-2021-7\">barring mask mandates and vaccine passports</a>. Businesses that violate the order will receive fines of up to $1,000. </p><p>Health officials are still urging all Americans to get vaccinated against the coronavirus, especially as the Delta variant continues to spike in various parts of the country. times last Saturday has been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/man-shot-six-times-waits-week-surgery-texas-overwhelmed-hospital-2021-8\">waiting for required surgery for a week now</a>. </p><p>Jenkins also <a href=\"https://twitter.com/JudgeClayJ/status/1426338730261024770\">tweeted</a> on Friday that there were only 17 ICU beds in all of Dallas County available for adults as of More than 10,000 Texans <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/texas-governor-to-deploy-2500-healthcare-workers-as-delta-surges-2021-8\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"e10163bb8a77685b74830c7b46d0eb38\">have been hospitalized</a> as of August 10, according to data from the <a href=\"https://txdshs.maps.arcgis.com/apps/dashboards/ed483ecd702b4298ab01e8b9cafc8b83\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"c5089fa05e2ef33acf042ecb608fcb34\">Texas Department of State Health Services</a>. Compared to the past week, that figure reflects an increase of nearly 3,000 patients. </p><p>In June, Texas Gov. Greg Abbott issued an executive order <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gov-abbott-banned-covid-19-vaccine-mask-mandates-in-texas-2021-7\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"1b4dfac0d83427b94b3260c26e52d129\">barring mask mandates and vaccine passports</a>. Businesses that violate the order will receive fines of up to $1,000. The order has been defied by many <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/austin-schools-masks-mandate-defy-texas-governor-abbott-2021-8\">schools</a> and businesses.</p><p>Jenkins himself has directly <a href=\"https://www.dallasnews.com/news/politics/2021/08/13/state-appeals-court-upholds-dallas-county-judge-clay-jenkins-mask-mandate/\">challenged the order and won</a>. School districts and some Dallas County businesses are currently able to require masks. Abbott has filed an appeal with the Texas Supreme Court to uphold his original order.  </p><p>Health officials are still urging all Americans to get vaccinated against the coronavirus, especially as the Delta variant continues to spike in various parts of the country. About 52% of the US population is fully vaccinated, according to <a href=\"https://coronavirus.jhu.edu/vaccines/international\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Maurice &#34;Reggie&#34; Shepperson tested positive for COVID-19 in July and died on Tuesday, his family and friends told USA TODAY.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gofundme.com/f/funeral-expenses-for-reggie-shepperson?utm_source=facebook&#38;utm_medium=social&#38;utm_campaign=p_cf%20share-flow-1&#38;fbclid=IwAR37OGuZez55LhGz1Ek3Iew4Ux1rkAyjh1CtCaSGBGKYqG0nQ3kicD2c_j4\" reported.</li>\n<li>Maurice Shepperson was put on a ventilator in a Las Vegas hospital, his mother told the outlet.</li>\n<li>Shepperson tested positive for COVID-19 in early June after flying to Hawaii, she told USA TODAY.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/southwest-american-delta-will-not-require-employees-to-get-vaccine-2021-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">Southwest Airlines</a> flight attendant died from COVID-19 less than two months after he tested positive following a work trip to Hawaii, his family and friends told <a href=\"https://eu.usatoday.com/story/travel/airline-news/2021/08/11/southwest-airlines-flight-attendant-covid-maurice-reggie-shepperson/8100532002/\">USA TODAY</a> on Thursday.</p><p>Maurice Reginald &#34;Reggie&#34; Shepperson, 36, died on Tuesday, Dawn Shepperson, his mother, told the paper.</p><p>Shepperson tested positive for <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/woman-overcame-vaccine-hesitancy-fears-facts-2021-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">coronavirus</a> in early July, Marcia Hildreth, a friend and fellow Southwest flight attendant, told USA TODAY.</p><p>Both Hildreth and Shepperson&#39;s mother told the paper that he was fully <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mandated-vaccines-employees-business-covid-19-safe-delta-2021-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">vaccinated</a>.</p><p>More than <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/over-half-of-us-population-vaccinated-for-covid-19-2021-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">half of the US population</a> has had two shots, meaning they&#39;re fully vaccinated against COVID-19, <a href=\"https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#vaccinations_vacc-people-onedose-pop-pop18\">data</a> from the CDC showed.</p><p>A <a href=\"https://spiral.imperial.ac.uk/bitstream/10044/1/90800/2/react1_r13_final_preprint_final.pdf\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"05a22c8a2a18ffb0a2afdcb53610e9b6\">UK study</a> recently found that having <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/covid-19-2-vaccines-gives-50-60-protection-delta-variant-2021-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">two vaccine shots lowers the risk of infection</a> from the Delta variant by 50% to 60%, compared with unvaccinated people. Another UK study in July found that two doses of the Pfizer or AstraZeneca vaccines were <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-vaccine-works-against-delta-covid-but-both-shots-needed-2021-7?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">88% and 67% effective</a>, respectively, against symptomatic COVID-19 from the Delta variant.</p><p>Shepperson often flew to Hawaii for work, his mother told USA TODAY. She told the paper that she joined Shepperson for one of the trips in early June. This was one of the last plane journeys that he took for <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/southwest-airlines-legal-battles-search-engines-skiplagged-cheap-flights-2021-7?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">Southwest</a> before testing positive for the virus, his mother said.</p><p>Insider has reached out to Southwest for comment. A <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/southwest-airlines-sues-skiplagged-in-texas-for-displaying-cheap-fares-2021-7?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">Southwest</a> spokesman confirmed to USA TODAY that an employee died on Tuesday, but declined a request for further details.</p><p>&#34;We are heartbroken over the loss of our Southwest employee,&#34; the spokesperson said in a statement to the paper. &#34;Out of respect for the family, we do not have additional information to share.&#34;</p><p>Shepperson spent one month in a Las Vegas hospital, where he was put on a ventilator, his mother and Hildreth told USA TODAY.</p><p>&#34;It hurt me so bad because it was just so quick,&#34; his mother told USA TODAY. &#34;I didn&#39;t have time to really even acknowledge what was going on.&#34;</p><p>In a separate interview with the <a href=\"https://www.reviewjournal.com/local/local-las-vegas/vaccinated-las-vegas-flight-attendant-dies-from-covid-mother-says-2419704/\">Las Vegas Review-Journal</a>, his mother said Shepperson drove himself to the hospital after saying that he couldn&#39;t breathe.</p><p>Hildreth set up a <a href=\"https://www.gofundme.com/f/funeral-expenses-for-reggie-shepperson?utm_source=facebook&utm_medium=social&utm_campaign=p_cf%20share-flow-1&fbclid=IwAR37OGuZez55LhGz1Ek3Iew4Ux1rkAyjh1CtCaSGBGKYqG0nQ3kicD2c_j4nQ3kicD2c_j4\">GoFundMe</a> page on Friday to raise money for the funeral expenses on behalf of Shepperson&#39;s mother. So far, it&#39;s reached nearly $4,500.</p><p>Southwest is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/southwest-american-delta-will-not-require-employees-to-get-vaccine-2021-8?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">one of three airlines</a> in the US that are not requiring employees to get vaccinated, <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/travel/article/three-us-airlines-no-vaccine-mandate-workers/index.html\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"87736bd5a3ee45b71269d37c705a8bbe\">CNN</a> reported on Wednesday. CEO Gary Kelly said the company will &#34;continue to strongly encourage&#34; that workers get vaccinated, but won&#39;t require it.</p><p>In February, a survey by the <a href=\"https://www.kff.org/coronavirus-covid-19/poll-finding/kff-covid-19-vaccine-monitor-february-2021/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"ce7c1aebf5823d51b386fc2b8caec899\">Kaiser Family Foundation</a> found that 55% of Americans said they had already been vaccinated or would get a shot as soon as possible. <a href=\"https://www.kff.org/coronavirus-covid-19/poll-finding/kff-covid-19-vaccine-monitor-july-2021/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"19d25da51062804280a86730686de150\">That figure rose</a> to 69% in July.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Bell</a>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Millennials&#39; favorite stocks over the past year include <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/aapl-stock\">Apple</a>, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/tsla-stock\">Tesla</a>, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/f-stock\">Ford</a>, and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/pfe-stock\">Pfizer</a>, according to a <a href=\"https://www.dailyfx.com/nas-100/what-are-millennials-and-gen-z-investing-in.html\">study</a> by DailyFX.</p><p>The financial-news website turned to Robinhood to figure out which companies were most popular among young investors. DailyFX looked at data from the trading app - whose users are predominantly aged 18 to 35 - for the 12-month period to April 1, 2021.</p><p>Millennials piled into several stocks that were hammered by pandemic-related travel restrictions and lockdowns, including Disney, Delta Air Lines, and Carnival, the cruise operator. GameStop was excluded from the study as it risked skewing the results, given the frenzied buying of the stock during the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/reddit-day-traders-wallstreetbets-gamestop-gme-rally-upending-stock-market-2021-1\">Reddit-fuelled trading frenzy</a> in January. </p><p>Here are the top 10 stocks that millennials put their money into during the COVID-19 crisis, ranging from electric-car makers and airlines to healthcare firms:</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\t10. Disney\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60b8d95fbee0fc0019d5b11a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"disney world\" height=\"1353\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">John Raoux/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>Ticker: </strong>DIS<strong><br /></strong><strong>Market Cap:</strong> $323 billion</p><p>Disney <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.wsj.com%2Farticles%2Fdisney-loses-nearly-5-billion-as-pandemic-slams-theme-parks-11596573570\">lost nearly $5 billion</a> last year when its theme parks were shuttered due to the spread of coronavirus, but its stock has since <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/disney-stock-price-streaming-subscriber-growth-theme-park-reopening-tourists-2021-8\">rebounded</a> as visitors flocked back to its entertainment venues.</p>\n\t9. Nio\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60b62ffd02ac410018f93b04?format=jpeg\" alt=\"GettyImages 1232435708\" height=\"2000\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo by Zhe Ji/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>Ticker: </strong>NIO<strong><br />Market Cap:</strong> $72 billion</p><p>Seven-year-old Nio, one of the most successful EV startups to come out of China, is a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/5-electric-car-startups-built-to-survive-auto-industry-2021-8\">major disruptor</a> in the global car market.</p>\n\t8. Delta Air Lines\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/609a9845ba78eb001906e9b3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Delta Air Lines Boeing 737-700\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Markus Mainka/Shutterstock.com</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>Ticker: </strong>DAL<strong><br /></strong><strong>Market Cap:</strong> $26 billion</p><p>The airline, which <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-refuses-to-use-name-of-new-covid-19-variant-2021-7\">doesn't use</a> the Delta variant's name, wants to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-pilots-travel-hire-1000-summer-labor-shortage-2021-6\">hire over 1,000 pilots</a> by next summer as travel recovers.</p>\n\t7. Carnival Corporation\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e71e30ec4854067050ce692?format=jpeg\" alt=\"carnival cruise ship\" height=\"1503\" width=\"2048\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>Ticker: </strong>CCL<strong><br /></strong><strong>Market Cap: </strong>$27 billion</p><p>Carnival, the world's biggest cruising company, saw future bookings jump 45% in the second-quarter as Americans were <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/carnival-cruise-demand-ship-sail-travel-donald-arnold-costa-2021-6\">raring to spend lavishly</a> again on cruises.</p>\n\t6. Pfizer\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/609c33646a3ce80019e04169?format=jpeg\" alt=\"pfizer administered to a teenager\" height=\"1400\" width=\"2100\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Matthew Hatcher/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>Ticker: </strong>PFE<strong><br /></strong><strong>Market Cap:</strong> $260 billion</p><p>The COVID-19 vaccine has driven Pfizer's revenue <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/pfizer-stock-price-surpasses-record-1999-high-amid-vaccine-strength-2021-8\">61% higher</a> in the second-quarter to nearly $19 billion. That figure is expected to grow as its vaccine for children gets approved, and a booster shot is explored.</p>\n\t5. Ford\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60d65026df1db80018f3a64b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The new Ford Bronco near a lake.\" height=\"3243\" width=\"5093\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Alanis King</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>Ticker: </strong>F<strong><br />Market Cap: </strong>$54 billion</p><p>Ford plans to boost investment in electric-vehicle spending and aims to have 40% of its global sales to be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.wsj.com%2Farticles%2Fford-expects-40-of-global-vehicle-volume-to-be-fully-electric-by-2030-11622033457\">fully electric by 2030</a>, with its cross-town rival GM going fully EV by 2035.</p>\n\t3. General Electric\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61140ba76fe08d0019978658?format=jpeg\" alt=\"General Electric logo and buildings are pictured, in Belfort, eastern France\" height=\"681\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">SEBASTIEN BOZON/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>Ticker: </strong>GE<strong><br />Market Cap: </strong>$116 billion</p><p>US conglomerate General Electric's stock is up 23% so far this year, and 101% higher in the past 12 months.</p>\n\t2. Tesla\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ef4a6661b8600019f17258?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The interior of a Tesla driving down the highway\" height=\"1751\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><strong>Ticker: </strong>TSLA<strong><br />Market Cap: </strong>$699 billion</p><p>Tesla's stock is up 20,000% since it went public in 2010, making some believe it may be highly overvalued. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-stock-price-rally-explained-elon-musk-electric-vehicle-frenzy-2021-2\">Analysts and investors</a> think the EV-maker's production capacity, demand from China, and its \"full self-driving\" mode justifies its stock price.</p>\n\t1. third quarter despite a global chip shortage, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/apple-earnings-q3-2021-revenue-iphone-eps-profit-analysis-2021-7\">posting a 50% surge</a> in iPhone sales 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"University of Alabama sorority recruitment is going viral on TikTok and it's giving a boost to some retailers","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/university-of-alabama-rush-viral-tiktok-impacting-retailers-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6117defa3dd01000199dbac3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Sorority Recruitment University of Alabama\" height=\"1000\" width=\"1333\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Sorority recruitment at the University of Alabama.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://www.apimages.com/metadata/Index/Alabama-Sororities/112e19fbc1574c5c93ac5e4b1ca5dfcb/15/0\" target=\"_blank\">Brynn Anderson/AP</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>TikToks of students participating in sorority recruitment at the University of Alabama are going viral.</li>\n<li>Outfit of the day, or OOTD, videos from the young women are gaining millions of views.</li>\n<li>Jewelry retailer Kendra Scott is taking advantage of the latest TikTok trend.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>With summer winding down, colleges and universities are preparing for the fall semester. Students are dorm shopping, buying school supplies, and new clothes. At the University of Alabama in Tuscaloosa, Alabama, students are also participating in sorority recruitment. </p><p>For one week every year, more than 2,200 women participate in recruitment (also known as &#34;rush&#34;) at the school, according to <a href=\"https://www.al.com/life/2020/08/nearly-2000-women-receive-bids-after-virtual-sorority-rush-at-ua.html\">AL.com</a>. During the week, current sisters from the sororities on campus are meet potential new members to learn more about them and determine who is the best fit for their sorority. This year, they&#39;re also <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/alabama-rush-bama-tiktok-university-of-alabama-sorority-recruitment-2021-8\">going viral on TikTok</a>.</p><p>The popular video social media app has been flooded with videos of women rushing at the University of Alabama. They&#39;re gaining millions of views every day by sharing their experiences, their new friends, and their outfits.</p><p>Every day of recruitment before heading out to the day&#39;s activities, many of the young women are <a href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/@dollypartonwannabe02/video/6995165943320104197?is_copy_url=1&is_from_webapp=v1p=v1\">posting videos showcasing their outfits</a>, also know as outfits of the day or OOTDs, and gaining millions of views on TikTok. </p><p>Videos showcasing new products, new trends, and new clothes can gain millions, sometimes <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fashion-hauls-popular-tiktok-trend-sustainability-overconsumption-backlash-2021-5\">billions of views</a> on TikTok and is often utilized as a<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tiktok-is-the-second-most-popular-app-for-influencer-marketing-2021-4\"> marketing tool</a> for retail companies. Many popular brands highlighted in the videos include <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/typical-target-shopper-demographic-white-millennial-woman-earning-middle-income-2021-7\">Target</a>, Shein, Franchesca&#39;s, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-track-customer-service-workers-biometrics-2021-8\">Amazon</a>. But several southern-based stores like <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/kendra-scott-advice-for-entrepreneurs-recession-pandemic-2020-10\">Kendra Scott</a> are gaining popularity after being featured in the videos.</p><p>Kendra Scott, a jewelry company based in Austin, Texas, quickly jumped on the TikTok trend when its <a href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/@haygoldenrayofsunshine/video/6996267118366936325?is_copy_url=1&is_from_webapp=v1p=v1\">accessories were featured</a> by women rushing at Alabama.</p><p>Since participating in what people are now calling &#34;<a href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/tag/bamarush?is_copy_url=1&is_from_webapp=v1p=v1\">#bamarush</a>&#34; and &#34;<a href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/tag/rushtok?is_copy_url=1&is_from_webapp=v1p=v1\">#rushtok</a>,&#34; Kendra Scott has seen an increase in its website traffic from new users by 11%, Mindy Perry, chief marketing officer at Kendra Scott told Insider over email. The website also saw an increase of 12% of new users in Alabama and over a 12% increase of new users who are between the ages of 18 to 24 years old.</p><p>&#34;The coolest part of this viral trend is that it all started organically- we weren&#39;t even tagged in the students&#39; #OOTDs at the beginning,&#34; Perry said. &#34;Our phenomenal social team jumped into the conversation right away to begin commenting and engaging, which started to take on a life of its own.&#34;</p><p>Kendra Scott has since made two viral <a href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/@kendrascott?is_copy_url=1&is_from_webapp=v1p=v1\">videos on TikTok</a> about rush which have almost reached a million views combined. The marketing team at the jewelry company, which says their strategy on TikTok is &#34;social listening,&#34; watching and listening to consumers in their everyday lives.</p><div Walsh)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/6117defa3dd01000199dbac3?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn48@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-29-924_0a810679aab9f85a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn49@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-32-122_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=kY68dpODIMw:6xhqbId4rio:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn54@2020_4/2021/08/15/03-53-32-841_b2e9069e399266ff.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=kY68dpODIMw:6xhqbId4rio:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn88@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-30-301_dfe4eba565df5ac4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn27@2020_5/2021/08/15/03-53-30-405_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=kY68dpODIMw:6xhqbId4rio:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn99@2020_1/2021/08/15/03-53-31-084_c1ad2c5d9ef1c58a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/kY68dpODIMw":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn58@2020_6/2021/08/15/03-53-32-819_d27fae72aa165e83.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1628999590218},{"createdTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"Delta's surging and antibodies are waning: What to know about when we'll need COVID-19 booster shots","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-covid-booster-shots-pfizer-moderna-experts-say-not-yet-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/611540ec6fe08d001997b748?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A healthcare professional wearing a mask fills a syringe of the Moderna COVID-19 vaccine from a glass vial.\" height=\"4040\" width=\"5386\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Moderna has soared over the past year on the back of its coronavirus vaccine.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Radek Mica/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Should the US start offering people an extra COVID-19 vaccines dose? </li>\n<li>Supporters cite signs of waning protection and data suggesting a booster shot would help. </li>\n<li>Others say boosting now is unnecessary, because the shots still prevent hospitalizations and death.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The debate over whether the US should roll out extra doses of coronavirus vaccines is reaching a fever pitch.</p><p>Pfizer and Moderna, the pharmaceutical companies selling two of the widely used US vaccines, have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-makes-case-for-booster-dose-of-covid-19-vaccine-2021-7\">forcefully argued</a> that booster doses will be necessary before the winter. Some vaccine experts have been just as forceful in saying they aren&#39;t needed yet.</p><p>&#34;No vaccine, at least not within this category, is going to have an indefinite amount of protection,&#34; Dr. Anthony Fauci, the nation&#39;s top infectious-disease expert, <a href=\"https://www.today.com/video/dr-fauci-booster-vaccine-shots-are-inevitable-118494277893\">said in an interview with NBC News on Thursday</a>.</p><p>&#34;What we&#39;re doing literally on a weekly and monthly basis is following cohorts of patients to determine if, when, and who should get it,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fauci-covid-19-vaccine-booster-shots-2021-8\">he said later</a>. &#34;But right now, at this moment, other than the immunocompromised, we&#39;re not going to be giving boosters to people.&#34;</p><p>Whether it&#39;s the opinions of independent experts, recommendations from drug companies, or the latest research fueling the debate, there are compelling arguments for and against rolling out booster doses to the broad US population.</p><p>It isn&#39;t obvious there&#39;s a clear answer at this point, which makes for a good argument as well as a tricky public-health situation. The rise of the Delta variant, which partially lowers protection from vaccines, is adding to the urgency of the situation.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/inside-moderna-labs-covid-19-and-future-mrna-research-2021-7\" data-analytics-position=\"14\">We got an exclusive look inside Moderna&#39;s labs, where the biotech upstart is planning what comes after its blockbuster coronavirus vaccine</a></em></p><p>The narrow exception here, where both sides agree, is that some Americans do need to be boosted now. Regulators have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fda-expands-covid-19-vaccine-authorization-eua-booster-rollout-2021-8\">OK&#39;d third shots for certain people who have severely weakened immune systems</a>, in the hopes of increasing their protection against the coronavirus.</p><h2>The case in favor: Better safe than sorry</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6116727b3dd01000199d8770?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Two patients with COVID-19 in hospital beds while a doctor wearing full personal protective equipment leans over to check on one.\" height=\"750\" width=\"1500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A doctor checks the vital signs of a patient at the intensive care unit of  Providence Cedars-Sinai Tarzana Medical Center in Tarzana, California on January 3.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Apu Gomes/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>We know that protection from the coronavirus vaccines peaks a few weeks after people get the second dose of a Pfizer or Moderna shot, then gradually declines.</p><p>The critical unknown is how fast it wanes and when we should care enough to act. </p><p>The vaccine developers Pfizer and Moderna have recently said that third doses should be rolled out between six and 12 months after the first two doses.</p><p>In part, that&#39;s because data from Pfizer&#39;s massive study testing its vaccine shows <a href=\"https://www.bmj.com/content/374/bmj.n1920\">protection against symptomatic cases of COVID-19 fell from 96% to 84% over six months</a>. Moderna has presented data showing the antibodies produced by its shot are not nearly as abundant and powerful when exposed to circulating variants after about six months.</p><p>The companies have also presented lab data showing a third dose significantly increases the level of virus-killing antibodies in people. Those boosted antibodies are also active in fighting the Delta variant. That matters because there&#39;s more <a href=\"https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2021.08.09.21261290v1\">research suggesting</a> that neutralizing antibodies correlate strongly to protection against COVID-19. </p><p>The vaccine makers do have a clear financial incentive to pitch booster doses. Moderna, in particular, has seen its valuation explode from $7 billion to more than $160 billion through the pandemic, thanks to its COVID-19 vaccine work that is now bringing in billions in revenue.</p><h2>Reports of waning protection are spurring booster shots</h2><p>Still, information from the <a href=\"https://spiral.imperial.ac.uk/bitstream/10044/1/90800/2/react1_r13_final_preprint_final.pdf\">UK</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/israel-to-give-pfizer-biontech-covid-19-booster-shot-to-elderly-2021-7\">Israel</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2021.08.06.21261707v2.full.pdf\">Mayo Clinic</a> researchers does show that protection from the vaccines seems to be decreasing, adding to the case for boosters. </p><p>Perhaps most shockingly, Israeli health officials said they have seen <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/israel-to-give-pfizer-biontech-covid-19-booster-shot-to-elderly-2021-7\">protection against severe illness tumble from 97% in April to 81% in July</a> among people who are 60 and over. While that data has yet to be published or posted on a preprint server, it is informing that country&#39;s public-health strategy.</p><p>Israel is in the middle of an aggressive booster campaign, <a href=\"https://www.jpost.com/israel-news/israel-approves-booster-for-people-as-young-as-50-676625\">opening eligibility for extra doses</a> to everyone 50 years and older and healthcare workers, among others. France and Germany <a href=\"https://www.france24.com/en/europe/20210805-france-germany-to-offer-vaccine-boosters-despite-who-call-to-prioritise-poorer-nations\">are also forming booster plans</a> that will start to give third shots in September.</p><p>So much of the pandemic has boiled down to problems of reacting rather than anticipating and preventing. Signs are emerging that protection is waning, and a booster shot holds the promise of patching up immunity. Why not try to maximize protection with the tools available?</p><h2>The case against: Boosters are unnecessary, selfish</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61167258c040ad0018ce2377?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Dr. Paul A. Offit speaks at a press conference while Pennsylvania Sen. Bob Casey Jr. looks on\" height=\"3257\" width=\"4343\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Dr. Paul A. Offit speaks during a news conference in Philadelphia.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Matt Rourke/AP Photos</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Dr. Paul Offit, a longtime vaccine developer who sits on the FDA&#39;s vaccine advisory committee, says it&#39;s not yet time for booster shots.</p><p>That&#39;s because the objective of these vaccines is not to prevent every infection. Instead, the aim is to prevent people from being hospitalized with COVID-19 or dying. They&#39;re still doing that extraordinarily well, Offit said.</p><p>When you take that perspective, some of the same studies driving concern look reassuring.</p><p>Take the Mayo Clinic study (and it&#39;s worth emphasizing that this is preliminary research).</p><p>While a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-vaccine-efficacy-dropped-when-delta-became-dominant-study-2021-8\">sharp drop in effectiveness for Pfizer&#39;s vaccine</a> in July has drawn attention, the same study found that its effectiveness at preventing the worst COVID-19 outcomes held up.</p><h2>The shots are still working</h2><p>Pfizer&#39;s shot was 75% effective at preventing hospitalizations, roughly in line with previous month. Moderna&#39;s vaccine was 81% effective by that measure.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5eb87c84e3c3fb4d3b24cc23?format=jpeg\" alt=\"a headshot of Dr. Maria Elena Bottazzi\" height=\"750\" width=\"1000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Dr. Maria Elena Bottazzi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Courtesy of Maria Elena Bottazzi</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Overall, the Mayo results show the vaccines are working, said Maria Elena Bottazzi, a vaccine developer at Baylor College of Medicine.</p><p>&#34;It&#39;s still not really, really clear by the data if it&#39;s advantageous to get a third boost now if you&#39;re a normal, healthy person with a normal immune response,&#34; Bottazzi said. &#34;We&#39;re still seeing great protection by the vaccines against the Delta variant.&#34;</p><p>Another good example is the <a href=\"https://www.cdc.gov/mmwr/volumes/70/wr/mm7031e2.htm\">outbreak in Provincetown, Massachusetts</a>, which drew headlines because most of the people infected were also fully vaccinated. But a CDC analysis of a subset of those cases found that out of 346 fully vaccinated people who got infected, only four, or roughly 1%, were hospitalized and no one died.</p><p>&#34;That&#39;s a vaccine that is still working,&#34; Offit said.</p><h2>Much of the world still needs doses</h2><p>If outbreaks increasingly send fully vaccinated people to the hospital, that&#39;s when you&#39;ll know we need boosters. That&#39;s not happening as of now, Offit said.</p><p>Finally, giving boosters overlooks the far more pressing issue of getting more people vaccinated, Offit and Bottazzi said.</p><p>The World Health Organization is<a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/business/healthcare-pharmaceuticals/who-calls-moratorium-covid-19-vaccine-booster-doses-until-september-end-2021-08-04/\"> pleading with rich nations to hold off on boosters</a> until at least the end of September so other countries can get more of their populations immunized. </p><p>&#34;I would rather see more people get protected against severe disease and deaths and hospitalizations, even if we all have breakthrough infections because that&#39;s what&#39;s going to stop this virus from continuing to mutate,&#34; Bottazzi said.</p><div 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"Free Garbatella:  A photo tour through Rome's revolutionary 'garden city' known for its street art","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/a-photo-tour-through-garbatella-rome-best-place-street-art-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61096201372268001a59671e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A mural is seen on a wall along a steep hilly road, with a baroque building in the background.\" height=\"4000\" width=\"6000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A mural depicting the resistance of a Kurdish fighter against ISIS, with Garbatella visible in the background.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Located in the outskirts of Rome, Garbatella is known both for its revolutionary, century-old housing experiment and as one of the best places to see Rome&#39;s street art. </li>\n<li>Photographer Bruno Federico visited Garbatella to capture its spirit of rebellion and creativity. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Garbatella is a working-class neighborhood in the outskirts of Rome. It&#39;s known for a century-old housing project that serves as a reminder of how good urban design can make for happy urban spaces. It&#39;s also home to some of the most interesting street art in the Italian capital. </p><p>Built in 1920 to house workers from nearby factories, Garbatella was itself a revolutionary idea: A garden-city with low-cost housing, and space to relax and commune with neighbors.</p><p>Today, Garbatella remains a wonderful example of the <em>barochetto Romano</em>. While high-rise buildings would become the dominant form of public housing in the later years of the mid-20th Century, Garbatella, with its winding streets and lush courtyards, is a place where greenery and urbanization coexist. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/610963e6c31de7001849fb1b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A gate leads to a green area surrounded by residential housing.\" height=\"3420\" width=\"5130\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Housing units at Garbatella surround a central garden, which serves as a place for residents to linger and socialize.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/610961acc31de7001849fa23?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A cut-out of Don Quixote appears next to a quote\" height=\"4000\" width=\"6000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The lyrics to a song by Italian singer-songwriter Francesco Guccini: &#34;Day and night we&#39;ll spit hour heart on the face of the injustice / We are the &#34;Greats of La Mancha&#34; Sancho Panza and Don Quixote!&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61096af4c31de7001849fd8f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A man at a water fountain at the base of a long outdoor staircase\" height=\"4000\" width=\"6000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The steps and public water fountains are among the best known features of the neighborhood.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The neighborhood is rich in social and culture initiatives and its walls and building facades tell a story of rebellion and the struggle for a better future. Walking through Garbatella, you&#39;ll see art that takes on the destruction of the environment, racism and the criminalization of the migration, the dystopic model of the city, and the cause of Free Palestine. </p><p>A common site along one street is Mrs. Gisella, who is 81 and likes to stay at her windows to greet neighbors and people-watch. She says that Garbatella it is a quiet and pleasant place to live. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/610975ebc31de700184a01c6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A woman is seen at her window alongside a street.\" height=\"4000\" width=\"6000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Mrs Gisella, 81, watches passerby from her window.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61096a70372268001a596a2e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"X\" height=\"3811\" width=\"5716\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The entrance of one of the social housing projects.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61096278c31de7001849fa6d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Murals along a roadside.\" height=\"4000\" width=\"6000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Murals in support of Palestinians.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Murals also celebrate the neighborhood&#39;s past, like the lady &#34;Garbatella&#34; who is thought to have given the neightborhood its name, and the Roman singer, Alvaro Amici, who grew up in Garbatella. </p><p>One mural pays tribute to Enrico Mancini, an Italian anti-fascist partisan who was captured and tortured by the Nazis. He was among the 335 civilians and political prisoners killed by Nazis in Rome on March 24, 1944, at the Fosse Ardeatine massacre in Rome.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61096172c31de7001849fa14?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A mural of a woman holding a shawl covers the side of a building.\" height=\"4054\" width=\"2703\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A mural of Garbatella, a lady who, some say, gave her name to the neighborhood.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/610962b7372268001a596763?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A mural of a man singing passionately into a microphone by the side of the road.\" height=\"4000\" width=\"6000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A mural depicts the Roman singer, Alvaro Amici, who grew up in Garbatella.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61096ac1372268001a596a4b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Apartment buildings are seen, partially covered in shadow.\" height=\"4000\" width=\"6000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A view inside Garbatella.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The Casetta Rossa Social Center is a local bar and cafe, but it&#39;s also much more than that. The group offers free classes to migrants, organizes cultural and social activities, and runs a food bank. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61096b4ec31de7001849fdb0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A woman is seen holding a crate of goods while others sit at tables or wait in line.\" height=\"4000\" width=\"6000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The cooperative Casetta Rossa, in the middle of the neighborhood, organizes social, political and cultural events and acts in solidarity with the migrants. In the photo they are distributing food to people in need.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61096239c31de7001849fa57?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A man&#39;s face is painted onto the facade of a building.\" height=\"4000\" width=\"6000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A mural celebrates the anti-Fascist partisan, Enrico Mancini.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/61096332372268001a596792?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A huge mural shows a storm-rocked sailing ship under attack by pirates.\" height=\"5362\" width=\"3575\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A huge mural from the Italian artist Blue shows a storm-rocked sailing ship under attack by pirates.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bruno Federico for 11:53:10","updatedTime":"2021-08-15 11:53:10","title":"Warren Buffett wrote to Congress in 1982 to voice his concerns about futures trading - and many of his fears have come true","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/warren-buffett-stocks-futures-options-trading-derivatives-congress-letter-robinhood-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/603cf7aa13b221001876acff?format=jpeg\" alt=\"warren buffett\" height=\"1533\" width=\"3066\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Warren Buffett.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Warren Buffett has warned against speculating on options, and accused Robinhood of encouraging it.</li>\n<li>The investor expressed similar concerns about futures trading in a letter to Congress in 1982.</li>\n<li>Buffett predicted mass gambling, heavy losses for investors, and damage to the stock market&#39;s image.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Warren Buffett has <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-warned-against-speculating-day-traders-dont-care-2020-6\">warned people against speculating on options</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/warren-buffett-michael-burry-robinhood-ipo-day-traders-speculation-warnings-2021-7\">accused Robinhood</a> of encouraging users to gamble on them instead of investing for the long term. The billionaire investor and Berkshire Hathaway CEO predicted derivatives would lead to risky trading and reckless brokers nearly 40 years ago.</p><p>Buffett penned a letter to John Dingell, the late Democratic politician who served in the House of Representatives for nearly 60 years, in 1982. The investor&#39;s missive <a href=\"https://twitter.com/10kdiver\">resurfaced this week</a> courtesy of 10-K Diver, a Twitter user who teaches finance and investing concepts on the platform.</p><p>The Berkshire chief wrote to Dingell to warn against introducing futures tied to the S&#38;P 500 index. Buffett noted that investors could short the contracts to hedge against short-term volatility, but he cautioned that virtually everyone buying them would be gambling on stocks rising in the near term - not betting on the long-term performance of the underlying companies.</p><p>&#34;The propensity to gamble is always increased by a large prize versus a small entry fee, no matter how poor the true odds may be,&#34; Buffett said. &#34;That&#39;s why Las Vegas casinos advertise big jackpots and why state lotteries headline big prizes.&#34;</p><p>&#34;The unintelligent are seduced&#34; by low prices and huge upside, he added, pointing to promoters of penny stocks and brokers who allow trading on minimal margin. Similarly, gamblers would use S&#38;P 500 futures to bet on the short-term direction of the index while avoiding margin requirements, he said.</p><p>Buffett also explained why introducing futures would lead to rampant speculation, and result in a net loss for investors.</p><p>&#34;Since the casino (the futures market and its supporting cast of brokers) gets paid a toll each time one of these transactions takes place, you can be sure that it will have a great interest in providing very large numbers of losers and winners,&#34; he said.</p><p>Moreover, transaction costs would make futures trading a &#34;negative sum game&#34; for investors, he said. In contrast, investing in stocks is a &#34;positive sum game&#34; as the underlying companies grow and generate more money for their shareholders, he continued.</p><p>Buffett predicted that at least 95% of the activity involving futures would be &#34;strictly gambling in nature.&#34; People would use small sums of money to bet big on short-term stock movements, and brokerages would encourage them to trade more and more to maximize their cut, he said.</p><p>Brokers would do better over time if they didn&#39;t let their customers fritter away their cash, but they&#39;re too short-sighted to care, Buffett continued. &#34;They often have been happiest when behavior was at its silliest,&#34; he noted.</p><p>The Berkshire chief also warned that futures would tarnish the stock market&#39;s image, as many people would get &#34;burned&#34; by them and blame their losses on stocks.</p><p>Finally, Buffett argued the country needed more people investing for the long term, not more gamblers egged on by brokers. Large volumes of future trading would be &#34;overwhelmingly detrimental to the security-buying public&#34; and markets as well, he added.</p><p>Buffett&#39;s warnings about futures nearly four decades ago could easily be written about options today, as a new generation of traders continue to buy them <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/reddit-day-traders-wallstreetbets-gamestop-gme-rally-upending-stock-market-2021-1\">based on memes and social media</a>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/warren-buffett-stocks-futures-options-trading-derivatives-congress-letter-robinhood-2021-8'>Business But lawmakers are asking why.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-wants-your-palm-prints-lawmakers-are-asking-why-2021-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6117d192c040ad0018ce587e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Silhouette of a person holding a phone, with the Amazon logo in the background\" height=\"2762\" width=\"3683\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Amazon is under regulatory scrutiny for its palm-print scanning technology.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li><strong>A bipartisan group of senators sent Amazon a letter questioning its use of biometric data.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>The tech giant introduced Amazon One, a palm-print scanner, last year.</strong></li>\n<li><strong>Lawmakers raised questions about data privacy and security.</strong></li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A bipartisan trio of senators is questioning Amazon about its collection of biometric data.</p><p>In a <a href=\"https://www.cassidy.senate.gov/imo/media/doc/0DA3E8409AD9EB20E056BC005E5858B1.8.12.21-letter-to-amazon.pdf\">letter</a> sent to Amazon&#39;s new CEO, Andy Jassy, Democratic Senators Amy Klobuchar and Jon Ossof and Republican Senator Bill Cassidy asked him to explain how the company will expand the use of Amazon One, its palm-scanner, and how it will use the data it collects.</p><p>&#34;Amazon&#39;s expansion of biometric data collection through Amazon One raises serious questions about Amazon&#39;s plans for this data and its respect for user privacy, including about how Amazon may use the data for advertising and tracking purposes,&#34; they wrote.</p><p>Amazon <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-one-palm-scanner-payment-system-trialed-amazon-go-seattle-2020-9\">introduced</a> its palm-scanning product, which can be used for people to identify themselves or make a payment, in September last year. It&#39;s since expanded to nearly 60 Amazon Go convenience stores, Whole Foods, and other Amazon retail stores, and the e-commerce giant plans to expand its use to things like entering stadiums and badging into work, <a href=\"https://www.aboutamazon.com/news/innovation-at-amazon/introducing-amazon-one-a-new-innovation-to-make-everyday-activities-effortless\">according to</a> Dilip Kumar, vice president of Amazon&#39;s physical retail and technology.</p><p>&#34;Just hover to enter, identify, and pay. Simply by being you,&#34; its website states.</p><p>The senators also voiced concerns over <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-big-tech-executive-order-mergers-data-privacy-net-neutrality-2021-7\">data security.</a></p><p>Unlike Apple&#39;s Face ID and Touch ID or Samsung Pass, which store biometric information on a user&#39;s device, Amazon One uploads it to the cloud, potentially exposing that information to security risks.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amazon-eu-fine-data-privacy-gdpr-luxembourg-european-union-2021-7\">Amazon has faced scrutiny</a> over user privacy in the past, grappling several lawsuits and class-actions that allege the company violated biometric privacy laws by sharing voice data with third-parties. </p><p>Users can opt to delete their biometric data, which is encrypted and stored in the cloud, according to the Amazon One FAQ page. Amazon declined to comment.</p><p>The company began offering a $10 credit for new users who enroll their palm prints in the program - a move as privacy advocates decried it as a cheap tactic to incentivize people to hand over sensitive personal data, as <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/08/02/amazon-credit-palm-biometrics/\">reported</a> by TechCrunch.</p><p>Sens. Klobuchar, Ossof, and Cassidy additionally said they worried that Amazon might use the biometric data to &#34;further cement its competitive power and suppress competition across various markets.&#34;</p><p>Amazon, as well as other Big Tech companies like Google, Facebook, and Apple, have been under fire over antitrust concerns by the government. Sen. Klobuchar has especially been a leading critic of Big Tech, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/amy-klobuchar-antitrust-bill-apple-amazon-google-facebook-fines-2021-2\">introducing</a> an antitrust bill in February that, if passed, could fine the companies up to 15% of their annual revenue.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/6115b08cc040ad0018ce1909?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Rich Osborne in front of Greene Bean Coffee\" height=\"3024\" width=\"4032\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Rich Osborne in front of Greene Bean Coffee.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Courtesy of Rich Osborne</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>At a coffee shop in Jefferson, Iowa, job applications are pouring in because it pays $15 an hour.</li>\n<li>Greene Bean Coffee owner Rich Osborne says he got about 50 applications in two weeks after raising pay.</li>\n<li>He told Insider it disproves the narrative that nobody wants to work right now.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><a href=\"https://greenebeancoffee.square.site/\">Greene Bean Coffee</a> in Iowa is demonstrating the power of paying workers $15 an hour.</p><p>Once the shop raised wages to $15 in June, owner Rich Osborne told Insider, &#34;that kind of upended the entire narrative out there that people don&#39;t want to work after the pandemic anymore.&#34; It wasn&#39;t a drastic increase - Osborne said they were averaging about $12 an hour beforehand - but it still stood to put a good chunk of money in employees&#39; pockets. </p><p>&#34;Once I wrote it down on a piece of paper in front of me and saw how little the numbers were, I mean, it was a no-brainer,&#34; Osborne said. &#34;So I think people just have a knee-jerk reaction to $15: &#39;Oh my God, that&#39;s so much.&#39; And it&#39;s not.&#34;  </p><p>He added: &#34;There&#39;s plenty of people out there that would gripe that high schoolers or college kids or entry-level jobs don&#39;t need to be making that much. That just fueled me even more to do something about it.&#34;</p><p>As college started back up, the shop needed to hire new workers. As The Jefferson Herald&#39;s Andrew McGinn <a href=\"http://beeherald.com/news/roasting-narrative\">first reported</a>, that&#39;s when the applications really started pouring in.  </p><p>&#34;I got like 50 in two weeks, and I think that&#39;s more I&#39;ve gotten than the entire nine years we&#39;ve been here,&#34; Osborne said. He said the coffee shop has &#34;proved otherwise&#34; the narrative that people <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-to-say-when-someone-says-people-dont-want-to-work-right-now-2021-7\">don&#39;t want to work right now</a>. </p><p>Osborne&#39;s story sticks out amidst a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/labor-shortage-your-pie-pizza-staff-poached-wages-2021-8\">sea of reports</a> about traditionally low-wage service jobs <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/labor-shortage-fast-food-jobs-restaurant-laynes-texas-2021-7\">desperately scrambling</a> for workers. Some are offering <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jersey-mikes-offering-hiring-bonus-labor-shortage-2021-6\">hiring bonuses</a>; others are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/labor-shortage-mcdonalds-amazon-jbs-staff-workers-jobs-employment-wages-2021-6\">offering free iPhones</a>. While it&#39;s true that leisure and hospitality <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/employment-changes-by-industry-july-2021-retail-leisure-and-hospitality-2021-8\">leads the pack in hiring</a>, it&#39;s also seeing an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/record-number-workers-quitting-in-third-month-here-to-stay-2021-8\">elevated number</a> of workers quitting.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-fix-labor-shortage-raising-minimum-wage-heidi-shierholz-2021-6\">Some economists</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-labor-worker-shortage-pay-15-hour-be-in-bind-2021-7\">the president</a> have argued that the solution to the labor shortage is hiking wages to at least $15 an hour. That&#39;s the number activists and politicians have coalesced around for years, and it&#39;s more than double the current federal minimum wage of $7.25 (which <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/federal-minimum-wage-raised-12-years-ago-wont-increase-soon-2021-7\">hasn&#39;t budged since 2009</a>). </p><p>Iowa is one of the <a href=\"https://www.dol.gov/agencies/whd/minimum-wage/state\">21 states</a> whose minimum wage is the same as the federal rate. Many states have raised wages on their own, but localities in Iowa are banned from raising their minimum wage above the state&#39;s level. </p><p>The current hot labor market has seemed to put <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/labor-shortage-wages-salaries-leisure-hospitality-highest-growth-20-years-2021-7\">some pressure on wages</a>, with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/july-jobs-report-high-wage-growth-restaurants-hotels-workers-raise-2021-8\">marked growth</a> every month (even <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/despite-inflation-wages-are-still-higher-than-pre-pandemic-levels-2021-8\">outpacing inflation</a> since the start of the pandemic). As <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/restaurant-grocery-store-workers-now-earn-above-15-on-average-2021-8\">Insider previously reported</a>, average pay for restaurant and grocery workers just exceeded $15 an hour for the first time. While that means half of workers still earn less than that, Greene Bean is part of a trend toward higher pay.</p><p>&#34;Smart people realize that you invest in your business, so therefore you have to invest in your employees,&#34; Osborne said. &#34;And that&#39;s what&#39;s great for me: I can trust them to run my business for me. I don&#39;t have to be the one waking up and opening the door first thing in the morning.&#34;</p><p>One big concern about raising wages: Things will get more expensive. Massive chain Chipotle <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chipotle-hiking-prices-across-menu-to-offset-higher-wages-2021-6\">said</a> that was the case when they raised their wages. </p><p>That&#39;s happening at Greene Bean, too. At the same time as the wage hike, they updated their menu, and Osborne said prices got rounded up to the next quarter. </p><p>Osborne said they did it so &#34;we didn&#39;t have to deal with so much change.&#34; Their most expensive drink is about $6, but a regular old large cup of coffee will still run you $2.</p><p>And his higher wage is impacting more than his own employees.</p><p>&#34;&#39;I&#39;ve already seen interest in other businesses trying to figure out how to do it,&#34; Osborne said. &#34;If you&#39;re going to invest in your business to make more money, investing in people to do it for you is probably a better investment than buying a shiny new machine.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
